# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 8

Regarding your question about the order of the *davening* and the *minhag* to recite *Kaddish* after the *Tehillim* that is recited by the *tzibbur*—

The *minhag* in our *shuls* is that *Kaddish* is not recited after the *Tehillim* that is recited by the *tzibbur* before *davening*. This is based on the fact that the *Tehillim* is not part of the *seder hatefillah* itself, but rather a preparation for *davening*.

However, if there is a *yahrzeit* or an *avel* who needs to recite *Kaddish*, they should be given the opportunity to recite *Kaddish* after the *Tehillim* if that is the *minhag* of the local *anash*, provided it does not cause any *machlokes* or disruption to the *seder* of the *shul*. 

Ultimately, the most important thing is the *hiskashrus* to the *Rebbe* and the *avodah* of *davening* with *kavanah*, which is the true *aliyah* for the *neshamah*.

## 2246

B"H, 4 Tishrei, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...In response to your questions:

1) Regarding your lack of *hispaalus* (emotional arousal) during your learning and davening: You should study the *Kuntres Pokeiach Ivrim*, which has also been translated into Lashon HaKodesh. It is by the Mitteler Rebbe, son of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch. It is surely available at the administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Brunoy. There, you will see several reasons why your body and *nefesh habehamis* do not feel *hispaalus* during learning and davening, and it is within your power to rectify them. As our Sages have said, Hashem does not deal harshly with His creations and only demands according to their capacity; since you have been given such a body and *nefesh habehamis*, you have certainly also been given the strength to conquer them.

2) Regarding your writing that *machshavos zaros* (alien thoughts) distract you during davening: It is well known that *machshavos zaros* during davening are caused by idle talk and idle thoughts prior to davening. To the extent that you discipline yourself in this, the *machshavos zaros* during davening will diminish. You should daven from a Siddur, recite several chapters of Tehillim before and after davening, and give a coin to *tzedakah* before davening.

3) Regarding what you wrote about suffering from evil thoughts: You should study *maamarim* of Chassidus, which ultimately gladden the heart and elevate the *neshamah*, thereby lifting you up and extracting you from the mire and mud. You can begin this study with the *Kuntres U’Maayan Mibeis Hashem Yetzei*.

4) In general, it is difficult to answer such questions in detail in writing. The virtue of words of *hisorerus* heard mouth-to-ear, face-to-face, is already well known. Therefore, you should seek the earliest opportunity to meet with the *mashpia* of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Brunoy, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and scholarly Rabbi Nissan, may he live, Neemanov. Show him this letter of mine and ask him to hear your concerns and advise you well in both material and spiritual matters. The sooner you do this, the better.

With blessings for a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah*.

On behalf of the Rebbe,
The Secretary

P.S. Regarding your question about finding kosher Sefardic *tefillin* here: In general, they are not available here. You should contact our office in Paris, which is in contact with the Sefardim in Morocco, and perhaps in this way they can procure them for you.

## 282

B"H, 5 Tishrei, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Administration of Kfar Chabad
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 25 Elul. Although time does not permit for the writing of letters, since your question is urgent, I am responding promptly.

The content of your question: Regarding the two possibilities concerning the location for the construction of the agricultural school and the vocational school in the village—whether they should be adjacent to one another or at a distance—you ask for my opinion on this.

I do not see any spiritual disadvantage in the two buildings being adjacent.

On the contrary. Regarding the physical aspect, you should consult with all those involved in the matter, and act in a way that will assist in the development of the institutions and the development of the village. May Hashem grant you success. May it be His will that in the immediate future you will proceed to the actual construction of the aforementioned buildings, and may it be with success in both material and spiritual matters.

With the blessing of a *chasima v’gmar chasima tova*.

## 2248

B"H, between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time. Please refer to the Kuntres U'Maayan, from page 15 onwards. Regarding the correction of the trait you mention: in my opinion, you should attempt to nullify it by completely diverting your attention away from it—meaning, even from the attempt to correct it.

When you feel that you are beginning to think about your own virtues, talents, and so forth, immediately turn your thoughts to some other matter (and it is best to focus on the greatness of the Creator).

To facilitate this more easily with Siyata Dishmaya, give a coin to tzedakah before davening, and after davening, recite Tehillim (at the very least, according to the daily portion for the days of the month).

If possible, it is worthwhile to study the sefer Derech Chaim by the Mitteler Rebbe (son of the Baal HaTanya).

During these days of ratzon between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, I hereby express my blessing to you and your family—may they live—a blessing of a good sealing and final sealing for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings.

#### ***2248***

**It is worthwhile to study:** See also letter 2574 below.

## 2,249

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished man of merit, energetic activist,
One who contemplates matters of goodness, etc., Dr. J. N. Steinberg,
May he be well.

Peace and blessing!

The secretariat has conveyed to me the content of your telephone conversation, specifically your protest regarding our use of the local language, as you fear this may lead to assimilation, etc.

I was pleased to hear your sharp perspective on the matter of assimilation. If there was always a need to be cautious in this regard, how much more so in these days of blurred boundaries, especially when there are those who call darkness light and light darkness. I hope that you will also look favorably upon others regarding this perspective and influence them for the good.

Regarding the practical aspect: the fact that we publish printed materials and the like not only in Lashon HaKodesh and Yiddish, but also in English (and French), it is well known what Chazal said: "The study is not the main thing, but the deed." In practice, we cannot wait until all our brothers, the Children of Israel, wherever they may be, learn to understand Lashon HaKodesh or Yiddish. We must save them and bring them closer to our Father in Heaven and to Torah and mitzvos in practice, for time lost is an irretrievable loss.

Furthermore, here in America, the matter of language is not linked to assimilation. To our sorrow, we find here youth who speak Lashon HaKodesh—especially those who use the Sephardic pronunciation—who, may they be awakened to teshuvah, are still in a state that is the opposite of Torah and mitzvos. I do not mean, Heaven forbid, that Lashon HaKodesh leads to this, but rather, as mentioned, there is a confusion of values here where they call light darkness and darkness light. This perspective, which sells out their Father in Heaven and the Torah and mitzvos for a mess of pottage—nationalism—is precisely what leads them to speak in Lashon HaKodesh. There is no need to elaborate on this distressing matter. How true are the words of our prophets: "Your destroyers and those who lay you waste shall go forth **from you**," for those false opinions and perspectives that contain a thin spark of holiness are the ones that cause the most damage.

Regarding yourself, the materials sent to you concerning the matters of the day in the local language were intended so that if you find substance in them, you would surely wish to bring them to the attention of a wider circle, among whom are those who do not understand Lashon HaKodesh or Yiddish. In any case, I am enclosing the material in Lashon HaKodesh and Yiddish.

May the prophecy be fulfilled speedily in our days: "And they shall all become one fellowship to serve Hashem as one," through the fulfillment of one Torah for us all. May this be, for now, in every language that one hears, and afterwards, in one language for us all.

With respect and blessing.

## 250

250

By the Grace of Hashem, 20 Tishrei, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, a man of energy, etc., R' Yehuda Leib, may he live and be well.

Greetings and blessings!

It gave me pleasure to see you at the farbrengen on Shabbos Bereishis. I am certain that the spiritual enjoyment you experienced will accompany you throughout the entire year.

Since the farbrengen continued even after you had to leave, I would like to convey here a point from the words that were heard later.

All the Yomim Tovim of the month of Tishrei are, as is known, comprehensive, intended to influence the entire year. The influence of Simchas Torah that one must take along for the entire year is—Simchas Torah—which means to rejoice with the Torah every day of the year.

Torah is not an abstract wisdom, and although it is that as well, the primary intent of Torah—as the word implies from the language of *hora'ah* (instruction)—is that even though one must have *kabbalas-ol* toward Torah as a higher and Divine obligation, it must nevertheless be done with *simcha* as well. And when one acts with *simcha*, that in itself is already the reward. But the Ribono shel Olam, who is the ultimate good, also grants for this health of the body, success in business, and *nachas* from children. As the Torah says—*Im b'chukosai teilechu*—that you should be *ameilim* in Torah, active in Torah—then *v'nasnah ha'aretz yevulah*, etc., and all good blessings in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius* will come.

All this is said regarding every Yid. It is understood that one who has merited, and the Ribono shel Olam has helped him to have an influence and an impact on his surroundings to help sustain an institution of *Torah temimah*, one of whose foundations is to be an incessant source of Torah for the wider world—such a Yid must certainly remember and fulfill his mission and his *zechus* not only on Simchas Torah, but every day of the year.

May the Hashem Yisbarach grant you success in your work for Torah; may it be with success and with *simcha*. And knowing how much your wife, may she live and be well, assists you in all your endeavors, she will certainly be a help to you in your undertaking for the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim and be a partner in all the Divine blessings.

With blessings for success in the above.

## 251

251

By the Grace of G-d
28 Tishrei, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished individual, a man of character, engaged in communal affairs with energy and many deeds, etc., Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your books, **Na'im Zemiros Yisrael**, the first three volumes, which are a compilation of the sayings of our Sages and the commentaries on the Book of Psalms. Many thanks for this gift.

As is known, there are two "rulers" in the spiritual life of a person: the brain and the heart, intellect and emotion.

Correspondingly, man’s service to his Creator also takes two paths and modes: the path of *tefillah* and the path of Torah. Torah is our wisdom and our understanding, while *tefillah* is the "service of the heart," and as our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, explains: **it must be with the heart and in the heart.**

In all of this, just as in the totality of creation—which, because it stems from the Simple Unity, is itself unified and integrated, to the extent that even in the externality of things, the eye of the observer and examiner recognizes the partnership and inclusion of the parts of creation within one another—

So too, and even more so, in the Jewish person and in all matters of holiness, where the light of Hashem is found in greater revelation, it is more recognizable and palpable that every element is included within its counterpart.

This is also the secret of what we find regarding several matters that are lenient according to Beis Shammai and stringent according to Beis Hillel. Although the root of the soul of Beis Shammai is from the aspect of the supernal "Left" (and therefore they were inclined to always be stringent), nevertheless, in several matters, Beis Shammai were lenient due to the inclusion of their soul-root, which also includes the "Right." Similarly, the root of the soul of Beis Hillel is also included from the "Left."

It is obvious that this is also true regarding the general categories of man’s service mentioned above: The study of Torah must be connected with the emotion of the heart. This applies both during the study—as our Sages said, "Whoever reads without melody and repeats without song, of him the verse says, 'And I also gave them statutes that were not good'"—and also before the study, which is the concept of the *berachah* of Torah at the beginning, namely, to feel its preciousness and the value of its subject matter until it is fixed in one’s heart.

And "Torah without *dichilu* (fear) and *rechimu* (love) does not fly upward and cannot ascend to stand before Hashem."

Likewise, in the service of *tefillah*, even though it is the "service of the heart," before *tefillah* one must contemplate the greatness of the Almighty and the lowliness of man, etc. And during *tefillah*, one should think as if the *Shechinah* is before him, etc. Without this *kavanah*, it is not *tefillah*.

Furthermore, within *tefillah* itself, there are parts that are primarily connected to the brain: the arrangement of the praises of the Place, *Pesukei D'Zimra*, the *berachos* of *Krias Shema*, etc. And in Torah, there are parts that are primarily connected to emotion.

Among these is the Book of Psalms, the praises and laudations of the Holy One, Blessed be He.

And in this, too, there is inclusion: the thought, contemplation, and *da'as* of the greatness of the Almighty, His wisdom, His magnitude, and His mighty hand must lead to the love and fear of the honored and awesome G-d.

And the *tefillah* that is within Torah—which, as mentioned above, includes the Book of Psalms—requires deep study with understanding and comprehension.

In the first two words of Psalm 30 (Tzadik), this concept is hinted at:

**Tefillah l'Moshe (A prayer of Moses) — a joining and a bonding** (of *tefillah* and Moses, for the entire Torah is called by his name) to become as one in a single union.

Since you have merited to benefit the public with your aforementioned books—so that in addition to the primary goal, which is the recitation of Psalms with the emotion of the heart and the outpouring of the soul, they will also study and examine its excellent commentaries with understanding and comprehension—surely the merit of the many depends upon you. May your strength and power be increased to draw near and unite the Children of Israel to their Father in Heaven through pure *tefillah* and perfect Torah.

With respect and blessing.

## 2,252

B"H, 2nd of Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter in which you inform me of the doubts and difficulties you have regarding the rabbinical position. It seems to me that the offer of the position is appropriate; however, since you are concerned about the influence of the environment upon you, you must increase your shiurim in the study of Nigleh and the study of Chassidus—which leads to the love and awe of Hashem—and the study of avodah of the heart through kabbalas ol. This will enable you to withstand the test, and especially the "imaginary tests," which are more numerous than the genuine ones. May Hashem grant you success in spreading the light of Torah and yiras shamayim in your surroundings, which, in the natural course of events, will also influence you.

It is surprising that in your letter you do not mention anything regarding your fixed shiurim in the study of Nigleh and the study of Chassidus. You will surely fill this in at the next opportunity.

With blessings.

## 253

B"H, 2nd of Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was alarmed to receive your letter after the holiday of Sukkos, informing me that you have abandoned your post—the holy post—at the Yeshiva... founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Although you write the reasons for this, citing a difference in material livelihood and describing the situation as a necessity, it is truly astonishing. One who holds onto the "Tree of Life" planted by our holy Nasi, especially in Eretz Yisrael and in the Holy City [Jerusalem], may it be rebuilt and established—even if one loses a few liras in material wages, what does that amount to?

Regarding what you wrote in your letter, that one of anash whom I trust greatly told you, "Er tut zeier gleich" [He is doing the right thing], since you do not state the reason for this, nor who this person is, I do not know how to respond to this.

May Hashem guide you on the path of truth and what is good before Him, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

As for what you brought from the Yerushalmi, Berachos 2:5, the question there concerns the father's wife, whom [the Gemara] calls "your mother" (Kesuvos 103a). And regarding what is written about "another nation" (Berachos 56a)—that can be explained.

With blessings for success in spreading the teachings of Chassidus, the wellsprings of the Baal Shem Tov, wherever your hand can reach.

#### ***253***

**From the Yerushalmi, Berachos 2:5:** A person whose mother despises him, but his father's wife honors him—where should he go?

## 254

B"H, 2 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn

Your letter has been received, in which you ask whether you should learn to drive a car.

May Hashem help that this should be with success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary: **A. Quint**

## 2155

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Agudas Chassidei Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may Hashem protect them, may they live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Rosh Hashanah and the 5th of Chol Hamoed Sukkos...

Regarding the Reshet educational institutions, whose intent and goal is to instill a spirit of yiras shamayim and education on the purity of holiness, as much as possible, even in those circles and environments that currently lack these matters—consequently, every step that is conquered is a reward (even if it is not yet satisfactory, as it is far from what it ought to be)—there must be an effort to maintain the Reshet institutions, at the very least in the places where they have existed until now... so that there will be the possibility to educate the students in a chinuch of Torah and yiras shamayim, and not to abandon them, chas v’shalom, to their own devices, and thereby [leave them] in a state of educational danger of kefirah, rachmana litzlan. And with appropriate contemplation of the magnitude of the matter of "extracting the precious from the vile," and that if they withhold their hand from this, the students will fall, chas v’shalom, into the hands of educators who are the opposite of Torah and mitzvos, they will surely work in this as well with the appropriate energy. And ultimately, the desire of Hashem will succeed in their hands, to overcome all the obstacles, concealments, and hidden matters, and to raise up students who are yirei shamayim in the Reshet institutions...

Regarding your previous question concerning your gemach fund, which is conducted through a bank: it is indeed correct that it be done specifically in this manner—that is, through a bank, and not through private individuals.

It causes me great distress that, once again, there is no news regarding the construction of the vocational and agricultural schools.

Awaiting good tidings and joyous occasions, and with a blessing of success in your work, in accordance with the intent of our Nesi’im, our Rebbeim, may their merit protect us.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2,256

2,256

B"H, 7 Mar-Cheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your notification that your son-in-law, the Rabbi, and your daughter, may they be well, have purchased—in a good and auspicious hour—a house, or as you put it, a "house of stones."

May it be the will of Hashem that this change of place brings a change of fortune for the good. May their home be a "house of gathering for the Sages," in accordance with what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus regarding the precise meaning of the term *chochma*, and specifically in the gloss of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in Tanya, Chapter 35, in the name of his teacher, the Maggid, regarding the explanation of the level of *chochma*...

- (One may also bring support for this from the revealed Torah, such as Yehuda and others, as is written in the introduction to *Chavas Da'as* on Yoreh De'ah, regarding the common practice among the Sages to refer to a *chacham* as a *talmid chacham*).

May Hashem grant you, may you be well, the merit to increase your efforts in the aforementioned, and to derive true Chassidishe *nachas* together with your wife, may she live, from all your descendants, may they live.

Surely, you will arrange the mortgage—if the seller is a Jew—with a *heter iska*.

With blessings.

## 257

B"H, 7 Cheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter regarding the receipt of your exit permit and your plans to travel here has just been received. Surely, there will be no external obstacles to this.

You are certainly already familiar with the content of my talk to the students who arrived from Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), based on the ruling of our Sages that leaving the Holy Land is permitted for the sake of Talmud Torah. If so, the Talmud Torah must be conducted in a manner that is defined as "Talmud Torah" according to Torah law. For all those who belong to the camp of Chassidim—and certainly those who stem from a lineage of Chassidim—the ruling regarding what constitutes Talmud Torah applies according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus. The core of this is the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in the name of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, of blessed memory: that one should study Torah in such a way that the Torah teaches him. I trust that you accept upon yourself, with absolute resolve, to conduct yourself in accordance with the above.

May Hashem grant you success, that your journey and your arrival be in a good and auspicious hour, and that it be with Talmud Torah and yiras shamayim.

With blessings,

#### ***257***

**That the Torah teaches him:** See also below, Letter 2612.

## 258

B"H, 7 MarCheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Shlomo Chaim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

With pleasure and at the appropriate time, I received your letters in which you write regarding the arrangements before Rosh Hashanah and subsequently, that the students remained, etc. You have revived my soul with this joyous news that you are proceeding step by step in preparing matters so that they may become vessels for the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu. One should not be discouraged or affected by the impression that the progress is slow or less than the measure [expected], for it is impossible to estimate the true extent of the progress. This is based on what is hinted at in the end of Iggeres HaTeshuvah: that the movement of a shadow on the earth by a handbreadth corresponds to (and consequently causes) the movement of the sun’s sphere in the heavens by thousands of miles, and even beyond that, to an infinite degree, etc. (and note the reference to Tanya, Chapter 26, regarding the matter of the shadow).

With a blessing for success in your holy work, and awaiting good and joyous tidings regarding the new Tishrei schedule, for Anash in general and for those you influence in particular.

***

**Rabbi Shlomo Chaim:** Kesselman. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 5, 1289, and the references in the notes there. Below: 2394, 2646, 2662.

## 2259

B"H, 9 Marcheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in the needs of the community, R' Avraham Chanoch, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of the 26th and 27th of Tishrei, along with the 14 chapters of *Beis Rebbe*, Part I. I have handed them over to be prepared for printing, and it is my hope that they will be completed by the upcoming 19th of Kislev. It is surprising, however, that it seems you did not utilize the material found in the book *Toras Shalom*; surely you have access to what was sent here. It would be worthwhile for you to review that book, supplement the work with what is found there, and send it here, indicating the chapter and the specific place where these additions should be integrated. It is understood that the sooner this is done, the better, so as not to delay the printing.

2) Regarding the four chapters concerning our Rebbe’s family and his books: as for finding someone here to work on this, at the moment I do not see anyone suitable. It would be appropriate—based on what is printed in *Toras Chassidus Chabad* and in the pamphlet *Shaarei Chabad* by Mr. A. M. Habermann (printed in Jerusalem, 5712, and he is one of the writers for the periodical *Kiryat Sefer*)—that you yourself edit the chapter on his books as well. The same applies to the chapter regarding his family and his teachers; you should edit them yourself, in the same manner as you did for the first 14 chapters.

3) Regarding the stories about the Chassidim of our Rebbe HaZaken: although your suggestion to collect and print them is worthy and correct, aside from the fact that we should not delay the current matter until then, there is doubt regarding the authenticity of some of these stories. Since it is difficult to verify them, it is not advisable to print them together with *Beis Rebbe*, so as not to weaken its authority.

4) I was pleased with the overall editing and transcription of *Beis Rebbe*, which makes a good and strong impression. I hope that its publication will bring benefit in several respects. Since the Ribono shel Olam has granted you the merit to benefit the many, the "merit of the many" depends on you, to bestow upon you and your wife, may she live, goodness in both material and spiritual matters, and to fulfill the desires of your hearts for the good, with joy and gladness, very soon.

5) I was very, very pleased that, according to your letter, the Vaad of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad has decided to intensify its activities. If only this would come to fruition in a practical manner, very soon, and with tangible actions. If this is true for propaganda that does not return empty, then how much more so for propaganda that is connected to and expressed through actual deeds, which can serve as an example of what they demand of others.

Awaiting good news, and signing with a blessing.

***

**R' Avraham Chanoch, may he live:** Glitzenstein. Additional letters to him—see above, Vol. VII, 1889, and the references in the notes there.

**Beis Rebbe:** See above, ibid., and the references in the notes there.

## 2,260

B"H, 9 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 4th of Menachem Av, in which you write that it is your desire and wish to study at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod, and that you have two considerations regarding this: whether to enter this yeshiva immediately, or to continue your studies as you have until now until your knowledge of the revealed Torah increases, and only after some time—about half a year or a year—to enter the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod. You ask for my opinion on this.

It is well known regarding the matter of Talmud Torah that while for many mitzvos one can fulfill them at a later time if they were missed previously, this does not apply to Talmud Torah. Every moment and hour that one fails to fulfill his obligation of Talmud Torah—which is a constant, positive mitzvah—is a loss. The same applies to the part of Torah that is Chassidus; since you have been awakened to this study, on the contrary, one should regret the time that has passed until now without this study, rather than delay it for several more months.

Therefore, if the administration of the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod agrees to accept you, it is proper and good to do so now. Through the study of the inner dimension of the Torah—which in the holy Zohar is called the "soul of the Torah"—you will certainly also gain soul and vitality in your study of the revealed Torah, which is an increase not only in quantity but also in quality.

I trust that you recite Tehillim after Shacharis every day, and also give some coins to tzedakah from time to time—which also assists in internalizing the Torah, until it effects a change of essence in all your ways, in accordance with what the Rambam writes in Hilchos De'os, chapter 5.

With blessings for success in your Talmud Torah and in yiras shamayim,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary: **A. Quint**

## 261

B"H, 10th of Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter: when I am at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you for success in your teaching with your students, may they live. Do not be discouraged by the fact that things are going with difficulty, for "all beginnings are difficult." With the appropriate attention to the nature of your students' souls, and by conducting yourself with them with a combination of firmness and pleasantness, you will surely become accustomed to fulfilling your work—the work of Heaven—and you will succeed in it. May Hashem grant you success in establishing yourself well, both materially and spiritually.

I trust that you have fixed times for study in both Nigleh and Chassidus, and that you are keeping the three well-known daily study portions: Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 262

10 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your letter in which you write about the acquaintance your daughter made some time ago with a young man. Over time, they grew closer until a shidduch was made between them, and they have already written tanaim, in a good and auspicious hour. You mention that you think the chassan, under better circumstances, could be closer to Yiddishkeit than he is at present, and you ask for a blessing in this regard.

It is self-understood that for everything, and especially for having nachas from children, sons-in-law, and daughters-in-law, one certainly needs the blessing of Hashem and His success. However, this does not exempt parents from doing what is within their power in this direction. On the contrary, when one wishes to receive the blessing and success of Hashem, one must prepare the vessels and means for it; through this, one receives it more quickly and in greater measure. This is achieved through an increase of effort in that direction.

Therefore, you and your husband should exert all efforts so that everything concerning your daughter and her chassan regarding Yiddishkeit should be realized in actual practice.

One must not be satisfied with the level that parents think is sufficient for them. For one must not forget that the state of Yiddishkeit one possesses in middle age is, in most cases, what remains after the erosion of the level that their own parents gave them—which, due to certain reasons, diminishes by a significant portion. And if what current parents give their children is not with sufficient vitality and warmth, then their children will also lack a certain portion; so what will remain after that?!

Especially when one considers that the young generation has greater nisyonos and greater difficulties in Yiddishkeit than the previous generation and generations before it. Consequently, one must have more "weapons"—which means more attachment to Torah and mitzvos—than a generation or two or more generations ago.

It is not as people convince themselves, that in the past one needed to learn Shulchan Aruch with the children so they would act and conduct themselves as the Shulchan Aruch states, and that today a Sunday school or a Talmud Torah until Bar Mitzvah is sufficient, and the maximum is a "parve" yeshiva. One understands and sees clearly that it is actually the opposite. For if one was raised and grew up in the past in a frum Jewish environment, that alone strengthened Yiddishkeit even without a cheder and without a yeshiva. But when one is raised in America (and especially in the smaller towns), the environment certainly does not provide this, and one must actively seek ways so that the shul and even the yeshiva do not cool down Yiddishkeit.

And when parents invest so much strength to ensure their children have and earn plenty for their physical well-being, it is even more necessary and important to ensure the children have "soul-abundance," for only then can the body also be as it ought to be.

May Hashem Yisbarach help you and your husband that you should realize all that has been said above in actual practice. The first condition for this is that you must yourselves become more attached to Yiddishkeit—to true Yiddishkeit. Through this, one can hope that your words with your children regarding Yiddishkeit will be accepted by them, seeing that their parents do this themselves, and indeed with their whole heart.

With a wish for Yiddishe nachas from your daughter and her chassan, and also for yourselves, you and your husband.

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

P.S.
I hope it is superfluous to point this out, yet I write about it nonetheless: at the very least two months before your daughter’s wedding, you must acquaint your daughter with the halachos connected to taharas hamishpacha, and also introduce her to young women who conduct themselves in this Jewish way, even though they were born in America and also come from wealthy homes.

## 263

B"H, 12 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs, R' Shmuel Elazar, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from Erev Sukkos and 4 Menachem Av. We begin with a blessing of Mazal Tov on the birth of your son, may he live. Surely he has already entered the covenant of Avraham Avinu, and just as he has entered the covenant, may he enter into Torah, the chuppah, and good deeds, and may you and your wife, may they live, derive from him much Chassidishe nachas.

Although you have sent—and with Hashem’s help will continue to send—printed materials directly to the editor of *HaModia*, you should certainly remain vigilant and ensure that the matters relevant to the public are indeed published.

I have informed the secretariat that you should be added to the list of those receiving the *kuntresim*, etc.

...The Torah’s perspective is that in a place where it is possible to save a child from an education of heresy, G-d forbid, and bring them to an education of *hiddur mitzvah* in the fullest sense, one must certainly exert every effort to do so. And if it is not possible in that manner, but at least to an education of the *Shulchan Aruch* alone—without going beyond the letter of the law—or even in a worse scenario, at least to an education of observing the fundamentals of the faith and the most severe prohibitions in the Torah, one must still strive to save them, provided they are not assimilated among the nations and receive an education of heresy, G-d forbid.

Anyone who says that in such a situation, "What do I have to do with this trouble?"—especially when the child was already **in his domain**—and withdraws his hand because of the fear of "what will people say," is not only **causing** this, but is literally pushing these students away with his own hands and handing them over to an anti-religious education.

It is known regarding one of our holy Nasi’im that he would answer those who wrote to him even during Chol HaMoed, with the saying: "I cannot sacrifice a fundamental principle for the sake of a *hiddur* (a stringency)." How much more so is it forbidden to lose even one Jewish soul due to political considerations or the like. And certainly, when the matter concerns hundreds and thousands of Jewish children, and certainly when the matter concerns students—both boys and girls—who were already in their domain, the administrators of the institutions bear full responsibility to do everything in their power to ensure they remain at least faithful to their religion, even if they are not yet able to influence them to remain Chassidim or *frum* individuals who are meticulous in *mitzvos* to the highest degree, etc., etc.

## 265

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks the date of writing—as well as the letter from your wife, *tichyeh*: I wish to reiterate my opinion, which I have already written, that my position regarding leaving Paris, especially when one is connected to the Yeshivah, is already known. The fact that you wish to obtain from me an agreement to go to another place to struggle, even if that place is America or Canada, is not my concern.

It would be worthwhile for you to correspond with those who came here months ago and ask them to write the truth about what is happening with them here: why they rushed, and what they have accomplished in the months they have been here, other than being able to write that they are in America—which, in my opinion, is not only far from being a virtue according to Torah, but also according to simple human reason.

Regarding what you write—that the Yeshivah’s attitude toward your work is not as it should be, and consequently you do not have enough work, and also that it is difficult to expand the Yeshivah—the solution to this is **not** to run away from Paris and struggle in another place.

It is time for everyone who has a connection to our *Nasi*, our Rebbeim, to utilize their strengths and do what has been placed upon them with sincerity. Then, it will certainly be with *hatzlacha*, and it will bring an improvement in health, not only in *ruchniyus* but truly in *gashmiyus* as well.

May *Hashem Yisbarach* help that you and your wife, *tichyeh*, should decide what is truly good for you, in *gashmiyus* and *ruchniyus* alike.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 267

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his holy work, R' Aharon, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure your letter of the 11th of Cheshvan, in which you write that you are visiting the villages on a mission for the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and faithful in his holy work, R' Shlomo, may he live, of Toussaf. The magnitude of the merit in this is beyond expression. It is a well-known saying of the Baal Shem Tov (which we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory) that every single Jew is beloved to Hashem incomparably more than the love of an only child born to parents in their old age. From this, one can imagine how great the merit is when one draws the heart of this "only child" closer to his Father in Heaven. Especially as you write that this also involves physical exertion, as you must travel by animal, etc.—and *l'fum tza'ara agra* (according to the effort is the reward).

May it be the will of Hashem that you also see, with physical eyes, success in this holy work, for that is the greatest reward, as the Mishnah rules: "The reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself." May this also be drawn down into success in your personal affairs. Certainly, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages that we "increase in holiness," you should add strength to all of the above, and "whoever adds, they add to him from Heaven" whatever he needs, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

2268

B”H, 18 MarCheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from today. When I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention his children, may they live, for an easy delivery, and that he and his wife, may they live, should receive from all of them an abundance of Chassidic nachas.

For Yisrael is one nation in the land, and therefore there must also be complete unity between the body and the soul; when there is an increase in the soul, it follows that there is an increase in the body.

A change in this is likely to cause more loss than gain, though one should endeavor that the position itself be as light as possible. It is understood that to avoid any agitation, this must be done with the full consent of your father, may he live and be well. If it is possible to arrange that the suggestion comes from your father himself, that would be best. In any case, may Hashem bless your father and mother together with long days and good years, and as the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, goes: "good years, with all the interpretations."

## 2,160

2,160

B”H, 18 MarCheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed avreich, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent, whose work is for the sake of Heaven,
Rabbi Chaim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter with pleasure, in which you write about your settling in Boston regarding your studies at the yeshiva and outside of it as well. I was pleased to see that you are not content merely with the obligations of your position, but are taking initiative and seeking out areas where you can utilize your strengths and exert influence. The precision of the Sages’ language is well-known: in every instance, the expression used is "engaging in Torah" (*osek b’Torah*). My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained that just as in the pursuit of material livelihood, one who requires it does not wait for someone to come into his four cubits and stir him to action; rather, he exerts himself day and night to find ways to secure his livelihood—and to do so with abundance—so too must be the "engagement" in Torah and Yiddishkeit in general. One must search with appropriate effort for areas in which to find one's spiritual livelihood. And the measure of good is even greater, in that through this, one is also granted blessing and success in material livelihood in particular, and in all one's personal affairs in general.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding Shabbos gatherings, as surely such a matter exists in your location. If it does not, it is worthwhile to establish them in an appropriate manner and with outreach.

You mention in your letter that you are teaching a *Ein Yaakov* shiur in the shul. It would be worthwhile to introduce there the study of *dinim*—at the very least *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch*, or at the very least the *dinim* collected in *Derech HaChaim* by the Gaon of Lissa, which are also printed in several siddurim, including the *Siddur* with *Shaar HaKollel*, the *Siddur Shelah*, and others.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for a good settling-in soon...

P.S.
Please convey my regards to your friend, the esteemed avreich, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent, etc., Mordechai, may he live. It is surprising that since you traveled, no word has been received from him.

## 2270

B"H, 18 MarCheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live.

Peace and blessing!

After the long silence, your letter of the 9th of MarCheshvan, along with its enclosures, was finally received. Thank you, at the very least, for writing now. It is my hope that in the future you will arrange matters so that there are not such long interruptions, as the very knowledge that one is required to write about these matters will add to the avodah itself.

2) Although, in general, I was pleased with the activities of the month of Tishrei, an important element is missing from them: the movement of expansion and growth. After all, one must always increase in holiness (*ma'alin bakodesh*), and regarding your activities since that time, not only have they not grown, but on the contrary. I understand the reasons mentioned—which are also alluded to in your letter—but the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is well known: this concerns the Angel Michael, who records the merits of Yisrael and advocates on their behalf. When there is a valid reason, there is no room for complaint. However, regarding ourselves, the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek is well known: "We are workers of the day, to make things bright." When the activity is missing, the illumination from the Source is also missing, and sometimes even the Source itself in a given place. Further elaboration on this is surely unnecessary.

3) It is surprising that you do not mention the publication of the next issue of the journal. Since the previous ones made a good impression, you will surely continue this in connection with the upcoming special days and the festivals of Chabad, especially the month of Kislev. May Hashem grant you success.

4) I believe I have already alerted you regarding the necessity of taking a special interest in penetrating the circles of Charedi youth (and it is understood that the circles of the yeshivos are the main focus here), and even the circles of youth who are not yet Charedi. In this, the soldiers are also a primary segment, and with the appropriate interest, you will find the ways to reach them as well.

I await good news and conclude with a blessing for success in your holy work, and specifically, for extraordinary success.

## 271

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Yeshiva and Talmud Torah in Kfar Chabad,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your inquiry regarding the fact that until now, the classes there were conducted in Yiddish, and you are uncertain about the coming period for several reasons mentioned in your letter, and you are asking for my opinion on this matter:

Despite the reasons you mention, it is imperative that you continue in these classes specifically in the Yiddish language, just as it has been until now. At a time when we see that the *sitra achra* fights for every *kotz* and *tag*, and nothing is considered too trivial if it serves to win, surely our complete Torah should not be treated as something minor. We must be vigilant even regarding the "thong of a shoe," and all the more so in a matter concerning chinuch, where it is extremely difficult to estimate in advance the consequences that a slight change during the years of childhood will have on the duration of a person’s life. For people like yourselves, further elaboration is surely unnecessary.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and awaiting good news.

## 2 Adar

2 Adar

B"H, 25 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished Torah scholar, who engages in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Avraham Alter, may he live, Shochet and Bodek.

Peace and blessing!

I received your regards with pleasure through the esteemed and distinguished Chossid, who engages in communal needs, Rabbi Menachem Zev HaLevi Greenglass, may he live. When I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you as you requested in your letter.

You are surely aware of what is brought in several places in Chassidus based on the Sages' teaching, "‘And he shall slaughter’ (Vayishchat) — this implies ‘and he shall draw’ (Vemashach)." Just as physically, through a kosher *shechitah*, one draws the animal or bird from its state so that it becomes fit to be blood and flesh like the flesh of man, so too is it in spirituality. One must draw his body and *nefesh habehamis* so that they become fit to be transformed into the *nefesh elokis*—the soul of man, which is called so because it is "like the Most High" (as written in *Sefer Asarah Maamaros*, *Chelek Im Kol Chai*, Part 2, Section 33; in *Shelah*, page 301b; and in many other places). This is accomplished through a kosher *shechitah*—meaning, if the vitality of the *nefesh habehamis* is abundant, through the *shechitah* of two *simanim* (signs), both regarding the desires of eating and drinking (*Berachos* 32a) and regarding the aspiration for the "air" of the environment (*Tanya*, end of Chapter 6), which are the *kaneh* (trachea) and *veshet* (esophagus). And if its vitality is lesser, then at least through the *shechitah* of one of the *simanim*—the one in which it is more deeply invested. And one must be careful with the *veridin* (veins)—to extract the blood and the enthusiasm for animalistic matters—like Rabbi Yehuda (who is named for "I will **thank** [odeh] Hashem"), which is *hoda'ah* (acknowledgment/surrender), even if one does not understand it at the present moment. May Hashem grant you success in accomplishing this within yourself and in your surroundings, now, with proper health and *harchavas hada'as*.

With blessing.

#### ***2 Adar***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 4, p. 1294, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

**Rabbi Avraham Alter, may he live:** Kalipan.

**What is brought in several places:** See above, Vol. 7, Letter 1881, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 2270

2270

B.H., 26 Menachem Av, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have just received your letter dated the 4th of Menachem Av, in which you write that you have scheduled your hernia surgery for this coming Friday.

In addition to the telegram I sent you, I hereby reiterate my blessing that the surgery should take place at a propitious time and be successful, and that you should soon return to your full strength and to your work of assisting the Bnei Yisrael. This assistance in physical matters is, of course, ultimately also assistance in spiritual matters. Furthermore, the physical well-being of the Bnei Yisrael—who are a "kingdom of priests and a holy nation"—is also holy to our G-d. As is well known, the Baal Shem Tov taught that a neshamah descends into a body for seventy years, or eighty years if it reaches the age of strength, for the sake of performing even one favor for a Yid, whether in physical or spiritual matters.

It was a pleasure to read in your letter that you have, in good time, married off your daughter to a fine bochur. Even though you write that it is not easy to influence him in matters of Torah and mitzvos, "according to the effort is the reward." What does it matter to you if the Ribono shel Olam wishes to grant you a great reward? On the contrary, this should only add to your courage in this matter, and all the more so when compared to the efforts parents make to assist their children in physical matters...

It is known that everything a person receives is by way of a loan from the Creator of the world.

The repayment for this is when a person arranges his life and actions in a way that brings nachas ruach to the Lender. Since a person is fashioned from matter and his foundation is from dust, he is prone to stumbling and delays in repayment. However, we have been promised that there is nothing that can stand before one’s will and teshuvah. Furthermore, the attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure": when a person, in his own loans, does not pressure those who owe him—and not only grants them an extension, but does so with a pleasant spirit and with appeasement—this influences the Great Lender, the Ribono shel Olam, to conduct His own dealings in such a manner as well.

I look forward to hearing good news that, following the surgery, your condition is improving and you are returning to your work in the direction mentioned above. May the Hashem grant you the merit to also share good news regarding your son-in-law, your daughter, and your wife, may they live.

With blessings,

## 2276

B"H, 26 Marcheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated Friday, Parshas Chayei Sarah. Regarding your question concerning your sister marrying the brother of your own intended bride—and you ask my opinion on this matter, noting that the intended bride is from a modest family of Torah scholars, etc.—

This matter is addressed in the *Tzava'as Rabbi Yehuda HaChasid*, section 33. The explanation is found in the *Piskei Dinim* of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, Yoreh Deah, page 213a, where he writes that he himself acted to facilitate a marriage between a son and daughter and a daughter and son; see there for the detailed reasoning. This is also discussed in the book *Shivim Temarim*, a commentary on the *Tzava'as Rabbi Yehuda HaChasid*, and in *Otzar HaPoskim* (printed in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established), Even HaEzer, section 2, near the end.

Regarding the practical application: the proposal is appropriate, and may their union be a successful one. It is proper, if it is easy to arrange, that the two couples should not live in the same city—or at the very least, not in the same neighborhood. Such an instruction was given regarding the marriage of two brothers to two sisters; how much more so is this sufficient for the marriage of a son and daughter and a daughter and son, which is considered more lenient. Indeed, even *lechatchilah*, the authorities were not stringent about this; see the *poskim* there. May Hashem grant that it be in a good and successful hour, to build a Chassidishe home.

With blessings, and awaiting good news.

#### ***2276***

**That they should not live in the same city:** See above, Vol. 6, Letter 1707, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 287

B.H., 26 Mar-Cheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Mar-Cheshvan, in which you write regarding the departure of your husband, may he live, to... and that it weighs heavily on your heart and you would prefer not to go, etc.

Your apprehension regarding this has no basis. You must strengthen your *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach and in the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, in whose name the *talmud torahs* and *yeshivos* in... were founded. His departure is not a matter of *agmas nefesh*, *chas v’shalom*; rather, it is the path to *bracha* and *hatzlacha* for all those who take part in it, as well as for their families.

As for the fact that it seems to be connected with difficulties: aside from the fact that one cannot know how great the difficulties are in any other arrangement, these difficulties are, for the most part, only great in one’s eyes because one chooses to view them that way. Primarily, because it is a new situation, it appears this way. When one sees how *anash*, may they live, struggle in the various places where they find themselves, and the difficulties they endure and what they achieve, the inconveniences in... are incomparable and far smaller than theirs.

I also wish to say that for those who go to..., it does not have to be for many years, but for at least one year, because the work cannot be interrupted in the middle of the year. However, after the year has passed, if they themselves request that they wish to leave, and present their reasons, we will then discuss it as one would with a new person who does not yet bear the responsibility of the work. It goes without saying that no one will be forced against their will.

On the other hand, the work that is done, even if it is only for one day, must be done one hundred percent. It must not be done merely to fulfill an obligation, while watching the clock to see when the twenty-four hours will end and one will be rid of the burden. In such a case, it is not only detrimental to the work, but it is also uncomfortable for those who are involved in it.

I wish to reiterate briefly what was said above: after the year in... has concluded, no one will be compelled to continue working in... . However, during the course of the year, I hope I can be certain that the work is being done faithfully, so that the *kavanah* of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, is fulfilled. I am confident that through this work, it is the path and a fitting *keli* to receive the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in everything that you and your family need.

Since a wife has a great influence on her husband, and since it works out that as soon as your husband, may he live, arrives there, he should also prepare the papers to bring you and your children, may they live, there—at that point you will see for yourself that Hashem is present in... as well, and He grants *bracha* and *hatzlacha* there too, and in your case, even more so than in other places. Consequently, both you and your husband, may he live, will be satisfied that Hashem has sent you the opportunity to fulfill His will and to receive His blessings, both *b’gashmius* and *b’ruchnius*.

In anticipation of good news, and with blessings for good health.

## 2278

2278

By the Grace of Hashem, 28 Mar-Cheshvan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, Torah scholar, engaged in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Nissan, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what you mention in your letter: that since the older students remained in a small number, this has caused some of them to feel broken that they were not privileged to be here. You must explain to them that there is no room or reason for such a feeling of brokenness at all. On the contrary, they should view themselves as my shluchim to illuminate their surroundings—the atmosphere and subsequently the people within that atmosphere—with the light of Torah, which is the Torah of Chassidus. Through this, they will also draw them closer to the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah" (see *Likutei Torah*, *Vayikra*, at the beginning, regarding the concept that "a person’s agent is like himself" according to the teachings of Chassidus). This is not something that can be said regarding all the students who are currently in Brooklyn, as is obvious, and the wise will understand.

When they take into account the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that "when a soldier goes to war, he must go with a head held high and with joy," then all the more so in our case, where joy is necessary, and their "walking"—their conduct among those around them—must be specifically with joy. Beyond the fact that this is a **demand** of the Baal Shem Tov, "Serve Hashem with joy," and is hinted at in the **ruling** of the Rambam at the end of *Hilchos Lulav*, this joy is a necessity for the fulfillment of their mission and their role in this world. To elaborate on this is superfluous, and you will surely find the appropriate words to expand upon this in a manner suitable to their current situation. It is unnecessary to note that this also applies to the students who do not feel broken, since the concept of "the sacrifices of G-d are a broken spirit" applies to everyone, but on the other hand, so does the command to "serve Hashem with joy."

Every single soul stood before the Holy King and subsequently descended into a body, all for the purpose of serving its Creator, as the Mishnah states, and to illuminate its portion of the world, as explained in *Tanya* and elsewhere. Our Rebbes, of blessed memory, added further explanation, and in particular my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: that one must work not only with oneself and those close to him, but even with those who are far away, so that the "wellsprings" (and not just well water or drawn water) may spread outward.

It is self-understood that even for this, one is not handed the tools ready-made; one must gird himself with all his strength to find a way to accomplish this. All the more so for one who has been privileged to have Divine Providence place him in a beautiful portion, telling him, "Choose life"—that he must perform his work with true joy that breaks through all barriers, even those of the intellect and emotion, so that his work will naturally be met with overwhelming success.

It is superfluous to explain how great is the compassion for a soul that traveled and descended many levels from before the Holy King and became enclothed in a coarse body and in this material world where the wicked prevail, only to find that it did not fulfill its role, or did not even come close to what was required of it. Conversely, it does not require explanation how great its happiness is when it strives to fulfill its role and endeavors to do so with inwardness and beauty, as explained in many places, including the *Hemshech* of 5666 regarding the manner of service of the true servant.

The same applies to you and your assistants, who have been privileged that Divine Providence and our Nasi, the Nasi of the generation, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, have placed you upon the path of Torah and avodah to illuminate all of Europe with the light of Torah—the essence of the Ein Sof, blessed be He—the Torah of Chassidus. All that has been said above applies to you.

"The study is not the main thing, but the action is the main thing." You must seek every stratagem, piece of advice, and path to increase the *Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim* in Brunoy, both in quality and in quantity. Perhaps for the time being, quantity is more pressing, based on the words of our Sages that "when a thousand enter for Scripture, one emerges for instruction" (see *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshiyos* regarding this teaching of our Sages). Accordingly, you must utilize all possible strengths, all the people who can be utilized, and all matters that can be utilized, in all different ways, so that ultimately the desire is carried out: that Yidden should be Chassidim. As per the saying of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, which we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who said that Chassidus is for all of Klal Yisrael. Consequently, all *Anash* who are under his influence must be harnessed—their strengths, their capabilities, and their time should be utilized for this. Not one of them should be able to say, "I am superfluous and cannot be utilized," with the proof being that they are not given work, etc., even though the obligation rests upon each and every one, as per the demand of the Nesi'im of Chabad that everyone must work personally in their own portion of the world. However, there are many levels of this responsibility, and whoever the Almighty has graced with greater influence, his responsibility is increased many times over.

It is my hope that these few lines will suffice for you to mobilize all those under your influence, and even those outside of it who can be of benefit in this matter. Simply "work" for the dissemination of Chassidus, beginning with the expansion of the Yeshiva in Brunoy, both through Ashkenazic students and Sephardic students, etc., with the maximum quantity and the best possible quality. Not only should those who are working on this until now continue their work and be given the ability to continue, but on the contrary, each one should add strength to this, not only in quality but also in quantity.

It is certainly possible to arrange things so that they do not interfere with one another, and that the arrangement is such that the worker finds satisfaction in the manner of their work and they will not need to be constantly supervised. Surely the Holy One, blessed be He, does not withhold the reward of any creature, and their work will be successful, and their livelihood and the livelihood of their households, may they live, will be as it should be.

I await good news soon, and I sign with a blessing for success in your holy work and with regards to all *Anash*, may they live.

B"H, 1 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you inform me of your birthday and ask whether you should begin wearing Rabbeinu Tam tefillin:

May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success in your study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of *Chassidus* (and it is known that Rabbeinu Tam tefillin are the *mochin* of *Abba*, which relate more to the study of the inner dimension of the Torah), and may you also influence others to bring them closer to the "candle of a mitzvah and the Torah of light," and the "light of the Torah," out of *ahavas Yisrael*.

Furthermore, there should be some holy books found there, such as a Siddur, Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. Every day that the building is open, the people who are there—whether the owners or the employees—should recite something of holiness from one of the aforementioned books, or pray there.

May Hashem grant you success to bring good tidings in all of the above. And the broader your approach, the better it will be for you.

Your check was delivered to the secret charity fund, from which general causes and private individuals who cannot be identified as recipients are supported. This is one of the highest virtues in the mitzvah of tzedakah, and it is especially effective in ensuring that the "evil eye" and the like will not hold sway, and that you may multiply like fish in the midst of the land.

Awaiting good tidings.

## 285

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and scholarly, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Schneur Zalman, may he live, Halevi

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter with pleasure, which also contained a continuation of your memoirs. It is a pity that you are brief in them, and surely, at the appropriate opportunity, you will continue this with additions.

It is surprising that you do not write anything regarding the matter of "sowing spirituality." As is well known, the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to those traveling for matters such as your current trip, is that one must "gather physicality **and** sow spirituality." Since he included them together and in a context of addition, it is proven that the one depends on the other. This is especially true regarding your current status, where even the physicality involved is spirituality; and conversely, the spirituality involved is also physicality—meaning that it must be drawn down below ten tefachim, and not only in physical matters, but also in material ones. This is along the lines of what I wrote in my letter for this past Rosh Hashanah, that one must ensure that the portion of *domem, tzomeiach, chai* (inanimate, vegetative, animate) within a person is also transformed into *adam* (human). And *adam* is from the expression *adameh l'elyon* (I will resemble the Supernal). Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

This is especially relevant in the month of Kislev, the month of redemption, and the month in which the verdict was issued Above that it is permitted—and consequently, mandatory—to disseminate the teachings of Chassidus, and by extension, the matters of Chassidus, with breadth and expansion. As it is recounted, after it was explained to our Alter Rebbe—against whom there was an accusation because he spoke with expansion—the conclusion was nonetheless that since he had already begun, he should continue in this manner.

With blessings for success in your travels, both in gathering physicality and in sowing spirituality.

## 2887

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After the long silence, your letter of 3 Kislev has finally been received, in which you write about the various difficulties in arranging the new students. It is a known statement of the Mechilta that "all beginnings are difficult." And while knowing this statement does not necessarily make things much easier, the bewilderment regarding the matter is removed. Consequently, one should not be discouraged by this; surely Hashem will grant success, provided that you make the effort, and you will succeed in arranging the new class and, in the same vein, the development of the Yeshiva from level to level.

Regarding what you write about the aforementioned students traveling here for the Chag HaGeulah, the upcoming 19 Kislev:

In general, the procedure is that every student must receive permission from the Yeshiva administration. In the letter of authorization, the administration either limits the time or leaves it to the discretion of my secretariat. Based on this, the administration can be very strict. However, the custom in the United States regarding the approach to youth and students is known: not to rely too heavily on their capacity for *kabbalas ol*, and therefore not to bring them into a state of temptation. If, as you write, the desire of some of the students to travel here is strong, perhaps it is worth utilizing this by making it a condition that if they are permitted to travel, it is on the condition that they will be diligent in their studies and excel. But to prevent the trip entirely requires consideration as to whether it is worthwhile, especially since, as you write, they also wish to see their families. On the other hand, their stay here must be limited to only a few days. It is understood that not everyone is the same in this regard, and the Yeshiva administration must decide on the spot regarding each individual.

With blessings for success in your holy work. Surely, since you do not mention anything, all is well among *anash* in your camp. It is a pity that there is not sufficient effort to bring them closer, especially those who were once close and for various reasons have drifted away somewhat.

## 289

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.
