I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 3rd and 11th of Kislev. Regarding Mr. Almalich and the newspaper: I have received a letter from him, along with a copy of the newspaper clipping, and he writes to me that he is relying on me to deny the statements, etc.

Evidently, he has had no prior dealings with newspaper writers, who are generally exempt from accountability for the damage they cause others.

It is better to avoid engaging with them if at all possible. In the present case, since a significant amount of time has already passed since the article appeared, and it seems that people have not paid attention to it, silence is the best course of action for many reasons.

Naturally, I will respond directly to him from here regarding his letter, and I am writing this to you—that should he speak with you again about this matter, it would be appropriate for you to explain to him, on your own initiative, what has been explained above.

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding the study of *shechitah*, as it is generally a sound proposal. One must consider the matter: if it is possible, it would be best to require them to study for a period of time beforehand at the *Tomchei Temimim* in Brunoy as preparation. This is in accordance with what is explained in many places—that a *shochet* must be exceptionally G-d-fearing, and the study of the inner dimension of Torah—which is the teachings of Chassidus (with an emphasis on the word "study," not merely "reciting")—is what leads to the fear of Hashem.

I will discuss this with the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, the dedicated communal worker, R' Binyomin Gorodetzky, as he was on-site, and he will surely receive specific instructions from him regarding the above.

Enclosed is a general letter for the upcoming *Chag HaGeulah*, 19 Kislev. You should certainly publicize it in an appropriate manner, and it would be best to have it printed. You may then send some copies here, as is your custom.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for proper health for you and your entire family, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## 290

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby confirm receipt of your letter dated 4 Kislev. As you requested, I will read your *pidyon nefesh* at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Surely, for someone like yourself, it is superfluous to explain the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the concept of a blessing is analogous to rain, which is effective only after plowing and sowing. Similarly, the efficacy of a *pidyon nefesh* is dependent upon the *hiskashrus* that exists between the petitioner and the one being petitioned. Since it is your desire and will that I read your *pidyon nefesh* at the gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, you must certainly establish a regular study session in the Torah that he taught over the last several years. Many of these *kuntreisim* and books are available in the Holy City of Jerusalem among *anash* and at the Yeshiva.

This month is especially auspicious, as it is the month of the *geulah* of the Alter Rebbe, the founder of the Chabad Chassidic philosophy, and with it, the beginning of the dissemination of the teachings of *Chassidus* in a manner of expansion and explanation that is understandable even to the human intellect. This naturally carries with it the obligation to study the Torah until it is understood and absorbed into the *Chabad* of the soul—not only the *Chabad* of the *nefesh elokis*, but also that of the *nefesh habahamis*. It is well known from our Sages that [the Holy One, Blessed be He] only makes demands according to their capacity, etc.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe,

The Secretary

## 291

9 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated Friday, Parshas Toldos. You will surely not take offense if I say that there are matters about which one should either ask *lechatchilah* (from the outset), or not ask at all.

You have certainly seen the letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe (printed in *Kuntres* 93), stating that he entrusted the publication of the writings, *sefarim*, and *maamarim* of our Nesi’im—both in *nigleh* and in *Chassidus* (and consequently, his own as well)—to Kehot Publication Society. The reasons for this are understandable. One of them is that many manuscripts contain errors, and there are also issues regarding *mahadura kamma* (first editions) and *mahadura basra* (later editions). Furthermore, and most importantly, "everything depends on *mazal*, even a *Sefer Torah* in the *heichal*." Consequently, it is not orderly for everyone to print or copy the aforementioned materials as they see fit. It is desirable to consult with others, and there are other reasons as well. In general, the investigation into these reasons is not as relevant as the fact that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, has already spoken.

Therefore, had one asked *lechatchilah* of Kehot before proceeding to copy the *maamarim*, the matter would have been handled as a *lechatchilah*—whether one should copy these, or whether others should take precedence. However, since a portion of this has already been done, you now ask from New York whether one should halt the printing of the *Torah* of the Rebbe Rashab, or whether one should not halt it, as they want the writings to become more widespread. What answer does one expect to receive to such a question? Especially since you admit in your letter that you have already invested a few hundred pounds into this. There is already an element of *ahavas Yisrael* involved here as well; therefore, one is already bound hand and foot, and one must answer that you should complete it *b’sha’ah tovah u’mutzlach*.

Regarding what you write—that the *Roshei Yeshivos* requested this of you—the fact that the *Roshei Yeshivos* study for themselves the *maamarim* to which they were accustomed during their own time in *yeshivah* is no wonder, for "a person should always learn in the place his heart desires." It is understood that it is easier for them than to begin new ones, as every Nasi in his generation—inevitably—has introduced innovations in his *Torah* teachings; consequently, there must be differences in style and content. However, when one wishes to implement such a system with the students of the *yeshivah*, the *Roshei Yeshivos* and the older *Temimim* should recall their own attitude at that time toward their *mashpi’im*, who wanted to teach them specifically the *maamarim* of the previous Nesi’im and not the *maamarim* of the Nasi of their own generation, the Rebbe Rashab.

The ruling of our Alter Rebbe in *Hilchos Talmud Torah* is well known: that a person, during his lifetime, must study at least once the *Torah Shebiksav* and *Torah Shebe'al Peh* in all their parts. Consequently, this includes the *maamarim* of every Chabad Nasi of all generations. *Aval ani b’daati aamodah* (but I will stand by my opinion): since more than one hundred *kuntresim* of *maamarim* from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, have been printed, as well as *maamarim* from entire years, **they must be established as a fixed study** in *Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim*. May Hashem grant success to each of us to fulfill our *shlichus* in accordance with the truth.

With blessings for *Chag HaGeulah* and success in general and private matters.

P.S. Your letter was delayed in transit because you addressed it to number 177 instead of 770.

## 292

By the Grace of Hashem
10 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash and to all our brothers and sisters of the House of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessings!

In connection with the Chag HaGeulah, the 19th of Kislev—the liberation of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, from his imprisonment for disseminating the teachings, guidance, and customs of Chassidus Chabad—whose liberation and emergence into freedom mark the beginning of the expansion, the broadening, and the dissemination of the path and way of life of Chassidus Chabad in particular, and of Chassidus in general:

I hereby express a heartfelt blessing that each and every one of us be redeemed, and redeem ourselves, from all matters—both internal and external—that bind and oppose the portion of goodness and kindness within every Jew. May this portion become the ruler and master; may the person become a *Chassid*, for he will love and perform acts of kindness, bestowing kindness upon his own soul and bestowing kindness upon his fellow, through the threefold love: love of Israel, love of the Torah, and love of Hashem, which are all one.

***

The statements of our Sages are well known: "Every single soul existed in its image before the Holy King"; souls are hewn from beneath the Throne of Glory.

These statements of our Sages emphasize most strongly what is understood and simple: the purity and clarity of the soul, which is entirely spiritual, and how it has, in and of itself, no connection whatsoever to physical and material matters, and certainly not to matters of desire, etc., which are awakened and arise solely from the body and the *nefesh habehamis*.

Nevertheless, the Holy One, Blessed be He, desired that this soul, which is truly a "part of G-d from above," should descend below and be enclothed in a physical and material body, to be bound and united with it for several decades. This means that for these decades, the soul is in a state that is in complete opposition to its own nature.

And all this is in order to fulfill the mission of the Creator: to refine the body and to illuminate the matters of this physical world that pertain to man with the light of *Ohr Ein Sof*, to make them a sanctuary and a dwelling place for His Divine Presence.

And then, all the suffering and anguish of the soul from being in a body and in a physical world are considered as naught, for the eternal reward and happiness that it merits through fulfilling its mission are *shelo b'erech* (incomparable) to the fleeting sufferings of this world.

***

It is easy to understand the magnitude and depth of the soul’s pain when the sufferings and anguish of the soul in the body are accepted, and even intensified, by the pursuit of physicality and materialism. The intent and purpose of the soul’s descent below—which can be achieved only through daily life according to the Torah and its *mitzvos*—is ignored; and if it is occasionally awakened, it is merely as a "commandment of men learned by rote," done only to fulfill an obligation.

Beyond the main point—that one loses the opportunity to fulfill the will of the Creator and the eternal reward and happiness that comes from it—it is contrary to common sense to pursue and grasp the difficult, evil part of life, namely, to enslave the soul and suppress it in its descent into the body, while rejecting with both hands the good part of the soul’s descent from the "highest height to the deepest depth," which is the great ascent achieved through fulfilling the will of the Creator.

This is what our Sages meant when they said: "A person does not commit a transgression unless a spirit of folly enters him." For it is easy for a person of understanding to see, even without any deep contemplation, that since you are alive by necessity—since the soul, which is truly a "part of G-d from above," must be enclothed in a physical body of dust from the earth for several decades—simple logic dictates that one must strive with tremendous effort to attain the good hidden within this, through daily life according to the instructions of the Torah of our G-d, so that it will be: "In all your ways, know Him."

***

And there is another point to this: Since Hashem, who is the essence of good, compels the soul to descend from the "highest height to the deepest depth" for the sake of Torah study and the performance of *mitzvos*, this is complete proof of how great is study and how great is action (of the *mitzvos*).

From this it also follows that it is impossible to reach the goal except through this great descent—to be according to the Torah specifically here on earth. If there were an easier and more comfortable way, the Holy One, Blessed be He, would not have forced the soul to descend, descent after descent, from beneath the Throne of Glory down to this lowest world, the lowest of all worlds.

Only here, in the "deepest depth," can the soul reach the pinnacle of its stature, even higher than the level of the angels, as our Sages said: "The righteous are on a higher level than the ministering angels."

***

When a person contemplates deeply the magnitude of the stature of Torah and *mitzvos*, and specifically in this world, and that Torah and *mitzvos* are the only way to reach the hoped-for goal, he will come to great joy in his portion and lot—despite the multitude of concealments and hiddenness, both internal and external, that exist in this world. And then, only then, can he truly and internally fulfill the command: "Serve Hashem with joy."

This path of *avodah* is a cornerstone of the Baal Shem Tov’s system, as explained at length in the teachings of Chassidus Chabad, and as instructed by the Alter Rebbe, the master of this joy, in the Tanya, from chapter 26 onwards, and from chapter 31 onwards, in a few lines that contain a great deal.

With blessings for the Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

## 295

I was pleased to receive the news that on Sunday, 15 Kislev, the tenth annual banquet of Yeshivas Achei Temimim of Boston will be celebrated. On this occasion, I greet the administration and all the participants of the banquet with the wish of "Baruchim HaBa'im" (welcome).

When Jews gather for a purpose connected to Torah and mitzvos, one can be certain that it will bear good fruit and meet with success. Especially when it concerns kosher education for Jewish children—upon whom we place our hope that they will continue the golden chain of Torah and mitzvos in the coming generation—this is, in the realm of Torah and mitzvos itself, one of the most select and highly important matters.

This goal and this work must elicit the greatest interest from all Jews in the area to take an ever-greater part in the cause, which in itself draws forth an added blessing and success from the Ribono shel Olam.

Therefore, I am certain that the current banquet will bring about very great results in the material sense, and—what is no less important—also in the spiritual sense.

I hope that each one of those gathered will take away from the banquet an added connection and vitality in matters of Torah and mitzvos in general, and in the vital work of kosher education in particular. According to the promise of our holy Torah, this will bring to each and every one of them, and their families, blessing and success in their personal lives, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success.

## 2890

B"H, 13 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Yehoshua Boruch, may he live:

Shalom and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your regards through your postscript in the letter dated 27 Tishrei last.

Regarding your request for a blessing: your blessing is already stated in the verse, "He will fulfill the desire of those who fear Him"—without limitation as to what that desire may be, provided it is the desire of one who fears Hashem. Since your occupation, my dear friend, is in drawing forth fear of Hashem for the Children of Israel through the matter of mikvaos—as explained in the Rambam at the end of Hilchos Mikvaos, that the immersion, etc., is a "decree of the King," etc., yet "there is a hint to the matter," etc., "one who directs his heart to purify his soul, etc., and brings his soul into the waters of knowledge, he is pure," etc.—it follows that just as in the physical act of immersion one must immerse his head and his entire body in the water—meaning that his entire body, even the most secondary parts of his body, must be covered by simple water—so too is it in the spiritual sense. The purification from the impurity caused by the sin of the Tree of Knowledge comes when one nullifies his entire being, starting from the intellect in the head and ending with the simplest faculty in the soul, which is the power of walking in the feet, into "simple water." This means humility (see Taanis 7a), a simple humility without sophistication; this purifies one from the impurity of [erroneous] opinions, through which one comes to fear Hashem, for "humility leads to fear" (end of Sotah). This is why the masters of truth said that the word *tevilah* (immersion) is composed of the same letters as *bitul* (nullification), and all the more so, this leads to a strengthening of the avodah that brings one to fear of Hashem.

Without a vow, when I am at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you as you requested.

Please convey my regards to the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs in faith, R' Efraim Zalman, may he live, with a blessing for success in your holy work.

#### ***2890***

**R' Yehoshua Boruch:** Levi, Jerusalem.

## B"Sh

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and esteemed R' Yitzchak Yaakov, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 10th of Kislev. I was pleased to read that your health has improved and that you are happy with your lot; may Hashem grant you success so that your portion may increase and your joy may grow.

Regarding what you write concerning talking during davening, etc.: It is well known how much our predecessors have cried out about this for many generations. Yet, after all that, you have surely heard the story from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that in his youth he asked his father, the Rebbe, why man was created with two eyes. His father answered him that with the right eye one must look at others with a *ayin yafah* (a favorable eye), and with the left eye, at the desires of this world.

When one takes into account that for these people, every davening takes place in the midst of their business and worldly affairs, and that despite this they pause and set aside time to daven before the Ribono shel Olam—this in itself will strengthen the side of good within them over the other side, and consequently, they will draw closer to the guidance of our holy Torah even in their day-to-day life.

It is understood that one should not always announce this matter, lest they use it as a form of justification for the aforementioned behavior. But for oneself, one must know the calculation: to look with the right eye—a favorable eye—and the aforementioned idea makes the matter easier.

Enclosed is what has been printed for the upcoming Chag HaGeulah, 19 Kislev, the essence of which is truly relevant all year round.

With blessings for proper health.

#### ***B'Sh***

**R' Yitzchak Yaakov:** Nelson.

**Printed for Chag HaGeulah:** The *maamar* "Padah B'Shalom" 5704.

## B'sha

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...In general, regarding matters such as these—and in conflict and strife in general—it requires the participation of two parties. When one side sees that no attention is being paid, and that no one is becoming agitated or participating in the conflict, then, little by little, their own agitation and appetite for it begin to diminish until, eventually, it is lost entirely. In the present case as well, this is so: it is necessary to restrain one’s spirit and not enter into a *shakla v’tarya*. Bearing in mind that "the mind of women is light" and "a woman’s tear is readily available," one should concede where it is possible to concede, and regarding the rest, pay no mind. Consequently, in the end, the side of good will prevail.

...Regarding what you wrote about your response to the *avreich*... While, in general, one must be careful not to create the impression that we are "chasing after them," one cannot, in the final analysis, lose sight of the goal: to bring them the knowledge of Chassidus, its Torah, and its guidance. Because of the magnitude of this matter, one cannot take into account considerations that do not hold weight against it. Therefore, after waiting a few days, it is worthwhile to steer the conversation from topic to topic until, eventually, an opportunity arises to once again inspire them regarding the matter of *kavius itim l’Torah* in general, and the matters of Chassidus in particular.

## 222

B.H., 17 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch
in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, may they live.

Peace and Blessing!

...2) Regarding what you mentioned, that you received proposals from school administrators... that since, for various reasons, they will not be maintaining a certain school in the year 5714, they are offering to transfer them into the Reshet: You must be cautious here, for it is highly probable that even if the school’s directors have the authority and power of attorney to do so, once the matter becomes known to others, and upon further reflection they find it disagreeable, they will attack you with full force and vigor. In that event, even those who handed the matter over to you will withdraw their support, etc.

3) You mention in your letter that you met with... It is long known that the Lubavitch approach is not to involve itself at all in partisan matters. Certainly, this should be explained pleasantly and in a spirit of peace. If the approach of "sit and do nothing" is sufficient, one should be content with that, but in any case, do not take upon yourselves any matter that has any partisan affiliation.

4) You also write that there are places where schools from other streams will be handed over to you, in accordance with the new law that there must be only one school. It is surely unnecessary to draw your attention to the caution required so that this does not affect in the slightest the sovereignty, authority, and ownership you must have over the school. It is well known that sometimes, one who wishes to destroy relies on the verse, "Your destroyers... shall go forth from you" (Yeshayahu 49:17). They begin with the approach of "today he tells him this"—meaning they agree to everything—but once they are inside, they express their own opinions, and from time to time with increasing force, and a word to the wise is sufficient. It is possible that this has no basis in the current case, and one must decide based on the local situation; I have only come to urge you to consider the matter from this perspective as well. Surely Hashem will protect you from any stumbling block, G-d forbid, and may the will of Hashem succeed in your hands to magnify Torah and make it glorious in the spirit of the Israel of old, by drawing the hearts of the sons and daughters of Israel to our Father in Heaven through the inner education they will receive through you in the institutions of the Reshet.

5) In your letter regarding the conclusion of the previous year, you write of your hope that you will soon receive what is due to you from the various offices for the Reshet schools in the different locations, etc., and the sum is over 12,000 Lira. It is puzzling that you do not write in detail what part of this has been realized, for you are surely utilizing all possible means to receive these sums in full.

6) I am somewhat troubled—and I hope that perhaps my concern is baseless—by the fact that, based on what you write regarding the negotiations you had with the representative of..., I get the impression that for you, too, the matter has entered the realm of external victory, and consequently you wish to expand as much as possible to show that you emerged victorious. While sometimes this is also necessary—for through "I will walk in a wide place" (Tehillim 119:45) one may be able to nullify obstacles and delays without any further action—in the current case (where the goal is the education of Jewish children in the spirit of fear of Heaven), one should not increase the difficulties, even slightly. It is known and seen clearly that when one proceeds in ways of peace and pleasantness, there is no feeling of victory on the other side, and when the other side speaks only based on reason, it is easier to reach an understanding with them...

It is understood that I do not at all intend by this to abandon the school there, but what is necessary, as much as one can estimate from a distance, is to remove, as far as is in your power, the perception that this is a fierce war and that you wish to conquer the entire village, etc. Rather, since the parents demand a specific type of education and the owners of the Reshet are experts in this, you are confident that you will fulfill the parents' wishes, and not force your own views upon them, etc., etc.

8) It is understood that what was said in section 4 regarding the caution in taking into your possession a school of a party or another stream: if the deed has already been done, then on the contrary, changing it might exacerbate relations, etc., and in that case, one must only take the appropriate measures and form so that there is no room for the aforementioned concerns. But it is also obvious that sending children who are under your jurisdiction to a school that is under the jurisdiction of other teachers—meaning that you did not hire them and you do not have authority over them—is absurd, and it is impossible to accept any responsibility whatsoever for education provided by others.

9) Regarding your question in the letter of the 6th of Cheshvan as to whether it is worthwhile to respond to matters printed in the newspapers: as experience has shown, entering into debates, etc., in the newspapers is a bottomless pit. Furthermore, at the end of the day, the newspapers are in the possession of others, not yours. Regarding responding in court, etc., my position has long been known that this is a path to consider only after all other possibilities have been exhausted.

With blessings for success in your holy work, awaiting good tidings as soon as possible.

## 252

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and industrious in communal affairs, R' Avraham Yaakov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter—though it was not dated—in which you write about your study schedule with the various classes. May Hashem grant you success in instilling in your students the Torah of the living G-d and a spirit of pure fear of Heaven.

Regarding your question as to whether you should attend the Bar Mitzvah of one of your students: You do not specify where the Bar Mitzvah will take place. If it is to be held in a synagogue where it is forbidden to pray, and—as is the custom of the land—they will conduct the Bar Mitzvah during the prayer service, including *aliyos* and so forth, which involves many halachic issues, it is not advisable to participate. This is so that your presence is not construed as an endorsement, for if you attend, others will certainly feel that they, too, may attend and pray there, and so on. However, if the Bar Mitzvah is being held in a different location and not during the prayer service, surely a way can be found for you to participate without it implying an endorsement of forbidden practices.

With blessings for success in both general and personal matters, and awaiting good news.

P.S. Enclosed are receipts for the checks you sent. Also enclosed is a copy of my general letter regarding the *Chag HaGeulah*, 19 Kislev, the content of which is truly relevant all year round. I am certain you will publicize its content to those for whom it is appropriate.

## B'shaz

B'shaz

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 9th of Kislev, Motzaei Shabbos Vayishlach, as well as those that preceded it.

You must tell your wife, *tichyeh*, that she should not overthink anything. Especially as I have already written, this indicates a lack of *emunah* in Hashem Yisbarach, who—*Baruch Hu*—is the essence of good, and therefore desires to do good for Yidden. This is certainly true when it concerns the request for *zera chaya v'kayama*, which is a mitzvah of the Torah given to every one of us. It is therefore certain that Hashem Yisbarach will grant blessing and success to fulfill this request. Being nervous about this—and certainly crying—only weakens the body and also weakens the *emunah* of the *neshamah*. Therefore, one should not allow such things to take hold. May Hashem Yisbarach help you both to share good news regarding this.

I was pleased to read in your letter about the various people you have encountered who asked you to convey regards and the content of what was discussed at the *farbrengen* this past month of Tishrei. It is my hope that you will continue to maintain a connection with them, as it is known that the connection of Yidden together brings benefit to all participants, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter in connection with *Chag HaGeulah*, the 19th of Kislev, which will surely be of benefit to you in connection with the aforementioned.

Regarding the *bochur* who asked you if there are commentaries on *Tanya*: you can tell him that, for the time being, there are none in print. However, when one approaches the study of *Tanya*, one must know that it is a part of Torah and should be studied like other parts of Torah. Just as when one studies *Chumash*, *Mishnayos*, *Gemara*, or *Rambam* for the first time, one does not demand of oneself—at the beginning, or even the second or third time—to understand every nuance and commentary. Rather, one first understands the matter in a general sense, and from time to time, more is added to that understanding. If one studies *Tanya* with a pure intention, it is like the rest of Torah: every Yid can understand what it is, yet no one can reach its depths, for "its measure is longer than the earth and broader than the sea." If the aforementioned *bochur* does not understand a specific detail in *Tanya*, I am confident that if he explains his question to *anash*, *shiy*, they will teach him. You may tell him this.

You may give one copy of the aforementioned general letter to the *bochur*.

With blessings.

## 2809

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Meir Lieber, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...I was most pleased by the good news regarding the expansion of the circle of students in their Tanya shiur. It is already a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that when one sees success in matters such as these, it should inspire an increase in strength and effort to expand these activities even further. One should say to himself: If, with the effort exerted until now—which was small in proportion—the Ribono shel Olam granted such success, then how much more so would this be the case had they exerted the proper effort! Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter in connection with the Chag HaGeulah, 19 Kislev. It would be appropriate to consult with the esteemed R' Eliyahu Moshe Liss, may he live, as to whether it is worthwhile to publicize its content among the participants of the shiur, and in what manner.

With blessing, and awaiting good news.

***

**R' Meir Lieber, may he live:** Keller. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 6, 1662, and in the references noted in the footnotes there [that letter is also from the year 5714, and was written in continuation of the letter before us].

**If, with the effort:** See also below, letter 2507.

## B'shi

B'shi

B"H, 23 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, engaged in communal needs, R' Asher, may he live and be well.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive reports from Anash, may they live, in Melbourne regarding your participation and assistance in the development of the Yeshiva Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch there. Although you will surely continue to act with the appropriate vigor in the future, according to the Sages' dictum, "One only encourages the diligent," I am writing these lines—not because it is necessary, but to emphasize that you should exert yourself in this matter with all your ability, and even beyond your ability.

According to what is explained in Chassidic discourse regarding the difference between the avodah of people before Matan Torah and after Matan Torah—"Your name is like oil poured forth"—before Matan Torah, before the decree that "the inhabitants of the lower realms shall not ascend to the higher realms" was nullified, a person could only achieve and accomplish through his avodah according to his own capacity, his root, and the root of his root, but no higher than the source of created beings. This is not the case after Matan Torah, when the aforementioned decree was nullified, "Hashem descended upon Mount Sinai," and "Moshe ascended," etc. Now, a person can accomplish not only by drawing down from the source of created beings, but even from a level higher than that. To elaborate on this for someone like you is surely unnecessary.

The reason I am writing to you about this now is that the organization of the Yeshiva there requires fundamental changes. It is my hope that, ultimately, they will be established and spread throughout the city itself, and subsequently in its surroundings. It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: "As one sets oneself up, so it proceeds." Therefore, one must muster all one's strength to establish this in a way that will be for a name and for glory, especially since this is the only Yeshiva in all of Australia, and from it will come the outcomes of life for all matters of religion in this country.

Awaiting good news, and signing with honor and blessing.

## 2513

2513

B.H., 24 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter requesting prayers on your behalf:

It is well known that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, spoke regarding the concept of a blessing being analogous to rain. Just as rain causes growth only when there has been plowing and sowing, so too with a blessing: the recipient must perform the "plowing" themselves. This means a broken and contrite heart, achieved through contemplation of the greatness of the Creator, may He be blessed, which naturally leads to an awareness of one’s own lowliness (see the commentary of the *Tur* in *Berachos*, beginning of chapter *Ein Omdin*, which is cited as a halachic ruling in the *Hagahos HaRema* to *Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chayim*, section 98, end of paragraph 1). The "sowing" is achieved by giving *tzedakah* before *davening* and by beautifying the *mitzvos*. When this is done, the blessing brings success, as stated in the *parsha* regarding the blessings of Yitzchak: that even in that land and in that year, he found a hundredfold—as the *Targum* and our Sages explain, a hundredfold in his grain.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize to you the absolute necessity of studying the inner dimension of the Torah—especially in these generations, as we have been informed by the *AriZal* that it is a *mitzvah* to reveal this wisdom—particularly for *avreichim* who dwell in the tents of Torah and are occupied with its study. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success.

With blessings for success in Torah study with *yiras shamayim*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary:

***

**Regarding the concept of a blessing:** See also letter 2290 above, and the references in the notes there.

**And it is cited as a halachic ruling:** See also letter 2251 above.

## 214

24 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...To highlight a lesson from the days of Chanukah: As the Rambam writes at the beginning of Hilchos Chanukah, the decree was that they "stretched out their hand, etc." From this, the salvation subsequently blossomed, as the sovereignty returned to Yisrael because the Jewish people stood firm in their trial through mesiras nefesh. And according to the Rashbam—Pesachim 108b—the miracle of Chanukah came about through women. So too in our days, through the mesiras nefesh with which Bnei Yisrael guard the flask of oil within the depths of their souls—which is the concept of the "seal of the Kohen Gadol"—may miracles be performed for us in this time as well, to illuminate the Sanctuary within each and every Jew with pure oil for all eight days, until the One who is unique among the eight shepherds arrives, and the harp of eight strings is revealed.

## 215

B"H, 24 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, [a man of] action and wisdom,
Rabbi Matisyahu Yechezkel, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your gift: the book of the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and his descendants, and the new edition of the book of the teachings of Rabbi Pinchas of Koritz. Many thanks for this gift. May Hashem grant you the ability to disseminate the teachings of the Nesi’ei HaChassidus and their greats to the widest possible circles, with peace of mind and proper health.

As you requested, I am sending you in a separate package the Tanya that was printed here in a new edition with indices, etc., and I am sure you will confirm receipt. Also enclosed is a publication issued in connection with the Chag HaGeulah, the 19th of Kislev, which I am sure will be of interest to you.

Regarding your request for my comments: while I do not have the time to examine them as thoroughly as required, out of affection for the matter, I have leafed through the pages. In my opinion, the lack of indices is even more apparent in these books. Furthermore—in the book of the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and his descendants—in quite a few maamarim, it is not clear to whom they belong. There should also have been an explicit instruction that some of the maamarim were brought with variations in wording.

**By the way:** The name of the daughter of the Baal Shem Tov should be spelled Adel, without a yud, as it is an acronym for: **Eish Das Lemo** (a fiery law unto them).

The son of the Baal HaTanya should not be referred to as Rabbi Dov **of Liadi**, for he conducted his leadership in **Lubavitch**. The Rabbi Dov of Liadi was the grandson of the Tzemach Tzedek, the son-in-law of the aforementioned.

In the book of the teachings of Rabbi Pinchas of Koritz, **section 121**, it mentions in the manuscript—he is there in the name of the Yerushalmi, even though it is not found in the Yerushalmi before us. See Torah Or, in the additions to the end of Parshas Tisa.

With blessings for success in your endeavors.

## 2816

B"H, 24 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Dovid Nosson, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive the candles to be used for Chanukah. Surely you are familiar with the saying of the Tzemach Tzedek, who interpreted the verse "He called the light Day" (Yom) — but the text says "Shemesh" (Sun), and he explained that it refers to the *shamash* (the attendant candle), for even the sun and moon are called *shamashim* (attendants) in the heavens.

May it be the will of Hashem that this be fulfilled within us as well: to shine light in our surroundings, each according to his ability, and from a place of true *harchavas hadaas*.

May the mitzvah of these eight days bring us, in the very near future, to the coming of the one who is unique among the eight shepherds, our righteous Moshiach, and to the revelation of the harp of eight strings.

With blessings for success in your *avodah* in holiness to shine light.

P.S.
I hereby acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your gift, the book *Sova Semachos*, and many thanks for this.

As is my custom year after year, I rely on the statement of the Zohar that a matter of a mitzvah should not be free of charge; therefore, I have paid for it, and may you enjoy it in good health.

## 2117

B"H, 24 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Vayeitzei, following the long silence. Regarding what you wrote about taking stock of your time in your city: in general, the time for such an accounting is the month of Elul. Throughout the rest of the year, one should only make the kind of calculations that one is certain will not bring about a weakening in one’s avodah, and certainly will not provide any room for even a shred of despair. As the witticism goes: "Despair is *shelo mada'as* (without knowledge/mindfulness)." It is also understood that this is the complete opposite of the Baal Shem Tov’s demand to "Serve Hashem with joy," for the term "serve" also includes the concept of "In all your ways know Him," as explained in Rambam, Hilchos Deios, and in Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, siman 231.

I was pleased to hear what you wrote regarding the month of Tishrei, even though you wrote very briefly. My hope is that this is merely a deficiency in writing, but not in actual practice.

Regarding writing for the newspaper: it is unnecessary to elaborate on the benefit of this, and therefore I wish to hope that from here on, you will exert yourself in this matter with the appropriate vigor.

Regarding what you wrote about your own personal "four amos": it is known that all the aforementioned does not justify a lack of avodah within one’s own four amos. On the other hand, in this area as well, sadness is closer to laziness than to alacrity. Therefore, you should begin with something practical—namely, learning—even if it is only through *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke), at least for a short time each day, and for a longer time during your more free hours. When there is a seed of growth in potential, it is easier to bring it into actualization.

Enclosed is the printed material for the Chag HaGeulah of Yud-Tes Kislev that has passed, which I am sure you will merit to share with the many, for in truth, its content is relevant all year round.

With blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S.
Regarding the chazarah of Chassidus at the wedding—in a good and auspicious hour—it is appropriate, in addition to the maamar you mention in your letter, to also repeat the D'H "Lecha Dodi" of 5689, based on the sicha of Simchas Torah 5713. It is surprising that you were not aware of this.

It is worthwhile to begin wearing Rabbeinu Tam tefillin. May Hashem grant you success.

## 2220

B”H, 27 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from 1 Kislev, as well as the one preceding it, along with their enclosures. I enjoyed reading about the schedule of classes and studies you have implemented in the grades under your supervision, which will surely be successful. However, on the face of it, this is a very long schedule, as it concludes at midnight and studies begin again at nine in the morning. One must also look after the health of the body, as this relates to the avodah of the neshamah. I also told the avreich... shlita, when he was here, that he should look for a way to take some of the studies off his shoulders so that he has more time to rest and renew his strength for his work.

I read with joy in both your letters that you are seeing success in your communal activities. According to our Sages, of blessed memory, "he to whom kindness is shown is not quickly..."—my hope is strong that you will tangibly see Hashgacha Pratis in your affairs in the future as well. Consequently, your work will be eased, and you will be able to perform it with greater vigor, which will naturally lead to even greater results.

Regarding your request for papers for the students to come study at Tomchei Temimim here, I have passed their names on to the Yeshiva office, and they will surely be in touch with you.

I will read the list of students you sent me at an auspicious time at the holy Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may his merit shield us, for their success in Torah study and yiras shamayim.

Regarding your personal question about a shidduch with a girl from a Sephardic family: as you describe it in your letter, they are a family that observes Torah and mitzvos. Therefore, it is worthwhile to pursue the matter, especially since she has agreed regarding the beard and also regarding the covering of the hair. As we know from Sephardic families, the matter of taharas hamishpachah is observed by them with hiddur. As for your parents, may they live and be well, you can put their minds at ease, as in recent years several shidduchim have taken place between Ashkenazic and Sephardic families, and both sides are very satisfied.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon you will build a home in Israel on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are illuminated by the "light of Torah"—this is the teachings of Chassidus—a Chassidishe home in every respect.

With regards and blessings, awaiting good news, and with blessings for extraordinary success in all your affairs.

P.S. It does not seem right to me that you write that you are delaying the wedding because you are currently unable to earn enough for your livelihood. For it is known from our Sages, of blessed memory—cited in Likutei Torah at the end of Parshas Beracha—that the Holy One, Blessed be He, provides a man with his livelihood for the sake of his wife.

Enclosed is a copy of a general letter I published in connection with the Festival of Redemption, 19 Kislev, the content of which is relevant all year round, and it will surely be of benefit to you in your affairs.

## 222

28 Kislev, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter. Please forgive the delay in my response, which was due to an abundance of preoccupations.

Regarding the contents of your letter concerning your son, the avreich, who wishes to travel to study in a yeshiva, relying on the ruling of our Sages, "Go into exile to a place of Torah"—I have agreed to this. It does not appear to me as you suggest, due to his state of health, especially since his education is also guaranteed while he is at home.

Now, for you and those like you, it is surely unnecessary to bring all the explanations and reasons stated regarding the aforementioned Mishnaic ruling that one should "go into exile to a place of Torah." The main point is whether or not the reason is accepted; since the reason is not explicitly stated in the Mishna, we have only the words of the Mishna itself. It is self-understood that this implies no slight to the honor of the parents or any lack of trust in them, especially according to the interpretation that the author of this statement, Rabbi Nehorai, is Rabbi Elazar ben Arach, who experienced this personally, as explained in Maseches Shabbos (147b).

Regarding what you wrote concerning the preservation of his health: one must certainly make an effort in this regard in the places to which he will travel. Both in the United States and in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, he will be able to find friends and loved ones who will look after your son to the extent possible. Furthermore, it is known that physical health depends to a great extent on the satisfaction of the soul. The very fact that your son will find himself in an environment of friends who are compatible with his spirit will also add to his physical health, whereas if he were isolated and in a state of frequent dissatisfaction, it would be otherwise.

On this occasion, I would like to point out another matter, which concerns the study of the teachings of Chassidus. It seems, between the lines of your letter, that you are not entirely comfortable with this. Relying on what I heard several times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding what he witnessed tangibly, I write the following:

It is known that in years past, there were several approaches regarding the education of the youth: whether it should consist solely of Shas, Rishonim, Acharonim, and Poskim, or whether it should also include the study of Mussar and Chassidus. It is known that about sixty or seventy years ago, the Geonim in the Lithuanian yeshivos strongly opposed even the study of Mussar, arguing that the study of Shas and Poskim is sufficient, that "Torah protects and saves," and furthermore, that even for one who has strayed from the path, the "light" within the Torah will return him to the right way. But as the decades passed, life demonstrated with living proof that some study which speaks directly to the matters of human character, the feelings of the soul, and the "duties of the heart" is essential—to the point that even the great scholars of Lithuania admitted and agreed to the study of Mussar, to a greater or lesser extent.

For those who have merited to benefit from the light of the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, his disciples, and the disciples of his disciples who followed him—who brought into life the directive of the Arizal that in our generation it is a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom (Pnimiyus HaTorah)—and furthermore, when the Baal Shem Tov asked Mashiach, "When will the Master come?" and the answer was, "When your wellsprings spread outward"—it is beyond any doubt that the study of the teachings of the disciples of the Baal Shem Tov is a necessity.

Nevertheless, in the previous generation, there was room for the approach that one could suffice with a very small measure of this study, because they were confident that the youth would have no connection to the study of philosophy and would not encounter those who would question him on matters of the "duties of the heart," matters of faith, and so on. But in our generation, and especially in recent years, when the decrees and destructions, G-d forbid, came and confused the entire world, and the youth and avreichim stand before the most difficult trials—and to our sorrow, it is unavoidable that they will encounter those who cast doubt on everything holy, and even on the foundations of faith—it is essential that they know what is stated in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and his disciples. This is a part of our holy Torah, and as our Sages say, "Everything that a veteran student will eventually innovate was already given to Moshe at Sinai," so that he will not be affected by what he hears from others.

Even if one were to find someone who says he is certain that his son or relative will never encounter those who are not G-d-fearing and observant (which is contrary to the words of our Sages, "Do not believe in yourself until the day of your death"), experience has shown the opposite. But even according to the one who says this, he cannot escape doubt; and it is known that in a matter of *pikuach nefesh*, one desecrates the Shabbos even for a *safek sfeika* and many other doubts.

It is universally agreed that the teachings of Chassidus are a part of our holy Torah. And even if, regarding himself, someone says he wants to study this part only after some time, it is simple that when a Jewish person comes and says that his soul desires a specific part of the Torah—which was said to Moshe at Sinai and from the mouth of the Almighty Himself—one must strengthen and encourage him to take courage in studying this part of the Torah. Especially since this is the part of which it is said that they ask, "Did he bring up a *kav* of wheat?" and if, G-d forbid, he did not bring it up, then as the Sages say (Shabbos 31a), "It would be better if you had not brought up the wheat at all."

As for me, you should thank Hashem, who has aroused a spirit of purity in your son, and that he desires to study Pnimiyus HaTorah, which, in the words of the holy Zohar (Part III, 152a, see there), is the "soul of the Torah." Just as the soul gives vitality to the body, so too does Pnimiyus HaTorah give vitality to the study of the revealed Torah. My hope is strong that you will receive much *nachas* from him.

With blessings for success in his holy work, and awaiting good tidings.

## 2263

B"H, the fifth night of Chanukah, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the entire congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and cherishers of Torah and mitzvos, may Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and abundant blessings!

The annual celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, which will, G-d willing, take place on Sunday, 13 Shevat, 5714, deserves the serious attention and greatest support of the broad Jewish public.

Since the Lubavitcher Yeshiva was founded 57 years ago by the Rebbe Rashab, and was also planted in America 14 years ago by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the Lubavitcher yeshivos here in this country have flourished with extraordinary Divine success.

It is impossible to measure the great illumination of the study of Torah with yiras shamayim that the **Tomchei Temimim** yeshivos have spread and continue to spread throughout all these years. This is thanks to the unique character of these yeshivos, whose students and those they educate are raised with the sense of responsibility to be "lights to illuminate"—to revive and strengthen Torah and Yiddishkeit all around them.

Just like the Chanukah lights, which are kindled after sunset—though they are small, they are not intimidated by the darkness; on the contrary, from night to night their number increases and their light grows stronger—

So too are the "lights to illuminate"—the students and those educated by the Lubavitcher yeshivos.

And just as the mitzvah of the Chanukah light originated from the fact that Jews, being few in number and weak in physical strength, fought with mesiras nefesh against a numerous and powerful enemy in order to purify and illuminate the Beis HaMikdash—so too must every Jew, to whom Torah and mitzvos are dear, not be intimidated by the fact that in number we are a minority compared to others, and in money we are weaker than they. On the contrary, one must fight with mesiras nefesh for the **Ribono shel Olam's** Torah and mitzvos (Your Torah, the laws of Your will). And then the Ribono shel Olam helps with supernatural success, in both gashmius and ruchnius.

The Lubavitcher yeshivos, which educate students in this spirit of mesiras nefesh and the study of Torah with yiras shamayim, should and must be supported with all one's strength, to the greatest extent. For with the pure and holy light of Toras Hashem Temimah with pure yiras shamayim, the difficult path of our people in golus is illuminated, and Jews are preserved in their wholeness,

Until the Ribono shel Olam's promise is fulfilled and the Geulah Shleimah and Amitis arrives, and the pure Menorah will once again shine in the Beis HaMikdash, which will be built by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days.

With the blessing that Hashem fulfill the desires of your hearts for good, and that we all merit the raising of the horn of Torah and the horn of Israel, our ancestors, very soon.

## 2,324

B"H, 2 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It has already been discussed once at a farbrengen that, in general, everyone agrees with all the matters stated in books of mussar, and certainly in the books and maamarim of Chassidus. The entire point of contention, however, is whether these things apply to oneself, or if all of this is spoken about someone else. Certainly, for someone like you, it is superfluous to elaborate on the concept that "days are fashioned, and for him one of them" — how all the days and moments are important and measured for each person, suited to the matters of his specific role... Yet, such conduct is astonishing to me: that after Hashem granted you the success to take part in one of the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, you then cease your involvement for several months...

I also have an obligation to write, before concluding this letter, that the conduit for blessing and success — both in personal matters and in general matters — is through our Nasi, my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Anyone who adds strength and courage to their hiskashrus to the "tree of life" through his holy institutions, in the literal sense, also adds to the influence and drawing down of the aforementioned.

I await your reply as soon as possible.

## 2525

2525

By the Grace of Hashem, 2 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from 2 Kislev, in which you write that the students have been tested and that success is visible in their learning, and also regarding the farbrengen you organized for 19 Kislev, etc.

And although you write that the farbrengen did not have the same "taste" as in [previous times]... see Tanya, Chapter 27, regarding the precision of the verse, "And make for me **delicacies**" (in the plural). Between the two types of delicacies, one cannot know which is more accepted Above; consequently, it must be tasteful Below as well.

The main point, however, is the well-known parable of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: wherever the general stations a soldier, if the general is a good one, the soldier can be certain that he has been chosen for the most suitable post—where there is the maximum good for him, as well as the greatest utility for the war and the victory. And although this should not stop the soldier from requesting **a higher** rank for himself, as long as he has not yet attained it, the soldier must be in a state of immense and great joy, for by carrying out his mission, he is connected with the entire administration of the state. The application of the parable is understood.

Hopefully, you utilized the days of Chanukah, both regarding the children and the adults, to tell them that Yidden have always had nisyonos—perhaps even greater than the current ones—and when one stands with the appropriate strength, one succeeds not only in ruchniyus but also in gashmiyus.

Regarding your questions on the method of study: it is self-evident that one must teach the students the letters separately and the nekudos separately, as is known from the battle that the gedolei Yisrael and our holy Nasi waged for this, to engrave in the children the holiness of the letters and the holiness of the nekudos.

With blessings for success in parnassah in gashmiyus, and for success in parnassah in ruchniyus, and with regards to all.

Waiting to hear good news.

Due to a certain reason, the sending of this letter was delayed. In the meantime, your letter of 4 Teves has arrived... [stating] that you understood the nisayon and have traveled to the town to spread Yiddishkeit. Although business is not yet as you would like, I calculate that now business can improve. And I hope that if you are tested through the other extreme—through many customers—you will also pass the "exam" and continue your holy work in the town.

And surely it will be with success. And "more than the householder does for the poor man, the poor man does for the householder."

## B'shal

B'shal

B"H, 3 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Moreinu HaRav Yosef, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding your observation concerning the mention in the English Chanukah booklet of the name "Syria," at a time when the phrasing in the words of our Sages is "the kingdom of Greece"—it is known that regarding whoever comes first, there is no obligation to detail his words, whereas those who come after must explain their words in detail in order to avoid error. Since the name "kingdom of Greece" includes several countries and several kingdoms that grew out of the kingdom of Greece of Alexander of Macedon (and specifically, the country of Greece is on the European peninsula and not in Syria, which is in Asia), they chose a more precise name to protect the reader from error.

As for why the name "Greece" was established in the text of the prayer, there are several intentions that can be suggested. The simplest one, seemingly, is that the war was waged in the name of Greek culture, its philosophy, and its customs. In addition to the reason that from the time of the end of the exile of Media and Persia until the beginning of the exile of Edom—which is Rome—the persecutions and exiles that occurred in the interim are called by the name "exile of Greece" in the words of our Sages, and for this, too, the reason mentioned above can be suggested.

Regarding your note about the name of the town "Krushta," it is a copyist's error and should be "Krutche" (mentioned in the letters of the *Avos HaChassidim* printed in *HaTamim*).

Enclosed is what you requested in connection with the bright day of our redemption and the salvation of our soul, the 19th of Kislev that recently passed, the content of which is relevant throughout the entire year. I hope it will be of interest to you.

With blessings for the true blessing in both body and soul.

#### ***B'shal***

**Moreinu HaRav Yosef:** Player. Additional letters to him—above, Vol. 7, 1878, and in the references in the footnotes there.

## B'shlav

B'shlav

B"H, 4 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

An inquiry was received in your name regarding the removal of a beard: whether there is a difference in the manner in which it is done, or if there is no difference at all.

Certainly, there is a very **great** difference. This can be understood through an analogy. There are beverages that are poison to a person, and when a person drinks them, the strictest measures must be taken to heal him from the damage caused to the human body—even if he drinks it only once, and certainly if he drinks it multiple times. On the other hand, there are things that also harm a person, but only when they reach a specific part of the body; in another part of the body, they do not cause harm, although they do not provide any benefit either. For example, when a person eats the peels of potatoes or melons, which certainly provide no benefit and one should seek to rid oneself of them as soon as possible, there is no danger when they enter the stomach. However, when they enter the lungs, they cause the greatest harm to the person.

So too, more or less, are there cases regarding the soul of a Yid. There are things that are poison to the soul; these are aveiros that all Yidden are equally obligated to avoid. If a non-Yid does them, it does not harm him, but for a Yid, it causes harm—not only to his soul but also to his body. However, there are other matters where a certain category of Yidden is harmed, while another category is not. For example, among us Ashkenazim, taking two wives is a violation of the cherem, whereas among Sephardim, it is permitted.

Likewise, there is a difference in the removal of a beard. Removing it with a ta'ar (a razor) is an issur d'oraisa for all Yidden equally, and one who does so, R"L, violates five lavin each time, as stated in the Gemara, Shulchan Aruch, and Poskim. However, removing it through a certain method involving a chemical (powder) or an electric shaver—for Chassidim, those who are connected to the talmidim of the Baal Shem Tov, this is an issur and causes harm to the soul and, consequently, to the body. Yet, it is not as great a damage as when one is, chas v'shalom, violating five lavin by using a razor or the like. But for Misnagdim and ordinary Yidden—those who do not know or have no connection to the p'sak din of the talmidim of the Baal Shem Tov—it is like the aforementioned analogy of the potato peels: it is not something for a person, and when the peels reach the stomach, one must rid oneself of them, but there is no danger in it (though if it reaches the lungs, one must be strict that it should not happen again, and seek to remove the damage caused by it).

Not knowing exactly about you, as to how much you are connected and belong to Chassidus, it is nevertheless a certain and clear matter that removing the beard with a razor or the like involves violating five lavin d'oraisa each time. And regarding an electric shaver or powder, it depends on how much one is connected to the Toras HaBaal Shem Tov. May Hashem Yisbarach help you to conduct yourself in the straight and correct path of Torah and mitzvos, which is for Yidden the truly happy path for happiness both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

With blessings,

The Secretary

## B’Shalah

B’Shalah

B”H, 7 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, R’ Avraham Zusya, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to the comments in your letter—which was sent without a date:

1) Regarding what you wrote concerning *Toras Chayim*, end of *Parshas Lech Lecha*, page 96, top of side b, that even the eating of Shabbos is from the *gashmius* of the body, stemming from the physical *taanug* of the body which is not refined and is a mixture of absolute good and evil from the *Eitz HaDaas Tov V’Ra*—which seemingly contradicts what is written in *Toras Chayim*, *Parshas Vayakhel*, pages 627 and 647, that the eating of Shabbos is not *megashem* (materializing), for it does not say "your Shabbos" [in a negative sense].

The explanation for this is that although the term *megashem* is used in both places, the distinction is that while there is no *ra* (evil) in the eating of Shabbos, it is still *megashem* in the sense of being permitted, and this is possible even with the eating of Shabbos. This is all the more so—*kal v’chomer*—from what is written in *Toras Chayim*, *Parshas Lech Lecha* (cited above), that even the **ahavah of the nefesh habah** that comes in a felt manner is drawn down from this, etc. See there.

Incidentally, these matters are discussed in *Toras Chayim*, beginning of *Parshas Chayei Sarah*, and in the *Siddur*, *Seder Seudas Shabbos* (Second Meal, *D’H Yigaleh Lan Ta’amei*), as well as in *Derech Mitzvosecha*, page 179 and there. **See there.**

2) Regarding what you wished to interpret in the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken in his *Shulchan Aruch*, section 186, paragraph 3, that Rabbeinu HaZaken holds that the *mitzvah* of *chinuch katan* (educating a minor) is incumbent upon the minor himself—this cannot be said, for the opinion of Rabbeinu HaZaken is the opposite, as he writes in his *Shulchan HaTahor*, beginning of section 39 (even though it is enclosed in parentheses).

3) The interpretation of Rabbeinu’s words in section 186 and the reason for them is that the matter of *chinuch katan* is not because of the circumstances of that specific time when he is a minor, but rather because of the results that will follow in his adulthood. Consequently, the *shiurim* (measurements) during the days of childhood do not change anything in this regard, and since the **results** in the days of adulthood do not change (whether he eats the full *shiur* or less than the *shiur*), there is only a *chad d’rabbanan* (one rabbinic requirement) even if he eats less than the *shiur*. This is unlike the case of *brachos*, *Hallel*, etc., which involve a *trei d’rabbanan* (two rabbinic requirements), as is understood. You should also look at what I wrote to you in my letter from the 27th of Shevat last year.

With blessing.

***

*[**An additional letter to him from the year 5713 — to which the preceding letter continues**]*

B”H, 27 Shevat, 5713
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, R’ Avraham Zusya, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your second letter: regarding the matter of sewing, I believe I at least hinted in my previous letter that, on the face of it, the matter of sewing consists of two details: a) connecting two separate things by means of a third thing; b) that the connecting thing must be by means of a sewing thread—meaning that it enters the hole with pressure, etc.

A connection can also be made by a metal wire, just as in the *Mishkan* one of the threads was made of gold (and with this, the doubt you raised in your letter regarding an iron wire is resolved). Therefore, one who glues papers or hides with a third substance—glue—is also liable.

With this, the distinction between connecting parts or "sewing" is also understood: sewing is by means of a third object, whereas the matter of connecting parts is not. This is also the basis for the *heter* (permission) when the holes are wide, fixed, and round, because then the thread does not enter with pressure. Based on the above, the *heter* mentioned simply regarding inserting hooks into loops is also understood. It is not comparable to what you brought in your letter from the *Korban Nethanel* regarding the prohibition to connect a garment with a safety pin, as that does not have the conditions for the *heter* mentioned above.

Based on the above, the *heter* for a zipper is also understood, since there is no third object connecting it. It falls under the law of a vessel with parts, where a vessel containing grooves may be connected on Shabbos because it is not an act of *uman* (craftsman) and because it is made to be opened and closed constantly (see *Taz* and *Magen Avraham*, section 313, paragraph 6, and in Rabbeinu’s *Shulchan Aruch* there, paragraph 21). Furthermore, even if there were a thread connecting the zipper, based on the above, it should be permitted, as it is similar to a round, sewn, wide hole where it is permitted to insert laces; the reason for this is that it is not like sewing, which is tight. And although a zipper is also tight, it is understood that the tightening of metal on metal is not comparable to fabric on fabric, similar to what is brought regarding *chatzitzah* (interposition) in *tevilah* (*Shabbos* 57a). And do not add to this.

**Note:** 1) Based on the above, it is also understood why we tighten a shoe with a shoelace that enters holes on both sides of the shoe; it is similar to the aforementioned laces, and this is done even if the metal circle surrounding the hole is missing, and no one objects or doubts this.

2) Regarding what was mentioned above concerning the *heter* to insert hooks into loops, it seemingly refers to hooks sewn on one side of the garment and loops sewn on the other side. It is not like the hooks and loops in the curtains of the *Mishkan*, where the hooks were a separate object, and based on the above, that is a *toldah* of *tofer* (sewing).

b) Regarding the *hemshech* (drawing down) through the actions of minors and *mitzvos asei* that are time-bound for women, which I wrote should be explained similarly to the *hemshech* of *mitzvos* that are *reshus* (optional): you object that according to this, in *Toras Chayim*, *D’H Moshe Yedaber*, item 4, it is explained that the *hemshech* of *Matan Torah* does not exclude anyone except a *nochri*. — The rule mentioned in many places is well known: "Should one go like a peddler and list everything in every place?" Therefore, I only brought the simplest thing, since all the details were brought elsewhere.

c) Regarding your objection from the fact that a minor who knows how to shake [the *lulav*] requires his father to buy him a *lulav*, etc.—which implies that through the minor’s shaking, the father has fulfilled the *mitzvah* of *chinuch*—if so, why would nothing be drawn down through his action? I do not understand what you are "squeezing" here. Since in these matters the minor is only the means through which the **father** fulfills his (the **father’s**) obligation—similar to the case of a minor’s *bris milah*—and it is not that the minor draws down **from his own side**, it is simple.

d) Regarding what you questioned from the Sages (*Shabbos* 149b): "Mine and yours, what is it? He said to him: The breath that has sin in it is not like the breath [that has no sin]..."—from which it is understood that he *is* performing the *hemshech*, only the difference is whether there is sin in it. I did not understand your question here either. It is obvious that the *hemshech* of women in taking a **lulav** is like the *hemshech* of men in the *mitzvah* of **lulav**, and the *hemshech* of women in the *mitzvah* of **tefillin**—like Michal the daughter of Shaul—is like the *hemshech* of men in the *mitzvah* of **tefillin**, and not in other *mitzvos*. Only, this draws down as a matter of *reshus* and that as a matter of obligation. Especially in this statement of the Sages, which speaks of the **superiority** of the Torah study of children **over** the study of adults, it is obvious that he should ask what "yours and mine" is.

e) Furthermore, in addition to all the above, the matter of Torah study for minors is distinct from other *mitzvos* that they perform, according to one interpretation of the *Tzemach Tzedek* in *Piskei Dinim, Chiddushim al HaRambam*, *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, law 1. He emphasizes there the language that a minor is obligated to study himself **when he recognizes**. See there. In truth, it is a great innovation that he writes there regarding this, that even for a minor there is an obligation **min haTorah**. This is unlike other *mitzvos*.

f) Regarding your doubt concerning the *mitzvah* of *chinuch*: Rabbeinu’s opinion is that it is *midrabbanan*, as he writes in *Hilchos Talmud Torah* at the beginning, and it is brought in the *Tzemach Tzedek* there (except for the *mitzvah* of *Talmud Torah*). This is also the case in his *Shulchan Aruch*, *Orach Chayim*, section 343. As for what he wrote in the introduction to *Chinuch Katan* that the *mitzvah* of *chinuch* is a *mitzvah asei*, this too apparently means a *mitzvah asei* *midrabbanan*.

g) Regarding a *mitzvah haba'ah b'aveirah* (a *mitzvah* performed through a sin), I pointed to what is written in *Tanya*, chapter 8: "And he also acted and did so, and read and prayed, etc."—meaning that the *mitzvah* was fulfilled, yet the vitality within it does not ascend, etc., as written there.

Regarding your objection as to how it is possible for the *mitzvah* to be fulfilled and yet be connected to the *Sitra Achra*—and not only that, but even to the *Gimel Kelipos HaTemei'os* entirely—see *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, chapter 4, end of section 3: "Then he extracts from the *kelipah* all the Torah and *mitzvos*, etc." (And based on this, what is written in *Tanya*, chapter 17, is also understood: "For in truth, it is impossible for the wicked to begin to serve G-d without doing *teshuvah*, etc." Seemingly, this is the opposite of what is seen with the eyes, but according to what is written in *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, it is understood, for then, on the contrary, they add strength to the *kelipah*).

h) Regarding your comment on the *Tzemach Tzedek*, *Chiddushei HaShas*, page 9b, where he writes that the language of the *Mishnah* requires study according to the Admur that the time for *Krias Shema* is considered from sunrise—although I have not heard an explicit instruction on this, in my opinion it is simple: one should not change the *psak* (ruling) because of a "requires study."

[Regarding] what is written in *Piskei Dinim* at the end, in the *Likutim*, regarding the *bracha* of *Shehecheyanu* on the *bracha* of the *Megillah* on Purim during the day, it states: "And even though it seems to me, etc., nevertheless, it is Torah, etc." See there in the notes printed in *Piskei Dinim*, published by Kehot, that on Purim of the year [5660] here in Lubavitch, the Admur ordered to recite *Shehecheyanu* in the morning before reading the *Megillah*.

With blessing.

## Beshalach

B.H., 9 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the fifth night of Chanukah, in which you write your thoughts regarding your standing in the avodah of Hashem. Surely you are familiar with the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the holy Rabbi Nachum of Chernobyl (also printed in the sicha of Pesach 5703), that one must frequently examine from which side a certain impulse or desire originates, for at first glance it is impossible to clarify whether it comes from the side of holiness or from the "other side." It is also a known saying of the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, that it is possible for the yetzer hara to dress itself in a "silk kapote." One of the fundamental tests for this is that if one sees that a certain impulse or desire brings about a weakening in one’s avodah, this is proof that it comes from the "left side."

So too in your specific case: as is apparent from your letter, the *cheshbon hanefesh* (soul-accounting) you write about is weakening your desire and vitality in your work—the work of Heaven, namely, the work of proper chinuch. Therefore, it is highly probable that this is one of the stratagems of the yetzer. This is in addition to what is explained in Tanya, that even if the sadness is regarding matters of Heaven, one must "take counsel with one's soul," etc. See there, Chapter 26, and in the *Kitzur Tanya*, from which it is also understood that it is possible for all the arguments and claims to be justified, yet one must distance oneself from them completely. Furthermore, regarding your own situation, from all the soul-accounting you describe, I still do not understand what the practical conclusion is, other than the sadness you write about. Consequently, this is not your concern; you should increase your strength in the chinuch of the sons and daughters of Israel—a chinuch that draws their hearts closer to their Father in Heaven. His reward is with Him, as stated in many places in the words of our Sages, that through this, Hashem will illuminate your eyes as well, to ascend the path that leads to Beis-El.

2) Regarding your question as to whether to attend your brother’s wedding: the general directive in matters such as these is that *through closeness one can accomplish more than through rejection and distance.* Although you do not write the details of the matters between you, the impression I have is that it is better for you to be present. Aside from the matter of *ahavas Yisrael* involved, surely you will be able to utilize this—whether on the spot or over time—to draw your brother and his wife closer to the ways of Yiddishkeit. May Hashem grant you success in this as well.

With blessings,
Waiting for good news.

B"H, 11 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn
