## 2540

B"H, 12 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn

Mrs. Rachel, may she live,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of Tuesday, in which you write that your children are in good health and are learning with *hasmadah*. May Hashem help that you and your husband, may they live, should have much *Yiddishe nachas* and *Chassidishe nachas* from them, and that you should receive this with good health, a joyful heart, and *parnassah*.

I was also pleased to learn that you are participating in a sisterhood, and I hope that you will work to improve the situation in *ruchniyus*. My hope is strengthened by reading your article, in which you write about "spiritual vitamins." This is one of the things that, in America, one must be vigilant about at every step, so that people do not think that with *tzedakah gashmius* one has already fulfilled all 613 *mitzvos*. For no matter how great the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah* may be—to the point that it is even referred to as "the *mitzvah* *stam*"—there are still 612 other *mitzvos* that one must fulfill. Among them are observing *Shabbos*, *kashrus*, *taharas hamishpachah*, and so on. No matter how much one repeats and speaks about this, it is still not enough, and there is always a great need to repeat it thoroughly—especially when one says this in English and with the appropriate explanations. May Hashem help you and grant you success in this as well.

With blessings,

[Signature]

## 2343

B"H, 14 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, a man of noble character, a branch of a thick-leaved tree, etc., R' Shneur Zalman, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure the news that the electrical lighting in Kfar Chabad has been set up in practice, and that you have already gathered by its light on the bright day of 19 Kislev. As I am informed, this was arranged thanks to your efforts and energy; may your strength be bolstered, and thank you, thank you.

It is an ancient Jewish custom to seek hints and guidance in everything that occurs, in accordance with the Mishnah’s teaching, "Who is wise? He who learns from every person," to which the Baal Shem Tov added the concept of learning from every event and every detail.

The light of our Alter Rebbe—*Shnei-Or* (Two Lights)—began to spread from the day of his liberation, 19 Kislev, without hindrances or delays, in a manner that reaches even simple people. This is the general point of the teachings of Chassidus: to draw down and connect the "depth of height" with the "depth of depth."

By way of a *melitzah* (a witty or metaphorical connection), the power of electricity is one of the hidden forces in nature. This power itself is not within the grasp of any of the five senses; its existence is known only through its actions and effects. Yet the light of this hidden power pushes away the darkness and illuminates the gloom of the night. This is, in the physical realm, akin to the aforementioned concept in the spiritual realm: that the hidden aspects of Torah, the secrets of secrets, are revealed through Chassidus and the Chassidic way of life, pushing away the darkness of materialism and illuminating the gloom of physicality.

And from the general to the particular:

One of the foundations of Judaism is the importance of the individual, in contrast to systems that mandate sacrificing the individual for the sake of the collective. This is also a concept from our Sages: "Whoever sustains one soul of Israel, it is as if he sustained an entire world," and there are many similar statements. This is in addition to the fact that every person possesses hidden powers, and at some point in time, one can become a "general" person. With this introduction, I take this opportunity to turn to you with a request on behalf of an individual, even though I am certain that even without this, you have done everything in your power—but "one only urges those who are already diligent."

To conclude with a good matter: these days, the Tanya was published here, its first printing in the "lower hemisphere" (since our Holy Land is above all lands, this hemisphere is the lower one). It is accompanied by indices, etc. I have instructed that a copy be sent to you in a separate package, and I am sure you will confirm its receipt.

With respect, appreciation, and a blessing for good health.

## B'shma

B'shma

B"H, 15 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein, which I will read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you write in your letter—that your heart is broken over your spiritual state because you see yourself in a state of "rising and falling"—you should study the *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe, the author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, which is printed at the end of the *Siddur Meah Shearim*, page 30a, beginning with the words, "To understand the advice offered..." Surely this *Siddur* can be found with one of *anash* in... You should also study the *Torah Or*, *Parshas Vayeishev*, in the discourse beginning with the words, "A song of ascents."

As for practical application, the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of his father, is well known: that any matter which distracts one from *Torah* and *avodah* certainly does not have a pure source. The *yetzer hara* sometimes dresses itself in a "silk *surtuk*." Since it appears from your letter that these thoughts are distracting you from proper Torah study and proper *tefillah*, there is doubt as to their origin, and consequently, you must reject them. The advice for this is also explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 26 and onwards. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings.

## B'shmo

B'shmo

B"H, 16 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Monday, and in accordance with your request, I hasten to reply, although I do not know what I have to add to what I told you explicitly when you were with me. I repeat once again: you are healthy, and your thoughts and *mrah shechorah* (melancholy) have no basis. In particular, since you went to the doctor and he told you the same, you see that the visit to the doctor was a waste, and it would have been better to give that money to *tzedakah*.

May *Hashem* help that, at the very least, from now on you should nullify all the aforementioned thoughts and strengthen yourself in learning *Torah* and fulfilling *mitzvos* with *simchah*.

Regarding what you write concerning *ta'anisim* (fasts), the letter of the *Baal Shem Tov* to his student, the *Baal HaToldos*, regarding this is well known, as is what *Rabbeinu HaZaken* writes at the beginning of *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*. In general, this is not a path for you. You must perform *hataras nedarim* (annulment of vows), since you previously conducted yourself this way without stating that it was *bli neder* (without a vow). For the days in this year and the coming year on which you held a fast (before performing *hataras nedarim* now), you should give *pidyon ta'anis* to *tzedakah* and add a *shiur*—an **additional** *shiur* in *Toras HaNigleh* and an additional *shiur* in *Toras HaChassidus*.

Regarding the business opportunity presented to you: if, as you write, it will not interfere with your work in *chinuch hakasher* (proper education), you may accept it. Presumably, you will set aside a *chumash* (one-fifth) of the additional income for *tzedakah*. It would be a fitting thing for that *tzedakah* to be for one of the funds established by my father-in-law, the *Rebbe*, *ztzukulleh"h nbg"m zi"e*.

With blessings for the *avodah* of *Hashem*, and specifically with *simchah*.

## 2,747

2,747

B"H, 17 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

I was pleased to receive the news that you participated in the gathering held by the Agudas N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in Paris and spoke words of inspiration before them, and as they write to me, your words had an impact on the listeners.

Certainly, for someone like yourself, it is unnecessary to elaborate on the benefit of such a thing, especially when it concerns a Chanukah gathering organized by women, upon whom the decree was directed—as the Rambam writes at the beginning of Hilchos Chanukah, and as is hinted at in the Gemara in the words of our Sages, "they, too, were part of that miracle."

If, in every generation, the woman was the "foundation of the home," and consequently, young women and girls needed to be prepared for this great role, then how much more so in this dark generation of ours, where the necessity for the aforementioned has increased many times over. This is especially true given that "winds" that are not favorable are blowing through the world, seeking to destroy and uproot our eternal structure to its very foundation. Surely, you will continue to exert effort in this direction in an appropriate manner, and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings.

## B'Simcha

B’Simcha

B”H, 17 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive the news from your mother, tichyeh, that a daughter has been born to your son. May Hashem Yisborach help the parents raise her in a good manner, in the Jewish way, in health and happiness.

It goes without saying that in these times, parents must speak with their children—even regarding matters that at one time were not considered questions at all. However, this only makes the obligation greater and more urgent.

I mean to say that one must influence children so that their home is conducted as a Jewish home should be: a kosher kitchen, observing Shabbos, observing Taharas HaMishpacha (mikveh), and so on. In most cases, this is not achieved all at once, but that should not deter parents from speaking about it repeatedly. Just as when one sees a child about to harm their body, one employs every means to prevent it, it is all the more understandable that when one sees a child about to harm themselves—both in body and in soul—one must speak repeatedly until one succeeds in influencing them.

And in order for this to be easier and more effective, it is almost always better to use the better way: not through fighting, but through requesting in an appropriate manner and providing the appropriate explanations. Above all, one should explain that by conducting oneself in the Jewish way, one is not doing a favor to the Ribono shel Olam; rather, if a Yid wants to have a good and happy life, they must conduct themselves in the way of Torah and Mitzvos.

As for the fact that one sees even those Yidden who are not observant living a "good day," there are two things to consider: Firstly, it is difficult to know what is happening in someone else’s life. People are ashamed to tell others about the bad things, especially when they know that they themselves are to blame due to their conduct against the Torah. Secondly, as the Torah tells us, Hashem Yisborach has much patience and wishes to give a Yid the maximum amount of time, in the hope that perhaps, in the end, they will grasp the truth and place themselves on the straight path. Therefore, it can sometimes take years until one sees the unfortunate outcome, chas v’shalom, of not conducting oneself according to the Torah. However, in order to ensure and prevent that unfortunate outcome, chas v’shalom, it is better to act now—even if one thinks that the unfortunate outcome, chas v’shalom, is years away.

I do not wish to be overly lengthy in this, so as not to cause you distress. I hope that the above will be sufficient for you to act with energy to influence your children in a way of kiruv, and in an appropriate manner, to bring them closer to Yiddishkeit. May Hashem Yisborach help you.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe,

Secretary

## 2,549

Consequently, you need only nullify the thought that if you were not to travel, these funds would remain in your pocket; this is not the case, for they were given from Above from the outset for this specific purpose...

With blessings.

## B'shana

B"H, 17 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Shlomo Shneur Zalman, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your prompt letter from Vayechi, and I thank you for the good news regarding the Melaveh Malkah farbrengens and the fixed times for study that you write about. It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the ruling of our Sages that we must increase in matters of holiness, and when one opens for Hashem an opening the size of a needle’s eye, He grants success as wide as the entrance to the Ulam.

2) Regarding what you wrote about the organization of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad, noting that there is already an organization of this nature that meets every Shabbos: It is obvious that it is not worth causing a division of hearts. On the other hand, one must not forgo the matter of disseminating the instructions of Chassidus, its ways, and its customs. There are two ways to approach this: If it is possible to transform the existing organization so that it also aligns with this goal, then that is best. If, however, this would cause machlokes or the like, then one should organize a group as mentioned that meets at times different from the existing organization’s meetings. The studies should also be in the nature of an enhancement and addition to the study already established in the existing organization, but not in the nature of competition (konkurentzia). Surely, a diplomatic way can be found for this.

3) I was pleased by what you wrote, that you have a fixed time for studying Chassidus with the avreich [name omitted]. You should certainly endeavor to draw more avreichim to such study, through the aforementioned avreich or by other appropriate means.

With blessing.

## 2552

B"H, 17 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter of 20/11, in which you write regarding the situation in your business and the health of your husband, *shichyeh*. In accordance with your request, I will mention you at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zi"a*, for an improvement in the aforementioned matters.

However, it surprises me that after you spoke with me several times with bitterness regarding a *shidduch* for your daughter, *tichyeh*, and viewed it pessimistically, now that Hashem Yisbarach has shown you miracles and she has made a good *shidduch*, you do not mention a word about it. This is despite the fact that this is a lifelong blessing for your daughter, and consequently, a blessing for you and your husband, *shichyu*. When one sees *chasadim* from Hashem Yisbarach that one did not expect at all, the first thing one must do is thank Hashem Yisbarach from the depths of one's heart for this, and only later complain about those matters which, for the time being, are not as one would wish.

It goes without saying that I do not mean to imply that the business should be slow, *chas v'chalilah*, etc. For Hashem Yisbarach wants to give a Yid everything they need, and not trade one thing for another. But after all is said and done, one must not overlook what Hashem Yisbarach does for a Yid. When one thanks Him for the miracles He has shown until now—with that gratitude being expressed through matters of Torah and *mitzvos*—that in itself draws down further blessings from Hashem Yisbarach.

May Hashem Yisbarach help you to share good news regarding yourself, your husband, and all your family.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe,

Secretary:

## B'shng

B'shng

B"H, 18 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 5th of Teves, in which you write regarding your state of health, which has caused you a sense of despondency.

You must distance yourself from this path. Hashem is the Healer of all flesh and performs wonders. Even though we do not know the intent of the Creator, and consequently the Yetzer Hara sometimes stirs up questions and thoughts that disturb a person’s spiritual health—and even their physical health—one must always know that this is nothing more than the machinations of the Yetzer. One must remain strong in trust in Hashem, that in due time He will send the necessary healing. Furthermore, until that healing arrives, you remain a part of the Ribono shel Olam’s world, and as such, you are His emissary to spread light in your surroundings by illuminating your own soul—both the nefesh elokis and the nefesh habahamis—with matters of Torah and mitzvos, and by illuminating your portion of the world by spreading the light of Torah and Yiddishkeit there. In order for all of this to be effective, the activity must be carried out with joy, as it is written, "Serve Hashem with joy." When you strengthen yourself in all the above, you will certainly be assisted from Above to bring this to fruition.

I trust that you have a fixed time for study in both the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, and that you also recite the daily portion of Tehillim (as divided for the days of the month) each day after davening Shacharis. It would also be excellent if, every Monday and Thursday before davening, you were to set aside a few coins for the tzedakah of Bikkur Cholim.

With blessings for a complete and speedy recovery, and awaiting good tidings.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary:

## 2554

B"H, 18 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual engaged in communal needs, R' Dovid, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

3) Regarding your request: When I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention [the name of the person] for a speedy recovery. You should certainly take the opportunity to clarify whether he was born in purity. This is similar to when one comes to a lawyer or a doctor; one must describe the situation exactly as it is, for otherwise, it is a detriment to the one asking and also contrary to reason. The same applies in this case. You should also explain to the child’s parents that my intent in the aforementioned question is, G-d forbid, not at all to arouse judgment, but rather that the remedies must be appropriate to the situation and the causes that led to such a state. This is also explained in the science of medicine: a true physician is one who heals not the results, but the causes. Healing the results alone is merely a temporary matter, since the cause remains as it was before. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

4) I was very pleased to hear that when you meet with our fellow Jews, you arouse them regarding the rock from which they were hewn and their source. I was even more pleased that you are shown tangibly that your words are having an effect—something not everyone is privileged to see, the fruits of their labor, on the spot or at least within a short time. This phenomenon itself is proof that not only is your intent desirable, but your actions are also desirable, and consequently, you are being assisted from Above and granted additional strength to increase these activities.

5) And last but not least, I see that you have reached the age of sixty and have celebrated this milestone, and that your professional colleagues also recognize your worth and your activities. May it be the will of Hashem that for many more years you will draw the hearts of the sons and daughters of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven, and may you do so in good health and with peace of mind...

With blessings for long life and good years—and as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, "good" with all its interpretations.

Enclosed is a copy of the maamar and the general letter that I published in connection with the auspicious day of the Festival of Liberation, 19 Kislev, the content of which is relevant for the entire year. I am sure it will interest you and also provide you with assistance in your aforementioned work.

I was pleased to hear that you are printing a collection of the Sages' sayings. You should certainly also add to them appropriate collections regarding spiritual medicine—that is, the healing of the soul. As explained in the Rambam’s *Shemonah Perakim*, there is an equivalence between this and the healing of the body. Indeed, even the physicians of our most recent generation are giving increasing importance to the science of the soul and its characteristics in order for a person to be healthy in body.

Regarding sources and collections of the Sages on medicine in the Shas: I recall seeing a special book of such collections a few years ago; I believe the author’s name is Heilpern. It will also surely interest you to see the book *HaTalmud U'Mad'ei HaTevel* by Rabbi Kamelhar—the latter is regarding all the sciences. Both authors appear to be G-d-fearing.

## B'shana

B'shana

B"H, 19 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was saddened to hear the news of the passing of your father, the G-d-fearing, upright, and distinguished [name omitted], of blessed memory. May his soul be bound in the bond of life.

May the Omnipresent console you among the other mourners of Tzion and Yerushalayim.

And may it be the will of Hashem that from here on out you know no further sorrow or distress, G-d forbid, and that you find only goodness all the days of your life.

Since your father, of blessed memory, was among those connected to Lubavitch and davened according to the Nusach Ari, and it is well known that the greatest satisfaction for the departed is when their affairs have continuity after them—especially when "a son is the leg of his father"—it would be most appropriate for you to continue as much as possible in the aforementioned, both in davening according to Nusach Ari and, even more so, in activities in that direction. This will bring satisfaction to the soul of the departed, and it is in line with the words of our Sages, "Just as his seed is alive, so too is he alive," through which one nullifies even that which the eulogizers have eulogized, the embalmers have embalmed, and the gravediggers have buried (Taanis 5b).

With blessings,

P.S.
You are surely aware of the responsa regarding changing the nusach: that under certain conditions one may change to Nusach Ari, but it is extremely difficult according to "custom" to change from Nusach Ari to another nusach. This is noted in the responsa of the Maharshdam, Orach Chaim, siman 35; Divrei Chaim, part 2, siman 8 (which contains responses to what is written in the responsa of the Chasam Sofer, Orach Chaim, siman 15-16); responsa Beis HaYotzer, siman 8 (which reconciles the words of the Divrei Chaim with the critiques of the Maharim Shik, Orach Chaim, siman 43); responsa Minchas Elazar, part 1, siman 11; Shirei HaMincha there, part 2, 3; and Pri HaSadeh, part 2.

#### ***B'shana***

**Changing the Nusach:** See also Likutei Sichos, Vol. 14, p. 226; Vol. 17, p. 455; Kovetz Yagdil Torah (N.Y.), Issue 52, siman 32, 39-40.

## 2557

B"H, 21 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It is surprising that, contrary to their custom until now, I have not received from you information regarding the study schedule for this new year, the lists of students' names, etc., etc. It is self-understood that all of this is relevant and important for several reasons. It is also understood that even when you do not receive a response from here, we are at least doing what is possible here regarding the practical matters, even if we do not inform you of them. This is not the case, however, when we receive no information from you, and this is in addition to the necessity of maintaining a connection in general, beyond the material benefit therein.

I am certain that you will fulfill all of the above at the earliest opportunity and with the appropriate level of detail. Thank you in advance.

2) In connection with the upcoming Yahrtzeit and Hillula of 10 Shevat, you should certainly consult among yourselves, as well as with other appropriate members of anash, on how to arrange the aforementioned in your holy institution in a manner appropriate for the students of each grade, according to its level. The necessity of this—both in the higher grades and in the lower ones—requires no explanation. In accordance with the will of the master of the Hillula, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, to connect every matter with actual practical action, you should take this into account in your planning. You should inspire the students, as well as the members of the administration, not only with general concepts, but also with specific details. Even though the details in such matters do not exhaust the entire whole—and furthermore, there is also the aspect of the whole that transcends the details, as is explained in Chassidus in many places—nevertheless, those details that can be specified should not be neglected. It is to be hoped that this, too, will eventually help to draw down the other details of the whole, and even that which exists in the whole that transcends the details, since the drawing down into actual practice will have begun immediately.

3) Enclosed is a check for the expenses related to organizing all of the above.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and awaiting good news.

## 258

258

B"H, 21 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Daled Vayechi. I am very displeased with what you write regarding your state of *atzvus* (sadness). Although you bring an example of other Jews who are also in *atzvus*, one should generally only emulate others in good matters, not in things that cause damage to many areas. Most importantly, *atzvus* hinders one from fulfilling the *shlichus* of the *Ribono shel Olam* that **everyone** has in this *olam hazeh hagashmi v'hachomri*. As the Alter Rebbe writes in his *sefer Tanya Hakadosh*, beginning of Chapter 26, that when one is "in a state of laziness and heaviness," he is easily defeated and will fall, even if he is stronger than his peer—and the same applies to the victory over the *yetzer* etc. It is superfluous to elaborate on this, as one sees it proven daily.

The second point I must take issue with in your letter is this: following the concept brought in *Chassidus*, we see tangibly that *machshavos zaros* (alien thoughts) only intrude during *davening*—when one suddenly begins thinking about business or family matters, etc.—whereas when one is occupied with business matters, no other thoughts enter his mind, such as thoughts about *davening* or family matters, etc.

So too in your case: when one is in *atzvus*, does it not hinder—not only according to our Sages regarding the *hashraas hashechinah*—but does it not also weaken one's energy in business matters, etc.? Primarily, one sees that this is [missing text] one of the stratagems of the *yetzer* who does not want to allow a person to conduct himself according to the *ratzon haborei*.

I am certain that you will not take offense at me for writing the above, and I am also certain that no further convincing is necessary. May the *Hashem Yisbarach* help you and me to hear good and happy tidings from one another.

With blessings and regards to those you influence and your surroundings—for ultimately, the entire environment should be *mushpa* (influenced), since one is not carrying out a personal agenda, but rather [working] to make things clearer and more refined, and *bederech mimila*, to bring them closer to *Torah* and *mitzvos* and *kedusha* in general. May the *Hashem Yisbarach* grant you success.

With blessings.

P.S.

In continuation of the above, I have requested that they send you the *Tanya* which was printed for the first time in America. Surely this will give you strength in your own learning and also in learning with others, at which time the *Hashem Yisbarach* fulfills His promise that "Hashem illuminates the eyes of them both," as the Alter Rebbe writes in his introduction to his *sefer Tanya Hakadosh*.

## B'shnat

B'shnat

B"H, 21 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Wednesday, which was received on Motzaei Shabbos, I am reiterating what I conveyed to your brother-in-law, may he live and be well, orally: as is known, in cases such as these, one first attempts to flush out what is in the kidneys by increasing fluid intake in general, and the consumption of appropriate liquids in particular. From the fact that you do not mention this in your letter, it seems that this has not yet been done, which is seemingly strange. It is possible that even now you could still attempt this, for to my knowledge, it is only after trying the aforementioned that one considers removing what is in the kidneys by means of the appropriate instrument. May the Ribono shel Olam send him a complete and speedy recovery, so that he may be able to engage in the study of the revealed Torah and the study of Chassidus with proper health and peace of mind.

Awaiting good news.

## 260

B"H, Eve of 24 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, a man of fine character, involved in communal needs, a man of energy and many accomplishments, a man of distinction, a descendant of holy lineage, etc., etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchak Meir, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I learned you have reached the age of sixty, may you have long days and good years. Surely, as our Sages of blessed memory say, one should make a festive day for the Sages, and I hereby join in this, albeit from a distance.

It is well known what is brought in the Rishonim (see Midrash Shmuel there) regarding the various versions in the Mishnah at the end of the fifth chapter of Avos: "At sixty, for old age," "At sixty, for understanding," "At sixty, for wisdom." In the writings of the Arizal (who says "At fifty, for old age"), it is "At sixty, for gray hair" (Me'orei Ohr, end of letter 7, based on what is written in Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 21, 57a, and in Shaar HaMitzvos, Parshas Kedoshim). May it be the will of Hashem that all of these be granted to you, and that these matters be fulfilled in a beautiful manner, in accordance with what is explained in Likutei Torah by our Alter Rebbe, Shir HaShirim, page 11, beginning of the first column, and there.

May the Almighty grant you the merit and success to utilize your talents—both your own and those inherited from your ancestors—to increase Torah and make it glorious, through greatness in Talmud and greatness in action, in the spirit of the elders of Israel, and in accordance with the light of the teachings of Chassidus.

With respect and blessings.

#### ***260***

**Rabbi Yitzchak Meir:** Levin. Additional letters to him - above, Vol. 4, 132; 145; 198.

## 2361

B"H, 24 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of Rosh Chodesh Teves, in which you write regarding your son, the *avreich*, the G-d-fearing, Torah-studying, and refined individual, [Name], *shiya*, who is currently in [Location] and is engaged in *avodas hakodesh*, and thank G-d it is proceeding with great success. However, you are concerned about two matters:

1) What will be with his own personal Torah study.
2) Regarding a *shidduch*.

It is certainly superfluous to remind you that the world is directed by Hashem, and when one fulfills His will, it is certain that not only will this cause no harm, but on the contrary, it must bring a great reward, both in *gashmius* and in *ruchnius*.

This is especially true in the matter of performing *tzedakah* with Jewish children—*ruchnius* *tzedakah*—to bring them closer to *Yiddishkeit*. It is well known in this regard the statement of our *Rabbeinu HaZakein*, the *Baal HaTanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, that this brings success in understanding the holy Torah a thousand times over. *Rabbeinu HaZakein* was generally very precise in his words, and when he writes "a thousand times over," it is not 999, but a full thousand. Beyond what is written in the holy *sefarim*, based on what I see in the case of your son, from his being in [Location], this is indeed the case.

If you encounter the current generation, even from observant homes, you certainly know the *nisyonos* and confusions they face. When Hashem helps one of them to stand with spiritual strength on his own two feet and with a living *neshamah*, and he feels that he is doing something that brings benefit to the *klal* and benefit to himself, this is one of the greatest blessings and the greatest reward that Hashem gives in these turbulent times to the rising generation.

Regarding the other question, that a *shidduch* might come about for him there with a girl from a Sephardic family: as far as I know, in recent times many *shidduchim* have been concluded between Ashkenazim and Sephardim, and both sides are satisfied. This is because they are not the same Ashkenazim and not the same Sephardim as in the past; today, both have become much closer to one another. The very fact that she sees that your son wears a beard, knows that he is occupied with *chinuch*, and agrees to all of this—this alone points to the inner connection and inner feeling she has for him, and that is one of the primary things in the life together of two people.

With blessings,

## 2,362

B"H, 25 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the congregants of the Chevra Liadi Nusach Ari synagogue in Brooklyn, N.Y., and at their head, the Chairman, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Eliyahu Moshe, Shochet, may he live and be well.

Peace and Blessing!

I was pleased to receive regards from you, and although there were no details, I hope that you are maintaining not only the order of davening but also the order of communal learning. In our current times, a synagogue must also be a beis medrash. According to the Gemara, a synagogue is called a *mikdash me'at* (a miniature sanctuary); just as light went forth from the Beis Hamikdash to the entire world, so too must a synagogue and beis medrash serve as a central point from which Yiddishkeit spreads throughout the entire surrounding area, with the proper warmth and mesiras nefesh.

In accordance with the demands of our time, one must not wait until someone else comes to shul to then hand them a Siddur, a Tehillim, or another sefer. Rather, one must seek ways to enter that person's home and make them want to come to shul to daven and to learn. From the shul, they should take with them an increase in *ner mitzvah v'torah ohr*—the light of Torah—which is the teachings of Chassidus.

For this, our holy Nesi'im have practiced mesiras nefesh, from the times of Liozna, Liadi, and Lubavitch, and in the other places, until my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. And we all have a promise from the Alter Rebbe—whose Chag HaGeulah we celebrated not long ago, and whose yom hilula, 24 Teves, was yesterday—that when one exerts effort in this, one will certainly be successful.

With blessings to all the congregants and their families, may they live, each and every one, for whatever they need in both material and spiritual matters.

***

**Promise:** See below, Letter 2,395, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 2,363

B"H, 25 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your question about copying [the manuscript]... It is truly puzzling that members of Anash, may they live, who when they were in their former country—where every matter of Torah and mitzvos was bound up with actual mesiras nefesh and dangers, Heaven forbid—did not retreat, and on the contrary, advanced with the appropriate vigor; yet now, when they have come to a place where there are no concealments, etc., and to a certain extent it can even be said that people demand and praise work in Torah and mitzvos (even if they do not yet assist as they should), each person is searching with the greatest vigor for a situation where he can sit under his own private vine and his own private fig tree, without concerning himself with all the [communal] matters...

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 2,364

B"H, 25 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...2) It is self-understood that what we have discussed several times—that you are a healthy person, but must preserve your physical health by maintaining a regular schedule of eating, drinking, and rest, etc.—remains in full force.

It is unnecessary to elaborate at length on how the lack of order, especially for those who have taken upon themselves *mleches shamayim* (the work of Heaven), is one of the *yetzer’s* tactics, and with great cunning at that. For, in most cases, they cloak this in arguments of *yiras shamayim*, claiming that it pertains to the *avodah* of *tefillah* and the study of *Chassidus*, etc. However, since our *Nesi’im*, in their written and oral teachings, have already warned against this—and have cautioned against it in every place and inquiry by negating this approach—if one truly desires to, one can implement this in life without any difficulties. Although, of course, it is hard to change even a second nature that has been formed by the habit of disorder over a long period of time, it is possible.

3) In a similar vein to the above is what we discussed regarding the absolute necessity of introducing order into your *avodah b’kodesh* and communal affairs.

Since it is impossible for one person to manage many different matters in all their details while also ensuring that order prevails in them, it is my opinion that you must immediately—before things become further complicated (*farplantaren*)—delegate a significant portion of the aforementioned work to suitable people. Your role should be only general oversight and receiving reports from time to time. You will certainly inform me how you have arranged all of this, and for the reasons mentioned above, the sooner this is done, the better.

With blessings for success in your *avodah b’kodesh* with proper health and an abundance of *nachas chassidishi* from yourself and from all your family members, may they live.

## 2367

B"H, 26 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., R' Meir, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

I was alarmed to receive your letter dated Tuesday, 2364, regarding fasting on Shabbos for a Yahrtzeit. There are several opinions on this matter, but according to all authorities, one does not fast [on Shabbos]. In my opinion, it is better to move the fast to Friday, and if that is not possible, to delay it until Sunday, or not to fast at all. You should examine the opinions on this in Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, 568, section 9, and in the Acharonim there: Turei Zahav, Siman 429, subsection 3; in our Rebbe’s Shulchan Aruch, section 9; in the books cited in Sdei Chemed, Asifat Dinim, Ma’areches Aveilus, subsection 96; and in the book Kol Bo by Rabbi Grunwald, page 390. In my opinion, even the [procedure of] *hataras nedarim* is not applicable here. In any event, do not fast on Shabbos Kodesh.

With blessings,

#### ***2367***

**R' Meir:** Labkowski.

## 270

B"H, 28 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Shaul Dov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

First and foremost, I hereby express my thanks for the booklets of Chassidus that you sent me. Thank you very much for the past, and I also request for the future, should it be in your power to honor me with these excellent materials. Especially since, in the final analysis, I make use of what I receive, including for matters that are being printed, and consequently, this is also a matter of *zchus harabim*.

2) In a separate package, I have sent you the *Tanya* that was published here, which includes an index of topics, etc., at the end. Since I have been told from several sources that you possess *mesoras chassidim*—as well as your own insights—regarding the *Tanya*, I would be most grateful if you would have your assistants transcribe all of the above. For even though you already have the notes, etc., surely over time there will be further additions and supplements, etc. It goes without saying that if you know the name of the person who related or explained these traditions, it is well known how meticulous my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, was that things should be reported with all their details. This applies here as well, even in cases where there is uncertainty regarding the tradition...

With respect and blessing.

## 271

B"H, 28 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letters, first regarding the improper thought [you had], and subsequently regarding your good resolution to continue learning at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim. Surely, Hashem will grant you success.

Regarding what you write—that it occurred to you that in order to be able to learn, the way forward is to travel to the United States to study in the Yeshiva here: the one who hinders learning is the *yetzer hara* within a person. Consequently, I do not know what benefit there would be in traveling here if you take the *yetzer hara* with you. Furthermore, matters of *pizur hanefesh* (distraction of the soul) are more prevalent in the United States than in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, and the *nisyonos* here are no less significant than they are there.

Therefore, my opinion is that you should increase your strength in the study of *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*. You should also find some way to perform *chessed* with some of your peers, to draw their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven. This spiritual *tzedakah* refines the mind and heart a thousand times over, as per the language of our holy Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, in the beginning of *Torah Or*.

It is understood that this must be done with the consent of your *mashpia* and your *rosh yeshiva*, and in a manner that will not disrupt your schedule in the Yeshiva. If you hold to this path with a firm resolve—a resolve that it cannot be otherwise—and this resolution is genuine, as it is written, "that no one be banished from Him," then you will surely succeed.

With blessings for Torah study with *yiras shamayim*.

## 2772

B"H, 28 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 22 Kislev, in which you describe the sequence of events regarding your position at... and the fact that you are now left without a position.

Life does not always proceed on a smooth path. Since it is within the will and capacity of a person to ascend, this very fact creates the possibility for descent as well. One must not become discouraged or lose heart, chas v'shalom, when experiencing a descent—especially when the descent concerns only material and personal matters, and is a situation beyond one’s control.

On the contrary, a descent should serve to awaken more internal and profound powers of emunah and bitachon, the external manifestation of which is courage of spirit and a lack of agitation over an unpleasant occurrence—especially when it is only for a very short time.

I have written to the activists in the field of chinuch, and it is my hope that within a short time they will be able to arrange your situation as well, provided, of course, that you also cooperate with them.

With blessings for success in the holy work of proper chinuch.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

28 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi, Chassid, G-d-fearing man, involved in communal affairs, etc., Rabbi Sh. Y. [Zevin] – may he live and be well.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have just received your letter of 21 Teves. Regarding what you wrote concerning the tenth volume of the *Sdei Chemed*, it has been some time since I wrote to the G-d-fearing man, Rabbi Y. [Motkin] – may he live and be well – instructing him to deliver it to you. It is surprising that he has not yet fulfilled this. If, by the time you receive this letter, it has still not reached you, please let me know and it will be sent from here.

2) Furthermore, a separate package was sent to you containing the *Tehillim* with the *Yehallel Ohr* commentary, and the *Tanya* that was published here in connection with the *Chag HaGeulah*, 19 Kislev. This is the first time it has been printed in the United States, etc., as I wrote in my previous letter. I am certain it has reached you.

3) I am writing now because I am sure you have heard about the public outcry regarding the issue of *Sherut Leumi* (National Service) abroad in general, and in the United States and New York in particular. Now that registration for *Sherut Leumi* has already begun, all circles have surely realized that it only affects a very limited number of people. The religious girls of Meah Shearim and the like will be exempted; on the other hand, there are those whom they wish to draft; and those in the middle are few in number—especially since many are already working in appropriate offices, and others are exempt for health reasons and the like. Since, on the face of it, the time has passed for the intoxication of "victory" in this matter—the desire to show that they are not impressed by any pressure, especially pressure coming from religious circles—now is the opportune time to endeavor to bury this matter quietly and discreetly, through a policy of "sit and do nothing," which is also a dignified approach.

In addition to all the above, according to information I have from behind the scenes, even in Mapai circles and the like, they have lost their appetite for this whole issue. Especially now that they have already demonstrated that they have the upper hand, if they could find a dignified way out, they would want to be rid of this entire mess and would grasp at the opportunity.

In accordance with all the above, now is the opportune time to influence him to issue a clear ruling for the cancellation of *Sherut Leumi*. After all, it is certainly no less severe than the matter of "speaking with her behind the fence," or the court "beating and punishing" as an emergency measure, etc.

This is especially true since many families and circles perceive the entire matter as an accessory to *gilui arayos* (forbidden sexual relations). Even if this is due to propaganda from certain circles, the fact remains that the matter has been accepted in—at times—broad circles, both of Jews and non-Jews, as a war against religion in general and a matter of *gilui arayos* in particular. If so, for them, it is a matter of being forced to abandon their religion, and they are obligated to act accordingly.

Since Rabbi Shimshon Raphael Weiss – a man of great energy, etc., whom you surely heard about during your visit to Eretz Yisrael last year, and who is the Executive Director of "Young Israel" here and has accomplished great things in matters of *yiras shamayim* with great energy despite opposition from various sides – is traveling to Eretz Yisrael these days, I have asked him to visit you on my behalf. After he conveys to you his own firsthand knowledge regarding the public outcry that the issue of *Sherut Leumi* has caused here—and that they will undoubtedly lose out on various fundraising campaigns and in the attitude toward the settlement of Eretz Yisrael, etc.—he will convey my perspective and request regarding the current situation concerning *Sherut Leumi*. Since, according to the aforementioned information from behind the scenes, even those on the left are looking for a dignified way to retract, now is the opportune time for them to take the initiative, and a beginning in this would be a clear instruction for the cancellation of the aforementioned. I have asked Rabbi Weiss to visit you first and ask that you arrange an interview for him with [the relevant official] specifically for this matter. It would be best if you were also present at this interview, and utilize your influence and standing with him to bring the matter to a conclusion as soon as possible, as any delay in this is liable to cause damage in several respects.

5) It is surely unnecessary to remind you that if you have any comments or insights regarding the additions to the *Tanya*, please let me know openly, and I thank you in advance.

6) I was pleased to hear that they honored you and had you give a *Gemara* *shiur* over the radio. (This will surely not interfere with your most necessary work on the *Talmudic Encyclopedia*, which, in your capacity, is a *mitzvah* that cannot be performed by others, and therefore one even interrupts Torah study for it.) I am sure that from time to time you will find the opportunity to season the *shiurim* with matters of *yiras shamayim* and practical *mitzvos*, for this is the whole of man, as it is written: "And He commanded us to do all these... to fear Hashem our G-d." May Hashem grant you success in spreading the light of Torah in places near and far, and may you see good fruit from your labor for long, good, and fruitful years.

With respect and blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. I have asked Rabbi Weiss that if he hears from you that it would be beneficial, he should also meet with [another official] and speak with him about the above on my behalf; he has my permission to do so. In that case, he should turn to Rabbi Sh. D. Zislin to arrange the interview with [that official] and to find the appropriate ways to influence him. I also told Rabbi Weiss that if he hears from you that it is worthwhile for him to meet with [a third official], he should endeavor to arrange that interview as well. If you are able to assist in this, you will surely do so, and may it be that through you and through him, the Name of the Holy One will be exalted.

## 2744

B"H, 29 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live.

Peace and Blessing!

For the sake of order, I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 5th and 14th of Tishrei, the 17th and 19th of Cheshvan, and the 17th of Kislev, which were received with a delay. It is surprising that you are so sparing with your correspondence, as the interval between one letter and the next is extremely long.

2) I am surprised to note in your letters a feeling of discouragement regarding the difficulties you encounter in your avodah. This has been the state of affairs since the destruction of the Beis Hamikdash: every matter of holiness is subject to various concealments and hiddenness, especially regarding Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. As the Ramban, of blessed memory, writes in his letter from Eretz Yisrael, "Everything that is holier than its counterpart is more desolate than its counterpart." On the contrary, this knowledge demands the awakening of inner and profound powers, for surely this is nothing other than Hashem testing [menaseh] you, to know [your hearts]. As explained in Likutei Torah, the word *menaseh* also implies the language of a *nes* (a banner/elevation), and through this, the true Da'as—the higher Da'as—is drawn down.

3) I am certain that you are continuing with vigor in your field of avodah to influence the youth who are, for the time being, not Chabad. It goes without saying that this applies not only to those from the lineage of anash, but even to those who are not from that lineage. For the saying of the Alter Rebbe is well known: that Chassidus is a matter for all of Klal Yisrael, and not merely the concern of a single sect. A Tzaddik decrees and the Ribono shel Olam fulfills, and fortunate is everyone who participates in this activity. Through this, you also hasten the true and complete Geulah, when the wellsprings will spread outward, our righteous Moshiach will come, and he will redeem us from all concealments and hiddenness, and will repair the world under the sovereignty of the Almighty. For all the children of Yisrael, the light of Hashem will shine, and they will delight in the pleasantness of Hashem, as explained in the discourses for the festival of Pesach—printed in Sefer HaMaamarim 5709—regarding the interpretation of "the pleasantness of Hashem."

4) I am sure you will write of your positive activities on Yud-Tes Kislev and Yud Shevat, and the days in between.

If any yeshivah wishes to have Kehot books sent for their library, they should apply directly here to the administration of Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch.

Enclosed is some script for the aforementioned expenses.

With blessings for success in your holy avodah, and awaiting good tidings.

## In the Hour

B"H, 29 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, R' Yissachar Dov, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

It is surprising that since the receipt of your letter from the 3rd of Teves, no news has arrived from you regarding general matters as you promised in that letter. Surely this is a sign that all is well; nevertheless, it is known that the ruling of our Sages (Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah, at the beginning) is that one does not rely on a presumption where it is possible to verify...

Your question was conveyed to me regarding whether to study Tanya with the older students. It is known that this was done according to the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, when he was in Riga, with a number of the daughters of Anash, and the esteemed R' Mordechai Cheifetz, may his blood be avenged, studied with them. There also exists a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, encouraging and strengthening him in this. However, it is also understood that the study with them need not necessarily be in order; one should begin with the easier and more *avodah*-oriented sections. For even according to Shulchan Aruch, a woman is obligated to study this part of Torah, since she is obligated in all the negative commandments and all the positive commandments that are not time-bound. Consequently, this includes the six constant mitzvos: belief in Hashem, not to believe in any other, to unify Him, to love Him, to fear Him, not to stray after the thoughts of the heart and the sight of the eyes—as they are enumerated in the introduction to Sefer HaChinuch. One arrives at all of this through knowing the concepts explained in Chassidus.

With blessings for success in your holy work and in your personal affairs.

[The Rebbe]

P.S.
Enclosed is a copy of a general letter that was published in connection with the bright day, the festival of our redemption and the liberation of our souls, the 19th of Kislev that just passed, the content of which is relevant for the entire year. You should explain its content to the older students with appropriate clarity.

B'H, 29 Teves, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

...Although you do not mention this in your letter, since the first building in the orchard is already connected to the electric company, surely this will extend to the other buildings as well.

5) I was very pleased that there are already veteran Yemenite students serving as *madrichim* and even teachers. Depending on the talents of each one, it is possible—and perhaps worthwhile, even though he is already a teacher—that he should continue to improve his own studies by also being a student in one of the higher classes, or in a special class for them. However, it is understood that this must be done in a way that they do not view it as a diminution of their stature. I rely on your insight. In general, the time has come when the *mashpi'im* of all types, as well as those in the other institutions of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), should be from among the graduates of our own institutions, or at the very least from *anash*. Their *mesiras nefesh* is of a different order. Since "one who has bread in his basket" is not deterred by the surrounding environment, they will not oppose what is required of them, knowing that, in the end, they will act in accordance with the requirement, and therefore, it is not worth fighting over this.

6) It is somewhat surprising, as your good custom at the beginning of every *zman* was to notify me of the list of new students, including their records and photographs, as well as a list of students leaving, along with the reason for their departure from the institution. At this time, I have not yet received any information regarding this.

7) In accordance with the saying of our Sages, "At the time of gathering..."—given the shortage of students who are without partisan or other affiliations—it is worthwhile to be lenient and not be overly exacting in the acceptance of new students. Especially since *Aliyas HaNoar* in general is shrinking, it is understood that one must take into account not to cause damage to the students already in the Yeshiva, but surely a way can be found to ensure both this and that.

8) Regarding new students—I have already expressed my opinion long ago that this is very, very necessary. Often in such matters, it is worthwhile to begin the thing itself, which subsequently brings the means, rather than the opposite—waiting at the beginning until the means are available. As for connecting this to the question of the plot of land where there are olive trees that bear fruit, I am not comfortable intervening in this question, especially since, as is apparent from your letter, there is another drawback: it is not in your orchard, and consequently, it is at a distance from the main buildings. This is the opposite of the goal to concentrate the Yeshiva’s affairs in one location, which is a great advantage in both spiritual and even material terms. It is understood that if it is impossible otherwise, and you receive a ruling from those in authority that there is no concern at all regarding the matter of the olive trees, then I will not intervene.

9) Regarding what you wrote in your letter... although the great virtue of those who are insulted but do not insult is known from our Sages, I do not know if this also applies when the one being insulted is a public institution, and especially a large and spiritual movement. It is surprising that precisely in matters such as these, you are so scrupulous about humility...

10) Regarding what you wrote in the letter of 9 Kislev about a campaign for the vocational school here, it is in contradiction to the preparation for the annual Tomchei Temimim dinner here, which will take place in another month. Also, regarding the trip to Australia—seemingly, according to the information received from there, the material situation there is not at all suitable for this. Especially since, according to the letter from the administration of our Yeshiva there, they are currently struggling hard to collect the funds needed for the Yeshiva building there, and they should have spoken directly with *anash* in Australia.

11) It is surely unnecessary to remind you that it is necessary to find ways not to sever the connection with the students who have left your Yeshiva for any reason whatsoever.

12) It is surprising that since you wrote that the material for the *Torah* booklet was already ready, I have heard nothing about it since. It would be appropriate to print it for 10 Shevat, the coming *yom tov* (naturally, if there are no special reasons related to your location and time that contradict this). At that time, you should also print in the booklet some of my letters regarding the *histalkus* and the *yahrzeit* and its order, which were printed at various times in the introductions to the *kuntreisim*. Perhaps you should also include a copy of my general letter from 19 Kislev of this year, which surely is already in your possession.

13) The sending of my letter was delayed, and in the meantime, your letters from 12, 14, 15, 16, 19, and 25 Teves were received, as well as the plans for the vocational school. I have come to add to the above:

14) The curriculum for the vocational school, etc., will follow your proposal in detail. It is understood that the beginning of the day must be dedicated to *tefillah* and *limudei kodesh*. The age of the students, at least for the majority, should correspond to the age of those supported by *Aliyas HaNoar*.

15) My intention in training *madrichim* from among the Yemenites was not only *madrichim* for Tomchei Temimim of Lod, but also for the *Reshet*, the *Kfar*, etc.

16) Regarding the students from the *Reshet*, you should surely be lenient in the conditions for their acceptance into your Yeshiva, of course.

17) It is certainly unnecessary to remind you that you must accustom the Yemenite students to our *seder* of study, and not the other way around, even when their numbers increase...

With a blessing for success in your holy work, I await good news.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2,757

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar, disseminator of Torah in public, a man of energy, etc., Rabbi Pinchas Mordechai, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Following our conversation regarding the weekly *daf* shiur via radio and the *Melaveh Malkah* meal to strengthen this initiative, which will take place shortly,

I hereby reiterate my blessing that you should succeed in establishing this shiur, strengthening it, and expanding it, both in quantity and in quality.

If regarding several manifest things in creation, our Sages of blessed memory said that they were created for the sake of the Holy One, Blessed be He’s Holy Temple, and only by virtue of this does the world also use them (*Shemos Rabbah* 52:5),

Then all the more so regarding a hidden and wondrous power in nature, which finds its rectification only by becoming a medium, a vessel, and a sanctuary for Him, may He be blessed. And from the day the Holy Temple was destroyed, the Holy One, Blessed be He, has nothing in this world but the four cubits of *halachah* alone.

And according to the ruling of our Sages of blessed memory that "study is great, for it leads to action" (see the Rambam’s introduction to his Commentary on the Mishnah regarding the explanation of the statement "the Holy One, Blessed be He, has nothing, etc.") and "the beginning of wisdom is the fear of Hashem," I hope that this radio broadcast will be used to emphasize and strengthen matters of *yiras shamayim* and the performance of *mitzvos* in actual practice. For the end of the matter—everything is heard: "Fear G-d and keep His *mitzvos*."

With appreciation and a blessing for success.

## 2278

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Gabbaim and congregants of the Chabad Center Synagogue, Tel Aviv
May they live

Peace and blessing!

I was distressed to hear reports that there is not a minyan for communal prayer in your synagogue every day, and furthermore, that on some days the synagogue is completely closed.

It is surely unnecessary to point out that if, at all times and in all places, synagogues and batei medrash have been a "miniature sanctuary" from which Torah radiates to the entire surrounding area, then how much more so is this necessity magnified in our times, and especially in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—upon which the eyes of Hashem are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year.

During these days of the month of Shevat, which includes the yahrtzeit of our Nasi, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and the Shabbosos before and after it, it is an *eis ratzon* and a time of *segulah* to strengthen ourselves and find appropriate ways to rectify the aforementioned situation. From here on, the synagogue and beis medrash should be open every day and every night—a place for tefillah and Torah, Torah in public, both in the revealed Torah and in the teachings of Chassidus.

It is a known tradition from our Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya (who ruled in the *nistar*) and the Shulchan Aruch (who ruled in the *nigleh*), that "because of this *mesiras nefesh* for the teachings of Chassidus, it was decreed in the Heavenly Court that in every matter of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps shall be uppermost" (*Ketzurim V'He'aros l'Sefer Likutei Amarim*, end of p. 122).

With blessings for success in the aforementioned matter of this "miniature sanctuary," and in all your holy endeavors in general.

I await good news.

## 279

B"H, 2 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

To Anash in the city of Toronto, may they live,

Peace and abundant blessing!

It gave me pleasure to receive your letter from the day of the Hillula of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, when you gathered together. Surely, as the Torah of Truth rules, "those who fear Hashem spoke to one another, and Hashem listened and heard, and a book of remembrance was written before Him," which provides strength and assistance from Above for the avodah of Hashem that follows. Since it has already been written down in a "book of remembrance," it means that forgetfulness cannot apply there, for it is **before** the Throne of Your Glory—and I would point to the laws of Talmud Torah by our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, chapter 2, end of paragraph 10.

Surely, following your good custom mentioned above, you will also gather on the day of the Hillula of my sainted father-in-law, the Rebbe, the leader of the generation, with hispaorerus and by accepting good resolutions in thought, speech, and actual deed in daily life. I have enclosed the maamar that was said on the Hillula last year, which has just now been published, and it is my hope that it will assist you in the aforementioned.

With blessings for success in walking in the ways of the Baal HaHillula, which he paved before us, and who is found now in this world even more than during his lifetime.

## 280

## 282

B”H, 3 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his holy work,
R’ Yaakov, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter regarding the variation in the formation of the letters in the script according to the Alter Rebbe, compared to the custom of others. As is evident from your letter, this is not a tradition passed down to you from person to person, but rather the result of your own close examination of the parshiyos written by Chabad sofrim. In this regard, there is indeed doubt as to what is precise and essential, and what is merely incidental and not essential. Perhaps it would be worthwhile for you, as an expert in this field, to research the matter; perhaps you will find someone who possesses a tradition passed down from person to person regarding the formation of these letters, as mentioned above. And a wise man [will learn] from the beginning...

Enclosed is the maamar that was delivered last year on the day of the hillula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. I am certain that you will view it favorably and share it with others as well, and may Hashem grant you success.

## 2883

B"H, 3 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter in due time, in which you write regarding the state of your health. You should have consulted with your mashpia to arrange a schedule of study for you that would not strain your health at all. It is already a known ruling of our holy Torah (Rambam, Hilchos De’os, beginning of Chapter 4) that maintaining a healthy and sound body is a way of serving Hashem. You are surely also aware of the saying of our Alter Rebbe (printed in Hayom Yom, Erev Rosh Hashanah): "One does not know at all how precious the body of a Yid is." Consequently, you must follow the instructions of the doctors and ensure that your schedule of eating, drinking, and rest is as required for the health of your body. Then, Hashem will also grant you success in your avodah of tefillah and in the study of Torah with yiras shamayim as is proper.

Enclosed is a maamar in which you will also see that the drawback of a strong body applies only if it is under the dominion of the nefesh habehamis, but not, Heaven forbid, regarding the health that pertains to the nefesh elokis.

Your pidyon nefesh has been received.

With blessings for success in Torah study and the avodah of tefillah with yiras shamayim, in the proper manner.

**With your mashpia:** See letter 2894 below.

## 2,384

B”H, 3 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, a scion of a noble family, a man of character, etc., etc., R’ Yosef Bardugo, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive word from the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, etc., R’ Michael Lipskar, may he live, that you have assumed your position to lead the holy community of the city of Meknes as in the past. It is already known from the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that every appointment is from Heaven, especially an appointment to lead a holy community, whose very material affairs are holy—and all the more so its spiritual affairs. Surely, you will utilize your fine talents and influence to uphold and disseminate the foundations of Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos in the spirit of our ancestors throughout the entire community. May the glorious past of your holy community continue to serve as a model of Yiddishkeit and as a center for Torah and yiras shamayim for all of Morocco.

With blessings for success in communal matters and in your personal affairs, for you and for your entire family, may they live.

## B'Safa

B"H, 4 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was informed of the state of your health, and subsequently of the results of your eye surgery, which, thank Hashem, was successful. May the Ribono shel Olam grant that your health continues to improve, and that you may gain strength in Torah and avodah, for a healthy and whole body is one of the ways of Hashem.

You have surely heard the saying of the Baal Shem Tov that every event a person encounters, and everything they see or hear, contains a hidden lesson for their path in the avodah of Hashem. This is especially true regarding a significant event, such as the one mentioned above, as a person’s eyesight is among their most important faculties. As is known in the revealed laws of our Torah, this is why (according to one opinion) a sighted person is specifically obligated in and merits the commandment of all the mitzvos, for "he is alive," etc. You are surely also familiar with the language of our Sages regarding the power of sight, which is the **light** (*maor*) of a person’s eyes. Every detail in the words of our Sages is precise to the ultimate degree, since even a single word in our holy Torah must have been given to Moshe at Sinai, as ruled by the Rambam in Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 3, Halacha 8.

"And this is the Torah of man"—just as the Holy One, blessed be He, looked into the Torah and created the world, the "great world," the same applies to man, who is called by our Sages a "small world" (Tanchuma, Parshas Pekudei, beginning; Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 69, p. 100b, and elsewhere). Corresponding to the light of a person’s eyes, there is also found in the Torah the "light that is in the Torah," as mentioned in the beginning of Eichah Rabbah: "The light within it returns one to the good." This light within the Torah is the *nistar* of the Torah—the *s'tim d'oraisa*—which brings one to the fear and love of Hashem, as our Sages stated (Shabbos 31a, end) and as is explained in Likutei Torah by the Alter Rebbe at the end of Parshas Vayikra. This was revealed in recent generations through the teachings of Chassidus in a way that everyone can understand it well, as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, explained at length in the *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*. I am not writing this as a mere sermon, but for practical application: you should resolve with absolute certainty to establish a regular shiur in the study of Chassidus from this point forward. This very resolution will hasten the healing of your eyes, and you will be able to realize it in practice soon.

With blessings for a speedy recovery.

#### ***B'Safa***

Published in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 11, p. 295; edited according to the secretariat's copy.

For its content, see also above, Vol. 7, Letter 2,137.

## 2827

B"H, 4 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter of 19 Teves has been received, in which you write that you are in the hospital under the care of doctors, describing your state of health and expressing your concern regarding this.

It is a well-known general principle that every person must be strong in their trust in Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, and as one’s trust increases, so too will the improvement in one’s health. However, at the same time, our holy Torah has stated, "and he shall surely heal," meaning that the doctor is the messenger of the Healer of all flesh to bring healing to those who require it. In order to strengthen this trust and increase the blessings of Hashem, one must also increase their involvement in matters of Torah and mitzvos, each person according to their standing and situation. Furthermore, one should not be satisfied with working only on oneself, but should also encourage those in one’s surroundings—whom one can surely influence to some degree—and encourage them as well in these two matters together: in trust and in increasing Torah and mitzvos. The attribute of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is "measure for measure"; when one increases the spiritual or physical health of a fellow Jew, the Holy One, Blessed be He, adds many times over for the one who exerts effort in this. May Hashem grant you success and bring you good tidings regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary:
