## 2339

B"H, 25 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you ask for a *tikkun* for having traveled by ship, etc.: You should establish a regular study of the *halachos* of Shabbos. This is understood, apart from the fact that this is the very matter discussed in the *Kuntres Acharon* of the Alter Rebbe at its conclusion—to be proficient in *hilchasa rabbata l'shabta* (the great laws of Shabbos).

Furthermore, *bli neder*, every Erev Shabbos you should give some coins to *tzedakah*. And on the day of Shabbos itself, you should have an additional *shiur* in the study of *pnimiyus haTorah*, which is the Torah of Chassidus. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success, so that what is stated in the *Kuntres Acharon*—that all [his sins] are forgiven, etc.—may be fulfilled in you.

With blessings for success in your affairs, and in all the aforementioned in particular.

## 2336

2336

B"H, 25 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

It has been some time since I received your letter in which you express the heartfelt wishes of yourself and your wife, tichyeh, to be blessed with healthy children. When I am at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you for the aforementioned.

It is well known that in a letter from our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, he writes that a segulah for the birth of children is the matter of ahavah and yirah, for the love and fear of Hashem are called "son" and "daughter" in the spiritual sense. This letter is printed at length at the end of the Siddur Meah Shearim. Consequently, you should establish an additional shiur for the study of Chassidus.

It is understood that you must follow the instructions of the doctors, since for everything there must be an anchorage in the ways of nature. Furthermore, your wife, tichyeh, should give a few coins to tzedakah before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov. You should also have your mezuzos and tefillin checked once again. It would also be appropriate to clarify whether, during the time of your shidduch, there was any incident that might have touched upon a slight to the honor of a son or daughter of Yisrael.

May Hashem grant you success and enable you to share the good news that your wife, tichyeh, has been remembered. Certainly, as per the instruction of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, do not publicize this to relatives until she enters the fifth month of her pregnancy. By "publicize," I mean only in the aforementioned manner; it is understood that you may tell him, as well as the attending physician, etc. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings, awaiting good news.

Consequently, the shame of all those who rise up against it and against the ways of Avigdor, etc., is immediately revealed in public, and their downfall is certain from the outset. If at times it takes a little longer, it is only because the Chassidim give them a sense of importance. This is all the more so—a fortiori—given how much the Alter Rebbe suffered from the fact that he drank a cup of tea in the home of an opponent...

May it be Hashem’s will that it be fulfilled: "May sins cease, and not sinners."

With blessings—awaiting good news.

## 2349

B"H, 28 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your notification that you have begun putting on tefillin these days, that you are preparing for your Bar Mitzvah, and that you are studying the maamar beginning with the words "It is stated in Midrash Tehillim" in order to recite it at your Bar Mitzvah:

May it be the will of Hashem that you contemplate frequently the intent of the mitzvah of tefillin, as explained in the Shulchan Aruch and also in Tanya, Chapter 41—to nullify and include the aspects of one’s chochma and binah, etc. This means not to utilize the chochma and binah of one’s soul except for Hashem alone, and likewise to nullify the aspect of da'as in one’s soul, etc., which are the yirah and ahavah in one’s heart, etc. The main thing is to fulfill this in practice—namely, to increase in diligence and perseverance in the study of Torah, and for this to be with mesiras nefesh and dedication, with a sense of personal commitment, for then it will also be successful.

I am sure that after davening you recite several chapters of Tehillim, and that you also give a few coins to tzedakah before davening, as is the custom of the members of ATZ"H—Igud Talmidei HaYeshivos—and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings.

## 2,540

B"H, 28 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 20 Shevat, in which you write regarding your family situation and also that you have set times for Torah study. Although you do not detail them, you surely have set times for both the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, which, in the language of the holy Zohar, is called the "soul of the Torah." Just as the revelation of the soul acts to provide additional health and vitality to the movements of the body, so too in the analogy: the study of the inner dimension of the Torah provides additional vitality to the revealed Torah. If in all times and in all places one should strive ever more for additional vitality in matters of Torah and mitzvos, how much more so in this generation, the *ikvesa d'Meshicha*. Surely, elaborating on this is unnecessary.

You are certainly aware of the *takanah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzuklalleh-h, nbg"m, zy"a*, regarding the *shiurim* that are accessible to every person: 1) Reciting the daily *shiur* of Tehillim—as Tehillim is divided according to the days of the month—each day after *davening* Shacharis; 2) Studying the *parsha* of Chumash with Rashi’s commentary for the weekly *parsha* (on Sunday, from the beginning of the *sedra* until the second *aliyah*; on Monday, from the second *aliyah* until the third, etc.); 3) A *shiur* in Tanya, as Tanya is divided according to the days of the year. I trust you will strive to fulfill these.

May Hashem grant you success in your material livelihood and in your spiritual livelihood, regarding yourself, your wife, and your son, *shichyu*.

With blessings.

## 2441

B"H, 29 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 4 Shevat, regarding your request for advice on how to alleviate the trial of the well-known sin:

You should endeavor to memorize several chapters of Mishnayos, several chapters of Tanya, and also the maamar in Likutei Torah at the end of Parshas Kedoshim, entitled *Ve'hadarta Pnei Zaken*. For then, even when you are not actively reviewing them by heart, they remain stored in your memory—as is also explained in the additions at the end of the book of Vayikra in Likutei Torah. In your spare time, you should review the aforementioned by heart, in such a way that you go over at least one chapter of Tanya and Mishnayos every day.

It is understood that all of this must be done *bli neder* and outside of your yeshiva study schedule. You should increase your courage in the study of *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*, and take care of your physical health; all of the above will assist you in the battle against the *yetzer*. May Hashem purify your mind and heart so that you may achieve success in Torah and *mitzvos*.

And in anticipation of your birthday, may it be the will of Hashem that this year be a year of success for you in *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*, and in the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*.

With blessings.

## 2,742

2,742

B"H, 29 Shevat, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos. When I was at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I mentioned you and your wife, may they live, for the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for the good.

Regarding what you write about the reason you have not yet performed the *durchblazung* (clearing of the pipes): first, it must be clarified whether such a procedure is necessary—that is, whether the pipes are indeed blocked, and only then should it be performed. As for your writing that this is associated with great suffering, Heaven forbid, I find this surprising, as this is a daily occurrence here, and I have not heard of anyone complaining of great suffering, etc.

I was pleased to hear that you are keeping the three daily *shiurim* that are incumbent upon everyone—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—as is well known. It goes without saying that this should be done *bli neder* (without a vow), and consequently, if it is missed occasionally due to unavoidable circumstances, that is not the intent, and surely in such cases, you will make it up in the following days.

I trust you have had your *mezuzos* checked within the last twelve months; if it has been longer than that, it is worthwhile to have them checked. May Hashem grant you the merit to succeed and to bring good tidings regarding the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for the good.

With blessings,

2443

B”H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar Rishon, 5714
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established
To those upon whom may they live

Greetings and Blessings,

It is puzzling that for a long time now, I have not received any letter from you. Furthermore, regarding the telegram I sent for the day of the Yahrtzeit-Hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, leader of the generation—the tenth of Shevat—in which I requested that you notify Kfar Chabad and all Chabad institutions in the Holy Land to hold a farbrengen on the day of the Hilula and to inspire one another toward good deeds, relying on the well-known fact that the shepherd has not abandoned his flock—to this day, I have not received confirmation that the telegram was received, nor, most importantly, to which of our institutions this was conveyed, and what the practical outcome was. I am certain that you will fulfill all of the above at the earliest opportunity, and I thank you in advance.

2) I am also puzzled that, although I have requested many times that you inform me of developments that might concern Chabad institutions and Chabad avodah—and beyond what is known in the seforim, and not only in the books of Chassidus, it is understood even by common sense that every man and woman is not merely an individual, but that their actions affect the collective, for each of them is an emissary of the Makom to illuminate their surroundings with the light of Elokus. If one wishes to succeed within their own "four cubits," it is impossible to do so except by fulfilling the mission of the Makom, B”H, who is the Master of both the collective and the individual. This is the special task of Chassidei Chabad—since our Nesi’im invested special powers in them and assigned them a special task founded on ahavas Yisrael, as interpreted by our Rebbeim, that this intention includes even one who is at the edge of the world, even if one has never seen him, etc.

You must strive with the greatest energy to know what is happening in your surroundings, in your city, and in every place that your reach can extend, and seek counsel on how to act in these matters according to the ways our holy Rebbeim have taught us.

And as mentioned—this is the only path for Chassidim through which they can succeed in their private affairs, to be protected from an evil person and an evil occurrence, and to succeed in good deeds in Torah and mitzvos and in their material and spiritual needs—both for themselves and for their families, may they live.

3) I have hinted at all of the above many times, and to my sorrow, it has not led to tangible action. Since I have no choice, just as you have no choice, I repeat this again and again, perhaps it will be effective.

I have one justification for you: that your current state of mind is the opposite of the scriptural command, "and his heart was lifted up in the ways of Hashem," and consequently you are in a state of constriction and tzimtzum. I have already written many times in recent weeks that this is not the way to succeed, neither in the collective nor in the individual. On the contrary, tzimtzum is the root of the dinim, and it is imperative that you work in all Chabad matters with expansion and breadth, as is the will and instruction of the Rebbe. When you fulfill the command, "Serve Hashem with joy," then joy nullifies dinim and breaks through barriers.

It is already well-known from the days of our Rabbeinu HaZaken—who was the founder of Chassidus Chabad, its Torah, its guidance, and its customs—that many rose up against him, led by Avigdor, who also came with false accusations. But very quickly, his shame was revealed in public, even though he had succeeded in swaying the hearts of those not versed in the wiles of the yetzer hara. Nevertheless, his downfall was complete, his end was disgraceful, and the victory of Chassidus was total within a few weeks—and afterwards, it went on to spread more and more, capturing the hearts of tens of thousands of Jews.

Elaborating on this is unnecessary, as all the details are known.

And all the more so after seven generations have passed since the time of Rabbeinu HaZaken, and Chassidus continues to spread in spirituality, and consequently in physicality as well. If, at any given time, a lowly and despicable person rises up against it, one should not be affected at all. For all the chutzpah of the despicable person stems only from seeing that people fear him, and his intimidation makes an impression because they are not sufficiently prepared during times of challenge and the like. But if they were to see immediately that his shame is exposed and the whole truth about him is told as it is, then, as explained in Tanya, he would be null and void of his own accord, just as Avigdor later went around to the doors of Chassidim begging for help...

Now, one does not cry over the past. I have come only regarding the future: in order to succeed in your private affairs, in addition to Chabad activity in general, it is imperative that you not give any room at all to intimidations that have no substance... they will melt like wax, until even they themselves see that there is no substance to it, and all the distress he caused was only because you gave room to his existence. In this way, you will see with your own physical eyes success in your private affairs and in the general matters.

I hope these few lines will suffice for you to adopt the path of our forefathers, and according to the command of our holy Torah: that although "sins may cease, but not sinners," at the same time, the entire existence of the kelipah is, as explained in Tanya, Chapter 27, that regarding the holiness of the nefesh elokis within a person, Hashem gave it permission and ability to exalt itself against it, so that the person will be aroused to overcome it and humble it, etc., and then it is automatically nullified and cast aside.

And even if the kelipah is clothed in a person who has a beard and wears long garments and outwardly behaves in the ways of Chassidus, it is known from the saying of Rabbeinu HaZaken that Eisav the wicked wore a silk surtuk.

May Hashem grant you the breadth of mind and breadth of heart necessary for every Jewish person, and all the more so for Chassidei Chabad, of whom the Tzemach Tzedek said, "We are the workers of the day," that our task is to illuminate the world with the candle of mitzvah and the light of Torah, and the "light" in Torah is the Torah of Chassidus, which necessitates that one’s heart be lifted up in the ways of Hashem.

I await good news in all of the above, and I sign with a blessing for immense success in general matters and in your private affairs, for you and all your families, may they live.

With respect and blessings for success in communal matters and in your personal affairs—for in truth, the two are interdependent—I await good news.

Since time is passing and being lost, haste in this matter is to be praised. With blessings,

## 2747

B"H, Thursday, Parshas V'asu Li Mikdash
Brooklyn, N.Y.
5714

To the N'shei U'Bnos Chabad Organization
May Hashem grant them life
Branch:

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive regards from you and news of your work through the esteemed Chossid, who is involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Peretz שיחי' Matzkin. I also hope to receive from you directly more detailed news—joyous news—regarding you and your families שיחיו, concerning Torah and mitzvos, which is health and parnassah in ruchniyus, and which also brings health and parnassah in gashmiyus.

On this occasion, I wish to emphasize once again the tremendous zechus and the special kochos that the Ribono shel Olam has given to women to establish the home, so that it should be a truly Yiddishe home, and to occupy themselves with the chinuch of the children—in addition to the other mitzvos in general.

In these days and weeks when we read in the Torah the sedros that are connected with the establishment of the Mishkan and Mikdash, it is emphasized there that the women were the first and the most devoted in this holy work.

Building a Mikdash, the holy sefarim explain, exists for every Yid, man or woman—this is one's own home, as every Yiddishe home must be a Mikdash for the Ribono shel Olam. And the greatest part of establishing this Mikdash belongs to the woman, as is explained in detail in the words to women by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzk"l, nb"m, zy"a, which is enclosed herewith.

It is also explained in many places in the Gemara and Zohar that strengthening the ways of tznius of the woman is a certain path to health, parnassah, and much nachas—true nachas—from children and grandchildren. This depends on each one of you, to act in this yourself, and also to see to it that your good friends, relatives, and acquaintances should also know of the great possibilities they have, and the hatzlacha that is connected with this.

And may the Ribono shel Olam help that each one of you should act in this according to her full potential, and then the Ribono shel Olam will certainly fulfill His promise to grant health, parnassah, and true nachas in full measure.

Awaiting good tidings and blessing each and every one of you and your families שיחיו, in gashmiyus and in ruchniyus.

## 2748

2748

By the Grace of Hashem, 1 Adar Rishon, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the members of the Shila Association,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure the news from the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and dedicated worker for the sake of heaven, Rabbi Dovid Baumgarten, that this coming Shabbos, Parshas Terumah, you will be holding a *siyum* on Masechta Berachos at the *Kiddusha Rabba*.

May Hashem grant you success in your endeavors, that just as you have completed these *mishnayos*, so too may you begin and complete other *masechtos*, and continue your learning with an expanded mind, through which the ruling of our Sages will be fulfilled: "You have labored and you have found."

The reason why the beginning of the *masechtos* is Masechta Berachos is well known. Within this *masechta* itself, it begins with the laws of *Krias Shema*, which is as it is written, "The beginning of wisdom is the fear of Hashem," and this is the essence of *Krias Shema*.

As the *Mishnah* states at the beginning of the second chapter of Berachos, the first paragraph of *Shema* is the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, and the paragraph of *Ve'haya Im Shamoa* is the acceptance of the yoke of the *mitzvos*.

In this, we can also explain the precision as to why the *mitzvah* of *Krias Shema* itself begins with the laws of *Krias Shema* in the evening, at night. When a person begins their *avodah* of Hashem, they are still in darkness—both in terms of the world in general, and primarily, in terms of their own body and their animal and natural soul, which conceal and darken the light of the truth. For only Hashem is the Truth, and there is nothing else besides Him. All that exists—the heavens, the earth, and everything in between—exists only from the truth of His existence, from which it is understood *a priori* that He is the Master of all the earth (as explained in the beginning of Rambam, *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*). The beginning of *avodah* in such a state is to accept upon oneself the **yoke** of the Kingdom of Heaven and the **yoke** of Torah and *mitzvos* (in the language of Rabbeinu Yeshaya Acharon), just as in the giving of the Torah as a whole, the Jewish people preceded "we will do" to "we will hear."

This is also the explanation for the Gemara’s reasoning: the *Mishnah* begins with the *Krias Shema* of the evening, like the creation of the world. For the world in its entirety was created "first darkness"—the darkness of concealment and the hiding of the Divine light—and "afterwards light"—the light of man’s *avodah*, through which the Divine light illuminates the world. This is also true in the life of a person, who is called a "small world" (*Shabbos 77b*; *D"H Vayakam Eidus*, in *Sefer HaMaamarim 5700*).

And let no person say, "I have time to contemplate and consult whether I should begin this *avodah*, whether I should continue in it, etc.," and in general, "This is a private matter of mine, and who is to tell me what to do?"

For every single person is a part of the totality of the world, and upon every single person is placed the command of this week’s *parsha*:

"And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell among them." As our Sages of blessed memory noted, it does not say "in it" (*b'tocho*), but "among them" (*b'tocham*)—**within each and every Jew.**

Just as every single day one is obligated in the morning, evening, and night prayers—which were established corresponding to the *tamid* offerings and the incense—and the offering of the sacrifices in their literal sense had to be in the physical *Beis HaMikdash*, so too, the offering of prayers that replace the sacrifices must be in the spiritual sanctuary, which is each and every Jew. From this, it is also understood that just as the concept of the sanctuary is, as the name implies, holiness and the *avodah* of Hashem—which is why it is called a "house of prayer," for "serve Hashem with fear," and this *avodah* is prayer—in the same way, this applies to the entirety of a person’s *avodah*. It is to know and to make known that everything that was, is, and will be is through His word. The foundation for this, and the ultimate purpose of this, is as mentioned above regarding the *mitzvah* of *Krias Shema*: the fear of Heaven and the acceptance of the yoke of His Kingdom, which is the ultimate purpose of Torah study and the fulfillment of *mitzvos*.

As it is written: "And Hashem commanded us to perform all these statutes, to fear Hashem our G-d."

And the Holy One, blessed be He, is faithful to fulfill His promise at the conclusion of this verse:

"For our good all the days, to keep us alive as this day," and as explained by the Torah commentators, "for our good" in this world and in the World to Come.

With blessings for success, both in Torah study in groups and individually, and in the fulfillment of *mitzvos*, and to increase the "candle of *mitzvah* and the light of Torah"—with all your heart, with all your soul, and with all your might, in thought, speech, and action in your daily life.

## 2,349

B"H, 1st of Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of Tuesday, I am hastening to reply, as it concerns the purity of the daughters of Israel. It is not worthwhile to continue the back-and-forth discussion any further; one should immediately begin with the improvements upon which there is already agreement. It is understood that one must also strive for the other improvements in an appropriate manner.

To a great extent, it depends on how one initiates the conversation regarding this. Frequently, when one speaks with simplicity—conveying that this is a straightforward matter, not a major issue, and that there is absolutely no intention to cast aspersions on those who came before us—and when the main point is that one is not inconveniencing others and is showing them respect, it is possible to carry out all these matters without difficulties. Especially once they begin the improvements and all parties realize that there is no intention to diminish their stature or the like, it will be easier for them to agree to the remaining improvements and matters, even if they were not discussed beforehand.

With blessings for success in all of the above.

## 2550

B"H, 2 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Shevat, in which you write regarding the state of your health and also that you are suffering from aggressive neighbors.

Regarding your health, you must consult with two expert physicians and follow their instructions; the Torah has granted permission (which also implies the power) to the physician to heal...

Regarding what you wrote about bad neighbors, this usually stems from a lack of kavanah during the Birchas HaShachar when we pray, "Save us... from a bad neighbor." Most importantly, it stems from not striving as one ought regarding the "bad neighbor" that is within the heart of man—the Yetzer Hara. Naturally, when one increases their efforts in both of these areas, the attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure," only many times over. One then sees improvement even regarding the bad neighbor in the literal sense. It is also appropriate to have the mezuzos in your apartment checked to ensure they are all kosher, as well as your tefillin.

With blessings for good news in all the above.

## 2551

B"H, 4 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 3 Terumah, which begins with a request made with a "broken and contrite heart," etc.

Now, although "the sacrifices of Hashem are a broken spirit; a broken and contrite heart," this applies when it stems from thoughts of teshuvah or the like. However, when Hashem grants success and fulfills a request, yet one remains dissatisfied without any specific reason, this is not the correct path. Since Hashem has fulfilled the desires of your heart and the heart of your wife—may they live and be well—and will surely also bring the days of her pregnancy to completion in the proper manner, so that she gives birth to a healthy child at the proper time and with ease, I do not understand the premise of your letter, in which you describe yourself as broken and contrite. Furthermore, you make no mention of increasing your efforts in matters of Torah and mitzvos. To my mind, the opposite is true: your letter should have begun by expressing gratitude to Hashem for the fact that your wife has conceived. This itself provides you with the confidence that in the future, too, the Creator—who is the essence of goodness—will bestow goodness upon you, your wife, and your son—may they live and be well. Following that, you should have concluded by stating that you, for your part, have increased the "conduits and vessels" that serve to receive Hashem’s blessings in the future, with the addition that these conduits and vessels are the matters of Torah and mitzvos.

As we enter the month of Adar, during which we increase in joy, may Hashem add joy to you and your wife—may they live and be well—in all the aforementioned matters, and may you derive increased nachas from your son... may he live.

With blessings,

#### ***2551***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 14, p. 356, and edited according to the secretariat’s copy.

## 2552

2552

B"H, 4 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter from 4 Shevat has been received. May Hashem help that in the future, too, you will be able to share good news, both regarding your communal activities and regarding yourselves—and most importantly, may Hashem fulfill your hearts' desires for the good, with children, life, and ample sustenance.

In response to your question: the procedure that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, stated—that one should not publicize [a pregnancy] until entering the fifth month—refers only to publicizing it. It is self-understood, however, that one must inform the doctor, and one may inform relatives and close friends. It is also self-understood that one must follow the doctor’s instructions and also ask the doctor—even though he will do so on his own—that if he wishes to perform an examination, he should only examine from the outside, but not internally, as that is not as necessary for medical knowledge as it is for the sake of being certain of the situation. Therefore, if such an examination can be avoided, it would be worthwhile to avoid it.

It would also be a proper thing to have the mezuzos in your home checked once again, and I look forward to hearing good news from you.

With blessings for the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for the good, and very soon.

## 2554

B"H, 5 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 28 Teves, in which you write regarding the relationship between yourself and your wife, may she live.

It is well known how much our Sages of blessed memory emphasized the matter of *shalom bayis*, and that when a husband and wife are worthy, the *Shechinah* dwells between them. Consequently, you must increase your efforts to show affection toward your wife, may she live, so that she may return to your home, and that from this point forward, peace—and therefore joy—will dwell in your home.

You should certainly take note of the words of our Sages that women are sensitive by nature, that a woman’s tears are easily shed, and that the gates of tears are never locked. Therefore, in matters such as these, the husband must concede in worldly affairs as much as possible. This is especially true in your case, where one must consider the impact that the relationship between you will have on your children, may they live.

Given the great importance of these matters, I am certain that if you contemplate them, you will find the appropriate ways to bring about peace in practice. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings, and awaiting good news.

## 255

B"H, 5 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, the scribe and author,
Rabbi Avraham, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter—though it was undated—and subsequently I received your book, *Chutim HaMeshulashim*. May Hashem grant you the merit and success to increase Torah and glorify it, and to disseminate the light of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs to the widest possible circles. It is already known as a saying of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, which we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that Chassidus is not a matter belonging to one specific group in Israel, but rather to all the children of Israel for all generations. Happy is the portion of each and every one who strives to spread the wellsprings outward.

With blessings for long, good years and for success in your holy work.

P.S.
Enclosed is a check for your personal expenses.

Notes, written in haste while leafing through the pages of the book:

**In the Introduction, p. 75: Regarding *Zemiros*** — See *Tanya*, *Kuntres Acharon*, the discourse beginning *Dovid Zemiros*. And at length in *Likutei Torah*, *Bamidbar* 18a and onwards.

**Story 1 in the Introduction, p. 10, side 1: "The secret of the *mikveh*, etc.—this means, etc."** The explanation requires study, for this is not the "secret of the *mikveh*" but rather the literal meaning of the matter. The meaning of the saying is: elevation from the mundane to holiness, and from one level of holiness to another (this is similar to the five immersions of the *Kohen Gadol* on Yom Kippur, or the immersion on Shabbos even if one had already immersed on Erev Shabbos, and the like).

**Story 3.** That the Baal Shem Tov specifically attended to his needs and only afterwards read the *petek* (note) before *Birkas HaMazon* so that he would be able to find it, etc.—even if the story were received through tradition from person to person and were accurate in all its details, it is highly questionable whether it was appropriate to publish it in print and in Yiddish. Especially since, according to our Sages, the bathroom is the opposite of "and your camp shall be holy," and also because one must **hurry** to wash one's hands afterwards, for an evil spirit rests [there], etc.—it is near certain to me that the story, or at least its essential details, are not true. The matter of *nefilas apayim* proves this, as it is a great descent to elevate from the *kelipos* to the point that it is considered like death, and it is forbidden to do so in a place where there is a *Sefer Torah*, etc.

**Story 5, p. 122:** It is difficult to reconcile the story so that it conforms to the law of the Torah. Furthermore, **even if we were to say** that all the details of the story are true and accurate, as mentioned above, the publication of such stories—which are associated with the name of the Baal Shem Tov and Chassidus—is certainly a loss, while its benefit is highly doubtful.

**End of story 19, p. 173:** Based on the ruling of the *Magen Avraham* (*Orach Chaim*, end of 156): "Whoever does not say a thing in the name of the one who said it violates a negative commandment"—it is understood that the conclusion of the story is not true. I am astonished that you, sir, would print such a thing about the Alter Rebbe, even though your intention was surely desirable.

## 2557

B”H, 5 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 2 Shevat, along with the *pan* enclosed therein, which I read at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding your question: you have observed a change in the state of your business and are consequently searching for the cause, and it has occurred to you that perhaps this is connected to the fact that you accepted a rabbinical position when you went into exile during the war.

Now, common sense dictates that when there is an apparent cause, there is no necessity to search for hidden causes, for "the revealed things belong to us and to our children." In the present case, it is known from our Sages that "a statement made to the Almighty is like a delivery made to a common person." It is also known from the halachic ruling that "salt for money is lack" — meaning that the *segulah* for *parnassah* is the matter of *tzedakah*. Since it has been a long time since you took it upon yourselves in the name of the business to set aside a *maaser*—and even a little more than that—for *tzedakah*, and you have delayed this for several months, and the way of the *Ribono shel Olam* is one of kindness and mercy, surely this is a hint given to you to remind you of your commitment and the merit you possess, which you have not yet fulfilled in practice with the generosity of your pure hearts. This is a sufficient explanation for the change in the business. Consequently, you need not search for other matters, but rather fulfill your promise completely—and most importantly, with good will. When your decision to conduct yourselves this way in the future is absolute—and it is revealed before Heaven the nature of this decision—and it is done with joy rather than from fear of punishment, *chas v’shalom*, I am confident that an improvement in the business will follow as well. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you and your brother, *sheyichyeh*, the merit to decide this as soon as possible and with joy, for "joy breaks through barriers" to bestow upon you blessing and success.

With blessings.

The 36 [currency unit] that you sent as a start were received and delivered to the *tzedakah* fund.

## 2,559

B"H, 6 Adar, 5714

To the Administration of Yeshivas Toras Emes,

I trust that in the meantime my previous letter has been received, as well as the *scripts* that were written here on the day of the Hillula. They should arrange a *farbrengen*—it is understood that this should be in the presence of the *mashpia* of *Chassidus* as well as the *ramim* of *nigleh*—and after the program I suggested to them in the aforementioned letter, they should distribute the *scripts*. It is also understood that for those students who do not participate in the *farbrengen*, their *scripts* should be deposited into the general fund of the yeshiva. I will await good news regarding all of the above.

I await good news regarding all of the above, and I sign with a blessing for outstanding success in the administration of the holy institution of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a*, the leader of the generation, with true peace of mind in accordance with the ruling of our holy Torah, and may his heart be uplifted in the ways of Hashem, and may all the concealments and obstructions melt like wax, and may the desire of Hashem succeed in their hands.

## 2,762

B"H, 11 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write about your spiritual state and your desire to rectify the deficiencies in matters of *yiras shamayim*, the *avodah* of *tefillah*, and the study of Torah.

It is a well-known principle, as stated by our Sages regarding the above: "If one says, 'I have not labored but I have found,' do not believe him; 'I have labored and I have not found,' do not believe him." From this, it is understood that the matter depends on one's own efforts, provided that one labors in it sincerely and according to one's own capacity.

It is unnecessary to remind you—as this has already been publicized in several letters and subsequently in *maamarim* of *Chassidus*—that the proper path is not through fasts and self-afflictions that weaken one's health. Rather, "you shall surely help him" [involves working] together with the body and the *nefesh habehamis*. The *sigufim* (afflictions) must be of the *nefesh habehamis*, not of the human body, which is the possession of the *Ribono shel Olam*, as is explained in many places. See the *Hilchos Nizkei HaGuf* by our *Alter Rebbe*—the *posek* in the hidden dimensions of Torah—and the *Shulchan Aruch*—the *posek* in the revealed dimensions of Torah. The *sigufim* of the *nefesh habehamis* consist of restraining one's mouth from speaking idle words—and even words that are necessary, at times delaying them for a period or for a few moments—as well as guarding the sense of sight, etc., as is explained in many places (including *Sefer HaToldos* of the *Admur Maharash* *n.e.*, page 72, at the end). You should consult with a *mashpia* of *Chassidus* in your vicinity; it would be best to consult with the *chossid* Rabbi Shlomo Chaim *sheyichyeh* Kesselman, *mashpia* of *Chassidus* at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod. It is unnecessary to explain that all of the above is in addition to your regular *shiurim* in the study of *Chassidus* and the revealed Torah. May the *Hashem* grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the *Admur* *shlita*.

***

**Not this is the path:** See also above, letter 2,380, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 2,563

[11 Adar Rishon, 5714]

In response to your letter from the 4th of Tetzaveh regarding the *sheitel*: You write that you do not clearly understand what the intention is in this matter. The point of a *sheitel* is that the hair should be entirely covered; consequently, if one covers only a part, it is not as intended. Furthermore, you should have made an effort to ensure that others do the same, and help them understand that this is the path and the *segulah* for healthy *parnassah* and true *nachas* from children. May Hashem help that we hear good news regarding this...

#### ***2,563***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 8, p. 285.

## 2,464

B"H, 12 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It is unnecessary to elaborate on what is already detailed and explained at length by our Sages regarding the immense virtue of peace, and that "there is no vessel that holds blessing except for peace." Only in this manner can one align with the will of our holy Nasi, may the merit of his righteousness protect us, who sacrificed themselves for the cause of ahavas Yisrael. Conducting oneself in their spirit draws down additional blessing and success in one's activities...

Certainly, when the other administrators, teachers, and instructors see that he, for his part, has adopted the trait of concession and is not insistent that "his opinion must be accepted"—provided that it serves the benefit of the matters at hand, for sometimes one must apply the principle of "it is a time to act for Hashem, they have violated Your Torah"—then my hope is strong that through this conduct, peace will increase in their camp, and consequently, success in their activities will also increase. It is understood that sometimes, through concession, one may cause a temporary weakness in certain details, but as mentioned above, in "a time to act," this temporary pause leads to a much greater reward.

It is understood that one cannot set hard and fast rules in this regard, as conditions vary according to the places and the individuals. I have only come here with a general observation: it is essential that those participating in the same work should work with goodwill, and not out of compulsion or merely as one paying a debt for a salary... And one who is broad-minded finds it much easier not to get involved in matters of "my strength has prevailed" at all, and also to take into account that sometimes the loss caused by a concession is outweighed by its reward.

And another point that one must strive for **more and more**, as I have written several times: that all those from anash, and even those who are only of the lineage of anash—both male and female teachers—one must strive to the utmost to include them in the work. Even if at times there is no apparent absolute necessity, since it results in greater preference and perfection in the work, it is worthwhile. Especially in education, where every small addition in a boy or girl will, over time, grow significantly. And with the development of the work, surely in a short time, a way will be found to utilize their strengths to the fullest...

I await good news regarding all of the above, and thank you in advance for your promptness in this matter.

## 2765

B"H, 12 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Adar, in which you write that you have reached the age of shidduchim, that a suitable proposal has not yet been found for you, and that you are distressed by this.

It is well known from our Sages that "matching them is as difficult as the splitting of the Yam Suf." It is also known that the splitting of the Yam Suf was brought about through the strength of bitachon and emunah in Hashem. It is therefore understood that the same must apply to the matter of shidduchim; to the extent that one strengthens his bitachon (and it is understood that, together with this, one must also search in an appropriate manner), the actualization will be hastened.

The statement of the holy Zohar is well known: "He looked into the Torah and created the world"—both the world in its literal sense and all the details of a person's life, who is called an "olam katan." Consequently, you should increase your study, both in Torah Nigleh and in Chassidus, and Hashem will grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.

In response to your question from some time ago regarding the fact that on Shabbos there is an "ascent of the worlds" in their *chitzoniyus* (externality) but not in their *pnimiyus* (internality), whereas on Rosh Hashanah there is an "ascent of the worlds" in their *pnimiyus* but not in their *chitzoniyus* (as explained in many places in Chassidus; see also Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 14, and Kuntres Acharon, p. 157b; Hemshech Rosh Hashanah 5665, and elsewhere)—you asked how this works when Rosh Hashanah falls on Shabbos.

The matter is explained based on the well-known principle that there are many levels within *pnimiyus* and *chitzoniyus*; there is a *pnimiyus* of *pnimiyus*, a *chitzoniyus* of *chitzoniyus*, and so on. See also Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 29 (150a): "There are many levels of 'face to face' and many levels of 'back to back' without end, etc." See also the book Derech Mitzvosecha, at the end of Mitzvas Lo Teva'aru Eish: "And therefore it is not discernible from the outside to the eye of the beholder, etc." See there.

***

2765

Part of this letter was printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 14, p. 302, and part on p. 377; it was completed according to the secretariat’s copy.

**The matter is explained:** See also above, Vol. 7, Epistle 1940, and the references in the footnotes there.

On the other hand, being present at a child’s *simcha* is a great *zechus*, and that *zechus* is earned through *emunah* and *bitachon* in Hashem. However, from what I see in your letter, I have become doubtful as to whether the situation is truly such...

May Hashem help that you both strengthen yourselves in *emunah* and *bitachon* as is fitting in a Chassidishe home, and may Hashem grant you the *zechus* to derive Chassidishe *nachas* from all your children, *shichyu*, in good health.

With blessings.

## 2,659

B"H, 13 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks the date of writing—in which you write that you possess the book *Chemdas Tzvi* on *Tikkunei Zohar* and that you wish to consign it to the fire because you have heard that there are those who object to it, etc.

I was alarmed by such a notion. Even if there were grounds for the aforementioned objections, it is not for you to involve yourself in such matters. At most, you should simply refrain from studying it, but not condemn books to be burned. Regarding this book in particular, since the *Tzemach Tzedek* cites it (*Likutei Torah, Devarim* 27d; *Reshimot, Eichah* p. 44), these rumors certainly have no basis.

Regarding the book *Chemdas HaYamim*, there are differing opinions on this matter as well. Since I have not, for the time being, found it cited in the works of our holy Rebbes, then on the other hand, why must you begin your study of Kabbalah specifically with books about which there are differences of opinion? Especially since I have already emphasized the necessity of studying the teachings of Chassidus, in which the wisdom of Kabbalah is also included, and specifically through which one is protected from erring, Heaven forbid, in the *Chochmah HaEmes*. Who would dare say that he will study in his own way and "perform tricks"? The story of the *Tzemach Tzedek* is already well-known (*Shoresh Mitzvos HaTefillah*, end of Chapter 2, that the Baal Shem Tov commanded not to study books of Kabbalah, because one who does not know how to strip the concepts of their physicality becomes very materialized through this study, etc.; see there).

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

2770

14 Adar I, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, the man of action, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., Rabbi S.Y. [Zevin], may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 17 Shevat, as well as the *pidyon nefesh* delivered by the esteemed Rabbi, the man of action, the energetic one, etc., Rabbi Weiss, may he live. May Hashem grant each of us the merit to report only good news from now on, both in communal matters and in private affairs.

2) Thank you for pointing out the printing error you found in the *Moreh Shiur* for the 7th of Shevat in a leap year. As I wrote in my previous letter, due to the pressure of time, I entrusted and relied upon others for proofreading of this nature. In any case, the verse states, "Who can discern errors?"

3) Regarding your note on the *Tikkun Derech Efshar*—where you found "the esteemed Rabbi" in place of "the esteemed Chossid," or "the esteemed" in place of "the Chossid"—I found it recorded as such on the margin of a Tanya, copied from the Tanya of the elder Chassidim of past generations, who, as is evident from your other notes, were reliable sources. Nevertheless, I could not determine with certainty who it was, and therefore I included your changes in the section of *Tikkunim Derech Efshar*.

4) Regarding the doubt in Tanya, Chapter 1, page 5, line 7, regarding the word "mizeh" (from this): in my opinion, it connects to what precedes it. Similarly, the word "zeh" (this) on page 24b, line 11. Although some have recently suggested that it connects to what follows, this requires further study in the *Kuntres Bikkur Chicago*, page 63 and onwards.

5) Regarding the conversation that Rabbi Weiss had with [name omitted]... I was startled by how the entire matter was dismissed by the aforementioned person. The point is that one must do **something** about this, because as I wrote to you in my letter, there were several ways to approach the situation, and it was not necessarily an "absolute prohibition" as you write to me in your letter, but at the very least a strong protest or the like, or a simple prohibition, etc. Given the current climate, the precise wording of the letter from [name omitted] was less critical than the fact that it should be clear to everyone that his negative stance toward national service was absolute, even after the various lenient opinions...

As a foundation for merit, I found something I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. When he wanted to travel for a communal matter and was unable to do so due to his health, he sighed deeply and said that even when one wants to fulfill the will of the Creator, one needs a special merit for the ability to do so to be granted.

Regarding your concluding remark that since they turned the matter into politics you have ceased to be interested: regarding such a case, one might apply the saying of our Sages, "Shall he lose his world because of fools?"—asked rhetorically.

6) Regarding Chabad affairs, you are surely involving yourself in this to the best of your ability, and I am confident that in the end, *didan notzach* (ours shall be the victory). However, one must pray and act in practice as is necessary so that this happens as soon as possible, for "days are fashioned, and for Him is one of them."

7) Regarding what you write about having a small manuscript commentary on the Tanya: the copy that was in the possession of your late brother-in-law, Rabbi A. Levin of blessed memory, is not in my possession. However, I found here a *Biur Tanya* which, according to the note on it, is from Rabbi Y. Kaidaner, beginning with *Likutei Amarim* Chapter 1, etc. Although it is known that "the righteousness of the righteous and the wickedness of the wicked is in the thought, etc.," and it concludes with a commentary on Chapter 12—if this is not the one you have, I would be grateful if you could send it to me at a given time, as you suggested.

8) Regarding the *sichos* and *maamarim* printed here, the secretariat generally sends you everything that is published.

9) Thank you for the outline of the 19 Kislev *farbrengen* in the village.

10) And last but not least, I acknowledge receipt of the fifth volume of the *Talmudic Encyclopedia*. As with the previous volumes, so it is with this one—a wondrous and monumental work, wise and well-organized. Based on the aforementioned saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I see this as a great merit from Above, that a place was left for you to edit and actually publish such books, the benefit of which is immense.

While on this subject, I would like to note that not long ago I was surprised to learn that although last year—nearly a year and a half ago—they allocated aid from the *Keren Hatzalah* of Chicago in the amount of one thousand shekels for the publication of the Encyclopedia, the matter has not been brought to fruition. The obstacle is on the part of those working on the Encyclopedia, who have not provided the *Keren Hatzalah* with the details of income and expenses, etc., which they have been requesting from them for many months.

Incidentally, when I was studying in connection with one of the *farbrengens* here regarding the blessing on *mitzvos*, and I was naturally assisted by the Encyclopedia, it requires some study why the reason that one must recite the blessing *over* (before) performing them, as stated by the Rambam, is not brought there. It only cites the reason of the Ritba, even though later in the same entry it quotes the Rambam.

With blessings for success in all the above, and for long life, good and fruitful years, with peace of mind and breadth of spirit.

P.S. Since there are those who suggest that Chabad should take an important part in the campaign against the missionaries, even officially—which, of course, requires a responsible person at the helm, and the main thing is that there must be a responsible person to link Chabad with the offices in Eretz Yisrael from whom they will receive the means for this campaign—would you be so kind as to give your opinion on whether the aforementioned *avreich* is suitable for this? That is, is he organized, well-mannered, etc.? Or perhaps you have a suggestion regarding other people from Chabad circles who are suitable for this? It is also understood that it is not in Chabad's interest to compete if there are already concrete and organized activities on the part of other *chareidi* circles, but only in a way that there will be no competition or duplication of effort, of course.

## 2772

B"H, 15 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your note, in which you mention that the health of your wife, may she live and be well, has improved. May Hashem grant you the merit to share good news regarding both physical health and spiritual health—namely, the fulfillment of your mission in this world. The mission of every Jewish man and woman is to make the world a vessel for Elokus through the dissemination and support of the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah," and the "light within the Torah," which is the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs.

If this task is incumbent upon those who reside in large cities where there is a large minyan of G-d-fearing and observant Jews, then it is all the more so the duty of those who find themselves in smaller towns. They are there as unique individuals who know of the "light within the Torah" and its inner dimension, which also enlivens the revealed aspects of Torah and adds beauty to the performance of mitzvos. Certainly, you too have the opportunity to act in this regard, and naturally you are already doing so; however, we must always "increase in matters of holiness." You will surely increase your efforts in this as much as possible, for it is a presumption that a shaliach (an emissary of the Ribono shel Olam, which is the status of every Jewish man and woman) fulfills his mission.

With blessings for success in all the above.

P.S.
In a separate package, I am sending you the Tanya that was recently published for the first time in the United States, and you will surely confirm its receipt.

## 273

B"H, 19 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, pious, and diligent in the needs of the community, R' Avraham, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 9 Adar I. I was pleased to read that Hashem has granted you success and the merit to be among those who bring merit to the many, both in the beis medrash in the yeshiva and in the shul, a place of tefillah. May it be the will of Hashem that, as our Sages of blessed memory said, "The study is not the main thing, but the action," your aforementioned teachings should effect a change in the listeners regarding their actual conduct in their day-to-day lives. Since in our times one cannot rely on the listeners to draw all the conclusions from the study, it must be emphasized explicitly—meaning, from every lesson, the students should take away a practical application regarding mitzvos maasiyos or mitzvos that depend on speech and thought. And since, in order to influence others, the matters must be present within the mashpia in greater measure—so that there is enough to "moisten another" (toch al men al latpiach)—and as our Sages said, "One only urges the already diligent," you will surely also increase your own strength in your studies in the aforementioned manner: to seek out the greatness within the Talmud, for that is what leads to action. We are confident that "you have labored and you have found."

I was pleased by what you wrote regarding your plan to establish a fixed time for the study of Chassidus. This is especially true in light of what is known from the introduction to Sefer HaChinuch regarding the six constant mitzvos that apply at all times, in all places, and to every person—which are the belief in Elokus, the unity of Hashem, loving Him, and fearing Him, etc. The way to attain these, so that they are felt even in the physical heart and not merely spoken with the mouth alone (for that is not the essence of emunah, as is understood), is through the study of the teachings of Chassidus.

Regarding what you wrote about the study of Chumash, that the listeners are not satisfied with the simple explanation and that the verses should be "seasoned" in a manner appropriate for them: The commentators on Chumash are very numerous, and you will surely find those that are appropriate for the type of listeners you have. It would be appropriate for you to obtain from one of anash in Montreal the booklets of *Kriah VeKedushah*, which contain several maamarim pertaining to the weekly parsha and the haftorahs.

With blessing.

## 2474

B”H, 19 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 8 Adar, in which you ask for my opinion regarding the fact that, due to various reasons, you are unable to apply your mind to the study of Nigleh and Chassidus, and you wish to know how you should conduct yourself now:

Firstly, I do not understand your statement that you are "unable" to do so in any way, as this contradicts the words of our Sages: "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him." It is possible that what you mean is that you do not *want* to.

In any case, you should consult with your local mashpia regarding this. Explain your situation to him in detail, and may Hashem grant you success in organizing yourself in a manner that is appropriate for you, both materially and spiritually.

Secretary

## 2775

B"H, 19 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, whose work is the work of Heaven, R' Avraham Menachem Mendel, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I have received your request for a blessing of healing for one of your students, may he live, as well as your second piece of news, that the surgery was successful and all is well. May it be the will of Hashem that just as you bring good news regarding the physical results, so too may you bring good news regarding the spiritual results—namely, that your students are healthy as they should be in their spiritual lives.

Since for a Jewish person, the physical and the spiritual go hand in hand, one might say, by way of a clever observation, based on what our Alter Rebbe writes in Iggeres HaKodesh, Chapter 3, that in our generations we are not as healthy as in the earlier generations, and therefore, excessive fasting is harmful, as it may lead to illness or physical ailment, Heaven forbid—so too is it regarding the healing of the soul. If in earlier generations it was possible to suffice with a regimen of spiritual *sigufim* (ascetic practices)—that is, matters of *mussar* that humble a person and cause him distress—in our generations, this can lead to illness or ailment in the spiritual sense. That is, it may cause one to fall into excessive low spirits, or to become despondent, Heaven forbid, or it may cause the body, the *nefesh habahamit*, and the *yetzer hara* to rebel against this humiliation.

Therefore, one must hold fast to the path taught by the Baal Shem Tov, "You shall surely leave it with **him**" (*azov ta'azov imo*). This begins with the explanation that the *neshamah* is truly a part of Elokus from above, for He and His wisdom are one, and consequently, the emissary of the Supreme Man is like Him (see Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Vayikra on this). A person is granted the most sublime powers, not only to overcome obstacles but also to illuminate his soul, his body, and his portion in the world with additional light, and to create vessels for Elokus out of joy. Consequently, it is a pity to waste the time and the powers that he is not utilizing, the cause of which is the lowliness of his body, etc. And joy breaks through barriers—even the barriers of his body and his *nefesh habahamit*.

How wondrous is the precision of the ruling in the Rema, Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, section 98, end of paragraph 1, which states: "And he should think before *davening* about the exaltation of the Almighty, may He be exalted (and only afterwards) about the lowliness of man." It is well known that even the order of things in the Torah is Torah. If it is incumbent upon you to instill this order in your students, then all the more so must these matters be "moist enough to moisten" (*tofeach al menas lehatfiach*) within yourself. There is nothing that can stand before the will, even when it is necessary to change habits that have already become second nature.

With a blessing for success in all of the above.

## 2726

B"H, 19 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Adar, in which you share the good news regarding the improvement in your spiritual standing—may Hashem grant you the merit to continue increasing in this—it is certainly not the path to achieve this through fasts and self-affliction. As is also explained in the maamar *Basi L’Gani* 5713, maintaining a healthy and whole body is one of the ways of Hashem. The statement that "the strength of the body is the weakness of the soul" refers to the *nefesh hativ'is* and the *nefesh habahamish* (this is based on the *Basi L’Gani* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory). See also the *Sefer HaToldos* of the Rebbe Maharash, end of page 72...

With the blessing that your mother, may she live, should receive much Chassidishe nachas from all her children, may they live, in good health.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 2757

B"H, 20 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter asking for my opinion on whether you should travel to study at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Brooklyn, given the difficulties you are experiencing in your studies at the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Lod, and the fact that your parents wanted you to be in Jerusalem—may it be rebuilt and established—where the method of study does not satisfy you.

My opinion on this has long been known: one must study Torah and fulfill mitzvos with hiddur in the place where one is currently located. If one encounters difficulties in this, in the vast majority of cases, the primary cause is not external matters, but the yetzer hara within the person. If so, what benefit is there in traveling to another country, when the yetzer hara travels along with the person? On the contrary, the confusion of time and the distraction of the soul are increased even more by a new country and new people. You should consult with your mashpia on how to arrange for yourself the matter and method of studying Nigleh and Chassidus—whether in Lod or in Jerusalem—in a way that will enable you to fulfill the will of the Creator. Through this, you will naturally also draw down an increase in physical health, and "you have labored and you have found."

With blessings for Torah study with yiras shamayim.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

#### ***2757***

**My opinion on this has long been known:** See also letter 2792 below.

## 2778

B"H, 20 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished descendant of holy lineage, R' Shmuel Abba, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your two letters from the 8th and 25th of Shevat in one envelope, as well as your letter from the 5th of Adar. Thank you for what you wrote regarding the mezuzah, the spice box, and the silver plate. As the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished energetic *oisek b'tzorchei tzibbur*, R' P. Althaus, may he live, has conveyed to me, I am enclosing another mezuzah here in its place.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with what is explained in the Midrash regarding the difference in the relationship between Hashem and His servants, as opposed to the relationship between a master and a servant below—where below, it is the servant who must guard and attend to the affairs of his master and the master himself—above, it is written, "Hashem is your guardian, Hashem is your shade at your right hand." This is also the hint of the mezuzah: that the Name of Hashem is placed upon the doorpost between a person’s home and his possessions and the outside, guarding the person and all his affairs located within his "four cubits." It is also known that the hint of the Name written on the outside of the mezuzah is that He guards the doors of Yisrael. It is obvious that this does not refer only to a physical house, but also to a person’s domain and his spiritual affairs. Thus, may the Creator of the world guard each and every one of us, so that all our affairs and our possessions—both physical and spiritual—will be in perfection, and may each one fulfill his role in his *shlichus* in this world.

In this regard, I take the liberty of addressing what you wrote at the end of your letter concerning your life’s path for the future.

When one contemplates the world and sees that even in its inanimate parts, everything is ordered with firm laws, and everything has its place and purpose, and not a single thing is in vain—then how much more so is this true regarding a human being, who possesses intellect, and even more so regarding a member of that nation of whom it is said, "You have chosen us from all the nations." Consequently, there is no doubt or uncertainty that every single Jew has a *shlichus*, and therefore also a place in life. This is especially true for a *bar avohan* (one of noble lineage), whom the generations before him have surely endowed with special qualities.

As the saying goes, "The merit of their fathers assists them." Since *asiyah* (action) is the main thing, he will certainly be able to bring these qualities into actual practice. It is understood that it is not always easy to find the path and the matter, but we are promised, "You have labored and you have found." The very fact that a person is confident—with no doubt in his mind—that there is something to seek, and that he has been given the strengths not only to seek but also to find, brings closer, hastens, and adds success to the search and the finding.

It is unnecessary to emphasize, to one connected to Lubavitch and Chassidei Chabad, that our way is not one of moralizing—and it goes without saying that, G-d forbid, that is not my intention. Rather, it is only regarding the practical aspect: I am confident that through the appropriate search, you will find your path and your matter in which to act and influence your surroundings, which will then, in a reciprocal way, also add blessing and success to your own affairs.

With blessings for proper health and spiritual satisfaction,

[Signature]

Regarding his arrangement in the very near future.

P.S. Since your letter also touches upon the matter of the *Sefer Torah* that is in your possession, I would be grateful if you could write me some details regarding that as well.

## 2,279

B"H, 20 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Regarding your question about the location of your rented apartment: it is understood that you should endeavor for the apartment to be in close proximity to your place of work. This is not only to minimize the exertion of traveling from place to place, but also because living among those whom you influence adds strength to that influence, as is understood.

I read at the end of your letter about your study of Chassidus. It seems from the style of your writing that this study is not yet established within your soul. It appears that there is more here of the matter of "fulfilling an obligation" before others than there is a genuine interest in the study itself. And although, according to our Sages, a person should **always** study Torah, nevertheless—for one who knows the distinctions between the various modes of study: study *lishmah* (for its own sake), ordinary study, and the various modes of study *shelo lishmah* (not for its own sake)—it is certain that one must strive and exert oneself to the utmost so that one’s mode of study is on the highest level possible for one’s current standing. If this is true for the study of *Nigleh* (the revealed Torah), even though it is more connected to physical matters, then how much more so is this the case for the study of Chassidus, which is more connected to spiritual life and the path of the soul. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success in all the above, through setting fixed times for study in both the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, for the sake of your own soul.

With blessings.

## 2580

B”H, 23 Adar Rishon, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your question of whether to travel to Eretz HaKodesh (may it be rebuilt speedily in our days) or to use the money to purchase a Sefer Torah.

In my opinion, you should give the money to a Gemilas Chasadim fund. In that case, for the most part, the principal remains intact (as only a very small percentage are those who do not repay a Gemilas Chasadim loan), and this serves as an enduring zechus for the one who provides the funds. There are two ways to do this: to give the money specifically to a Gemach fund in our Holy Land (may it be rebuilt speedily in our days), or generally—meaning, for both Eretz HaKodesh and for outside the Land. If you wish, you may contribute the money to one of the Gemach funds located in my secretariat.

May Hashem grant you, and He will grant you, long and good days, so that you may be able, from time to time, to add to this Gemach fund—both from your own resources and from the funds that you will collect for this purpose from your children and friends, may they live.

With blessings.

## 2,484

2,484

B”H, 23 Adar Rishon, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Adar Rishon (which I am answering promptly, out of turn), in order to prevent the spread of rumors, etc.

You noted what is written in *Piskei Dinim* at the end, on page 69b, and you see a change there, as in previous editions it was written differently, while in the new edition the words "and it is not a response" (*ve'einah teshuvah*) have been added.

Surely you are aware—and have heard even more—of the attitude of Chassidim toward their Rebbe, the Admur, which in itself rules out any suspicion of a fundamental change here. The fact is that even in the first edition it was written "and it is not a response." I have a copy in my possession from which the new Kehot edition was photographed, as is stated in the introduction.

The incident occurred as follows, as I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: The printers in Vilna (and I did not hear clearly whether it was the typesetter, the supervisors, or the publisher) were, as is known, in a city that was a stronghold of the *misnagdim* at the time of the printing of *Piskei Dinim*. It seems this was compounded by the fact that the year 5644 was shortly after the passing of the Admur Moharash, of blessed memory, and consequently, it was a time of vulnerability during the transition between leaders. They took advantage of this opportunity to forge the text, and instead of "and it is not a response," they printed the version that you, may you be well, have transcribed. When the first copies reached Lubavitch, they took all necessary measures and reprinted the final pages with the version of the Tzemach Tzedek. It is understood that it was not possible to eradicate all the copies containing the forged version. This is the account of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

As is the way of most forgeries, the refutation is found within the text itself. Beyond the fact that it is not written in the style of the Tzemach Tzedek at all, in the continuation of the text—both before and after that passage—when the Tzemach Tzedek cites the *Rishonim*, he writes with incomparably greater breadth. It is obvious that he would not have made such a change in the same breath. You should also examine *Piskei Dinim* at the beginning, on pages 1 and 2, and the supplements to it that were printed in *She'eilos U'Teshuvos Tzemach Tzedek, Shaar HaMiluim* (Kehot edition), which were copied from the original booklets; there, the Tzemach Tzedek cites the words of the Gra, and you will see his style in this regard.

With blessings.

#### ***2,484***

Printed in the notes at the end of *Tzemach Tzedek, Shaar HaMiluim*, Vol. 4, p. 308, and completed based on a manuscript copy.

## 2788

2788

B"H, 26 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Nosson Menachem, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure your Haggadah Shel Pesach, which includes translations into Yiddish and English, as well as a collection of customs, reasons, and laws. Because of the importance of the matter, I went through the pages as time permitted. I have noted some comments in the margins. May Hashem grant you success in illuminating your surroundings with the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah," and with the "light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus—and especially with what is most necessary in our generation and in this country: the laws and customs of kosher Jewish life.

With respect and blessings for success in all the above.

P.S.
Surely, if you have any other books, please send them to my library as well, and I thank you in advance. In a separate package, I am sending you the Kehot-published Haggadah Shel Pesach, which includes a collection of reasons and customs.

**Notes:**

Page 10 (and the corresponding place in the English translation): [You wrote] that firstborns, Kohanim, and Leviim do not fast on Erev Pesach. This requires further study regarding the source for this. In any case, the halachic ruling is that they do fast, as explained in the Maharil and cited by the Acharonim in their place, Siman 470. To prevent a stumbling block, it would have been worthwhile to correct this by deleting those words.

Pages 15 and 16 in the Yiddish and English translations: Regarding the words "v'lehevi hefker k'afra d'ara." Since there are those who recite it in Yiddish and English rather than in the original Aramaic text, it is necessary to also include a translation of the word "hefker," not just the words "k'afra d'ara," as this is the essential point, as is understood.

Page 19, where the text of Kiddush begins with "Vayehi Erev": Although there are some who follow this custom, the vast majority of communities do not. In any case, it would have been appropriate to place this in parentheses.

Page 29, [where it says] that Rabbi Eliezer was a Kohen: This appears to be a printing error; see the introduction of the Radal to Pirkei D'Rabbi Eliezer. It should say "Rabbi Elazar."

Page 84, where you brought "Shir HaMaalos" instead of the Psalm "LiVnei Korach": This requires further study.

**R' Nosson Menachem:** Mandel. Another letter to him appears later in 2753. See there for the context of the letter before us.
