## B'Tetzai

B"H, 26 Adar Rishon, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In continuation of our conversation when you visited here, I would like to emphasize once again that in addition to the fact that every Jewish man and woman is a shaliach of the Ribono shel Olam to add light to their surroundings, this is all the more true for those who have merited to have a special influence, and from whose deeds and conduct others learn. Beyond the merit of having influence, Hashem Yisbarach also grants them special strengths and capabilities to succeed in their shlichus—the shlichus of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He.

Consequently, this is both a very great responsibility and a very great merit.

And since the Ribono shel Olam is *etzem hatov* (the essence of goodness) and rewards everyone in full, the more one exerts oneself and is **proactive** in the fulfillment of one’s shlichus, so too does Hashem Yisbarach grant them their reward, and all the sooner. And since one must rely on the *chasadim* of Hashem every single day, the sooner one fulfills the shlichus of Hashem, the more one adds to the *bracha* and *hatzlacha* that everyone requires.

I hope that the conversation we had is sufficient in itself. Nevertheless, I am writing these lines to ease the *nisayon* and the difficulties you perceive, and with an additional blessing: that you should succeed as soon as possible in realizing everything we spoke about while you were here. Hashem Yisbarach is certain to fulfill His promise to bestow upon you, your husband, and your children *shichyu*, everything you all need in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*, and as soon as possible as well. I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding all of this.

With blessings.

## 2,792

2,792

By the Grace of Hashem, 28 Adar, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from some time ago, in which you write that you are not satisfied with certain details regarding the conduct of the yeshiva, and in your opinion, these details interfere with your *hasmadah* (diligence) in learning as it should be, as well as with your *davening*.

Consequently, you have the idea of traveling to the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). You ask for my opinion on this matter.

It is unnecessary to elaborate on what is well-known and simple: that the things which disturb one’s Torah, *avodah*, or *gemilus chasadim* are caused by the "leaven in the dough"—that is, the *yetzer hara*—which confuses a person in many ways and manners. For even though it is called a "fool," regarding its *avodah*, it is an expert craftsman.

As is known from the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: the *yetzer hara* approaches each and every person with arguments tailored to the specific nature of that individual’s soul, to the point that it sometimes even cloaks itself in the mantle of a *tzurba meirabanan* (a Torah scholar), a G-d-fearing person, and so on. Therefore, each and every person must examine very, very carefully the thoughts that occur to them regarding changes in their *avodah* of Hashem, and know who is presenting these arguments—whether they are from the "right side" or the "left side." You are surely aware of the story regarding the *tzaddik* of Chernobyl, which was printed in the *sicha* of Pesach 5703. One of the tests in this regard is whether the change will lead to a neglect of Torah and *avodah* or not.

In your specific case, since you are in a yeshiva that was founded by the *tzaddikim*, the *nesi'im* (leaders) of the generation, and is conducted in their spirit—namely, the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim*—it is highly probable, even without knowing the specific details, that learning there involves great benefit. Consequently, it is also understood that the *yetzer hara* is rising up against this with various types of schemes to disrupt and confuse you, so that you do not conduct yourself in accordance with the requirements of the yeshiva in all details.

It is also understood that if the *yetzer hara* were to reveal its true intention—that it does not want to let you be diligent in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus—you would certainly not listen to it. Consistent with what is stated, "And the serpent was cunning," it comes with guile, suggesting that, on the contrary, the yeshiva is what is distracting you from diligence in Torah and from matters of *avodah* of Hashem with *yiras shamayim* as it should be. In this way, it hopes that its arguments will be accepted, and it will distract you from Torah and *davening*. And even though the *yetzer hara* must promise you that if you go to a different yeshiva, it will not distract you and you will be able to be diligent in Torah and meticulous in *davening*, the *yetzer hara* is confident that since you listened to its voice at the beginning—and "all beginnings are difficult"—it will certainly find a way afterward to draw you even further into its net.

For man has been given free choice, and two paths are before him, as the verse says, "See, I have set before you today life and good, etc." But together with this, man is given special assistance to choose the good, as the verse says, "Therefore choose life." Certainly, in your case as well, even though the *yetzer hara* is extremely cunning, you have been given the strength to nullify all of its arguments and to exert yourself with *mesiras nefesh* by completely turning your attention away from the distracting arguments—that the environment is not suitable for you, and that everyone else is to blame for your neglect of Torah and *davening*, and not yourself, etc., etc.

It is also understood that among your peers in the yeshiva, there are several matters that require correction, for there is nothing perfectly complete except for the Holy One, Blessed be He, the Creator of the world. But the advice for this is that you should influence your peers to correct their matters, rather than you being influenced by them. This is also a *segulah* (remedy) for your own shortcomings to be corrected through your peers, as is stated and explained regarding the concept that "all of Israel are responsible for one another," that they are one complete stature, and there is a quality in one that is not in the other, and through *ahavas Yisrael*, each one completes the other.

The conclusion of all the above is that you should turn your attention away from thoughts that distract from Torah and *avodah*, and **immerse** yourself in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, and in the *avodah* of *davening* as it should be, in accordance with the yeshiva’s order and requirements. Then, the promise of our Sages will be fulfilled in you: "If you have labored—then you will have found."

You do not mention whether regarding your friend... who is also being confused by these same arguments that you write about regarding your own situation. If that is the case, it is understood that the above response applies to him as well.

With blessings for success in the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim*.

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

## 2,496

B"H, 29 Adar Rishon, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos, in which you write that your financial situation is not as it was previously, having diminished since then.

It is well known that the Ribono shel Olam says, "Test Me now with this" [Malachi 3:10] — referring to the matter of tzedakah, that one should tithe so that he may become wealthy. It is also known that regarding tzedakah, the Sages said, "According to the camel is the load" [Sotah 13b] — meaning that the burden is commensurate with one's capacity. Consequently, what is the wonder if, when one is not careful regarding the matter of tzedakah as required—which is at the very least a tithe, and preferably more—the financial situation diminishes as a result?

However, on the other hand, from this very fact it is known that the matter is in his own hands. For if he immediately increases his tzedakah as mentioned above, and even more so, the Ribono shel Olam is certainly bound to fulfill His promise, as stated.

Yet, since in every matter one requires Siyata Dishmaya, one must establish a set time for the study of Nigleh and Chassidus, in addition to the three daily study portions that are equal for every soul, as instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—the Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, as is well known.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success to report good news regarding all of the above, and may it be His will that this happens soon.

With blessings.

## 2,797

[Adar 5714]

...As for me, having seen about three hundred of these letters in the possession of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (some of which were not authorized for publication), I can say that, on the contrary, there is no doubt that the content is authentic. (Unless one believes that the simplest explanation of an event is a miracle completely outside the laws of nature; such a person could also believe that, by a miracle, there happened to be someone in Odessa who could forge, fabricate, and write 300 such letters, and then disappear into thin air.) When Hashem wills it and I have more free time, it is my intention to publish once again all the letters that were printed in *HaTamim*, with the addition of the letters that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, authorized for publication at the time, but whose printing in *HaTamim* was interrupted. As an introduction to them, I intend to explain the reasons and arguments that compel my aforementioned conclusion. I will cite here only two points:

a) It is known to all those who were present at the time the letters from the *genizah* appeared in southern Russia—namely, in the vicinity of Odessa and Kherson—including the prominent figures, and especially those who had knowledge of the history of Chassidus and its teachings, that there was not a single person among them who was capable or even able to write such letters out of thin air.

b) To obtain at that time—given the great confusion between countries and the state of emergency regarding communication between one country and another—parchment such as that upon which the letters were written was almost an impossibility.

Most of the difficulties raised by those who doubt the authenticity of the letters are based on the fact that they found several contradictions in the dates of the letters, etc. That is to say, these are errors involving, for the most part, only a single letter or word, and sometimes the omission of words, etc. Now, anyone who has ever engaged in copying letters—especially when done in haste (unfortunately, I know this from the fact that I proofread a significant portion of the *maamarim* and books published by our publishing house)—knows that even with a good copyist, at least 5 percent of the lines contain errors after the first transcription, requiring proofreading a second and third time. And as mentioned, this is with the best of copyists.

On the other hand, a forger who wants to forge and subsequently sell the letters to one of the Rebbes' courts—that is, to those who have knowledge of the history of Chassidus and its teachings—would certainly be precise and proofread many times, because he would fear that if such errors were found, his shame would be revealed in public and he would lose his entire business. Therefore, the existence of these errors (after we subtract those added by the typesetter of *HaTamim*) is, on the contrary, proof that the letters were not written by a forger who wanted to sell them for full price to experts in this field, for whom extreme caution would have been required. Rather, they were written by a copyist for people who had no knowledge beyond the external appearance of the letters. This is further proof for the conclusion of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which he apparently heard from his father, the Rebbe: a) The content is undoubtedly authentic. b) They were copied from the handwriting of those who had a hand and a name, and **deep** knowledge, in the teachings of Chassidus and also Kabbalah.

One more point, which in my opinion also confirms the conclusion of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is this: Anyone who saw these hundreds of letters all at once—which is **how** they were brought for sale to the representative of Lubavitch—would have had no room at all for the opinion that this was the **original** handwriting, because in **all of them**, the script and the parchment were similar in **every** detail. A forger who wanted to carry out a forgery in such a way could only hope to find a buyer among those who lack a sense of criticism and simple common sense.

In addition to the above, among the letters that were not published, there were *kameios*, letters with *tagin*, and various vowel points. As I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, there were found within them—as well as in the letters that were published—matters that were not known to the public, but were transmitted by tradition, master from master, from the Alter Rebbe down to the Rebbe, the father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

I have not come here to present anything more than general points, but in my opinion, they are sufficient not only to refute the arguments in the aforementioned article and those preceding it, but also to compel a conclusion that is completely opposite and far more acceptable:

It is a clear fact that the Rebbe of Ruzhin, *ztz"l*, was imprisoned. (For the time being, "scientific" researchers have not yet been found to deny this, although there is a well-known and famous researcher in Poland who reached the "absolute scientific conclusion" that the Baal Shem Tov never existed). In a harsh imprisonment such as this, the writings found in the possession of the prisoner would be confiscated. The Rebbe of Ruzhin certainly possessed original manuscripts of his contemporaries and the generations preceding him, as well as books and objects dear to him, as they had come to him by inheritance and the like—whether few or many. Certainly, when the Rebbe found himself in a secure place, he wanted and sought ways to receive the aforementioned writings, etc., back. It is clear that he could not obtain them through open petitioning to the government, since he had fled his imprisonment—so only the path of secret methods remained. If those acting on his behalf succeeded in bribing the officials involved in some way, what would the officials have done to settle the matter and minimize, at the very least, the possibility that the **government investigators** would discover the return of the writings to their owners? The simplest thing—to place in their stead letters that, at least in their external appearance, their number, etc., would correspond to the original manuscripts that were taken. It is understood that they could not do all this with complete leisure, over a long period of time, etc., and therefore there was no room for precise proofreading, nor did they see a necessity for it, since the exchangers and the critics they feared understood Russian better than Chassidus. It is also understood that the copying of the letters was done on parchment or paper of the time of the exchange, not of the time of the writing, especially since in that era they did not know about the possibilities of examining parchment to determine when it was processed.

**M. Schneerson**

## 2,499

May Hashem Yisbarach help you to be able to realize all of the above in your daily life.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

## 2500

B"H, 2 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Yehuda Leib, may he live:

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated March 5th. It is surprising that in your letter you do not mention anything regarding your good works in spreading Torah and Yiddishkeit in your surroundings, which you are surely doing, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages that "there is a presumption that a shaliach performs his mission." Every Jew is a shaliach of the "Supreme Person who sits on the Throne," as it were, as explained in Likutei Torah at the beginning of Parshas Vayikra.

It is understood that in the fulfillment of this mission, there are various obstacles and hindrances arising from the nature of the world and the personal share of each individual. However, there is the advice offered by our Sages that "joy breaks through barriers"—the joy of a mitzvah, both in the performance of actual mitzvos and in the general instruction which is a great principle in the Torah: "In all your ways, know Him." And this is notwithstanding what the Rambam writes at the end of Hilchos Lulav regarding the nature of this joy. These days, the days of Adar, are especially conducive to this, as we "increase in joy," and especially in a leap year, when we are stringent (as per the ruling of the Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, siman 685, se'if 7) to increase in joy in both Adar I and Adar II.

With regards to your son, may he live, and with blessings.

P.S.
In a separate package, I am sending you the Tanya that was recently published for the first time in the United States.

## 2712

2712

B”H, 3 Adar [Shabbos], 5714

Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, learned in Torah and fear of Heaven, meticulous in his mitzvah observance, wise and understanding, renowned for his accomplishments, etc.,
Rabbi Aharon Chaim HaLevi, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the two books, *Machaneh Ephraim* and *Binyan Halacha*. Many thanks for this gift. I trust that you will continue to do so in the future by sending the publications you oversee to the library; thank you in advance.

As a token of appreciation, I have added a few notes in the margins, written in haste between the pages of the books.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant each and every one of us the merit to be builders of a dwelling place for the Kudsha Brich Hu and His Shechinah, and to occupy ourselves with Torah, tefillah, and teshuvah (as our Sages of blessed memory state: *Shabbos 114a*; *Tikkunei Zohar* in the introduction at the beginning: "They make a dwelling for the Kudsha Brich Hu"; *Bechoros 44b*; *Devarim Rabbah* 3:6; *Kiddushin 40a*; *Zohar Bereishis 26b*: "through which one fulfills the mitzvah of *pru u’rvu*").

With respect and blessings for success.

P.S.

**Binyan Halacha, at the beginning. Page 1a.** "Words that were transmitted orally, you are not permitted to recite from a written text." Regarding the general matter, see the cross-references in *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*, siman 49 (it is noteworthy that it is not cited in *Ein Mishpat* in the Gemara there), and see what is written and discussed in *Sdei Chemed*, *Kelalim* 4, 44; *Pe'as HaSadeh* 4, 4 and 22; *Orchos Chaim* to siman 49.

**Page 1b.** Regarding the source in the *sugya* of *Taanis*: The interpretation requires study, for on the contrary, it is proven there that it is permitted to recite [Torah] in public. As the language of the Gemara states: "Is it only an individual...? Rather, **all of them** enter and read." One must therefore conclude that the prohibition is because one person reads while the others listen (as he fulfills the obligation for others). This is the literal meaning of the *Sefer Mitzvos Gadol* (Smag), which he brings later. This is also the ruling of our Rebbe HaZaken in *Shulchan Aruch*, siman 49. See the *Magen Avraham* and *Machatzis HaShekel* there.

**Page 1c.** The reason for the prohibition is because it must be [recited] as it was given. See *Responsa Radbaz*, Vol. 4, siman 1,105.

It is worth noting—regarding the laws of *Krias HaTorah* in this context—*Zichron Chaim*, 116a, and there.

***

Regarding what is written and explained in *Binyan Halacha*—that there is no distinction in the aforementioned prohibitions between *Krias HaTorah* and *Talmud Torah* in public—there are still points that require study: 1) Why were these laws not brought in the Rambam regarding *Talmud Torah* in public? It is obvious that one cannot rely on what he wrote in the introduction to his book (which is merely a narrative, not a legal ruling), or in *Moreh Nevuchim*. 2) How did they permit the **prohibition**—according to Rambam, *Hilchos Tefillah* 12:5—in the reading of the Kohen Gadol, which is only on the Tenth [of Tishrei], on Yom Kippur? 3) The permissibility of reading the *Megillah* while sitting, even though *Talmud Torah* in public must be done while standing according to this reasoning, as stated in the *Yerushalmi* regarding this very *Mishnah*. Surely the *Megillah* is no less significant than the Oral Torah, which must be recited with awe, etc. Furthermore, and most importantly, from where is it derived to innovate that according to the Rambam these prohibitions exist for *Talmud Torah* in public?

In my opinion, we have nothing regarding the Rambam’s view other than what is explicitly stated: that in *Krias HaTorah* it is forbidden to read [the Torah] not from a written text, and likewise, that in *Krias HaTorah* it is forbidden to translate from a written text—as per the *Yerushalmi*. The Rambam holds that the *Yerushalmi* explains the words of the *Bavli* regarding this (as is also written in *Binyan Halacha*)—see *Tosafos* s.v. *Veha’amar*, *Yoma* 87b; *Targum Yonasan* s.v. *HaMelech*, *Yoma* 79a; and what is discussed in *Sdei Chemed*, *Kelalei HaPoskim* 7, subsection 1. Or, that it disagrees with the *Bavli* [and nevertheless], the *halacha* follows the *Yerushalmi*, since the *Stam Mishnah* in *Yoma* (68b)—that he reads only on the Tenth [of Tishrei] by heart—proves that it is not like the *Bavli* in *Gittin* (60b).

The unique status of *Krias HaTorah* can be explained in several ways. One of them is that it is an obligation of the community, not the individual (as per the reasoning of the *Milchamos* on *Megillah*, Chapter 1, s.v. *Ve’od Amar*; see *Tzafnas Paneach* to *Hilchos Tefillah* 12:5), unlike the reading of the *Megillah* (which is why it is permitted while sitting as well; the prohibition against reading it by heart is due to a specific derivation), and unlike the *Krias HaTorah* of the Kohen Gadol, which is a necessity of his service (*Yoma*, ibid.).

Were I not afraid, I would say that the entire reading of the *Korbanos*—on Yom Tov, Rosh Hashanah, and Yom Kippur—is distinct in this regard from other *Krias HaTorah* (see *Tosafos Megillah* 30b; the commentary of the *Riva* in *Targum Yonasan Yoma* 70a), except that in a place where it is possible and common, they did not differentiate in its laws due to the principle of *lo plug* (they did not make distinctions), unlike the reading of the Kohen Gadol.

***

It still requires explanation: if so, why was the Oral Torah not written down by our Sages of blessed memory? The gates of explanation are not locked: even though there is no prohibition in the matter, they did not write it down 1) because of the view of the *Bavli*—if one were to say that it disagrees with the *Yerushalmi*. 2) Because of "I will write for him the majority of My Torah," etc.—in *Gittin*, ibid. 3) For the reason brought in *Moreh Nevuchim*, Part 1, Chapter 71, and more. See also *Zohar*, Part 1, 253a; *Likkutei Torah* by our Rebbe HaZaken, *Derushim* for Sukkos, 80b.

In his notes, *Ha'aros Chaim* (14a), regarding what he cited from the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Admur concerning ownership in the context of the prohibition of *nissuch* (libations): I received the *Responsa Chesed Yehoshua* (N.Y., 5713), and there is a discussion there in section 23. There are points to be noted in their words, but time does not permit.

#### 2712

**Rabbi Aharon Chaim HaLevi:** Zimmerman.

## 2,503

B"H, 6 Adar Rishon, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I was pleased with the program of teshuvah provided for the avreich... He did well not to force him to memorize all of Iggeres HaTeshuvah, so as not to give the impression that this is merely an exercise in studying Chassidus and nothing more. Regarding the caution required in this matter in general...

It is impossible to set hard and fast rules, as it depends on the nature of the individuals involved. Great caution is needed, for even protest and emphasis are not always desirable; as is known, diverting one’s attention from these matters as much as possible is best. Nevertheless, from time to time, one must emphasize the reprehensibility of the matter and how it causes one to "descend from a high roof to a deep pit," and even further, as explained in the beginning of the Tzemach Tzedek’s Sefer HaMitzvos. Regarding the aforementioned suspicion, this is underscored by the severity of the punishment mentioned in the Torah Shebichtav in many places. One should season these matters by explaining the magnitude of the punishment, considering that the neshamah is literally a "part of Elokus from above," and "a person’s agent (the Supernal one upon the Throne) is like himself," as explained in Likutei Torah at the beginning of Parshas Vayikra. Consequently, nothing should prevent him from fulfilling his mission, etc., and the magnitude of the fall is understood when he does not utilize his powers, and even more so when he uses them for the opposite, etc.

Regarding what you wrote about the publication of the maamarim and sichos, etc., this is tied to an immense burden that necessitates setting aside interest in other matters. Since I am currently occupied with the publication of the maamarim from the year 5704, which have already been prepared for print and only lack editing and references, etc., and after that [will come] Sefer HaMaamarim 5701, etc., naturally, one matter hinders the other...

## 2549

## 2507

B"H, 7 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Heaven forbid that anyone should be satisfied with what has already been achieved through the field of chinuch, especially in accordance with the instruction of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that in matters pertaining to Torah and its mitzvos, any achievement—even the greatest one—must awaken an increased appetite to accomplish more and more. And all the more so: if such results were achieved through minor effort, how much more so would have been accomplished had the effort been as it should have been.

On the other hand, even the smallest achievement must add courage to the continuation of the avodah. And likewise, all the more so: if, even when acting with ulterior motives, one still overcame the concealments and obstructions whose source is the sin of the golden calf, and a ray of light shone forth, then surely, siyata d'shmaya is guaranteed, and "one who comes to purify himself is assisted," etc.

With blessings for proper health and for success in the chinuch of the sons and daughters of Yisrael, in yiras shamayim and in the study of our holy Torah.

#### ***2507***

**And all the more so:** See also above, letter 2299.

## 2508

B"H, 7 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Your letter from Parshas Vayikra has been received. It is surprising that you write about matters concerning the house and other physical affairs, yet mention nothing about your participation in learning, your participation in Chassidishe farbrengens, and the like—which are the only channels through which one receives bracha and hatzlacha in the things one needs. When these channels are in order, then there is room to wonder why the hashpaah is not as one desires; but when one only looks out for the hashpaah without paying attention to the channels, what is the wonder in that?!

It goes without saying that the point here is not to write about this, but rather that the main thing should be the actual deed—to increase strength in Torah and mitzvos as our holy Torah demands. For then, Hashem gives, and will certainly increase, bracha and hatzlacha.

Regarding the money you have received for Hachnasas Kallah, you may send it through my secretariat. However, it is necessary to know for which kallah this is, for in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) there are many who are in need of this, and then it will be sent in an appropriate manner.

With blessings.

## 2509

B"H, 9 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Adar I.

It would be best if the sofer himself writes to me regarding how he found them, as I suspect there may be some concern with them—perhaps in the batim, etc. Please ask the sofer who checks them to write to me personally about this, as mentioned above.

As for your concluding question regarding what your reward will be: the reward in this is that you will increase the drawing of the hearts of Jewish sons and daughters toward the service of the Almighty, specifically through ways of closeness and ahavas Yisrael. With appropriate effort, you will surely find the ways to achieve this. It would be excellent if, whenever possible, you invite a guest to eat in your home from time to time, as the mitzvah of hachnasas orchim is a special segulah for children.

With blessings for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires and those of your wife, may you both live for the good.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 2510

B"H, 9 Adar II, 5714

Greetings and blessings!

I was alarmed by the news that your health has not been as it should be for several weeks now. It is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, your condition will have already improved and you will be able to inform me of this yourself, for in all matters of mitzvos, "it is a mitzvah to perform it oneself more than through a messenger," and having a healthy and whole body is one of the ways of Hashem.

The simple faith of every Jewish man and woman compels one to believe that only the Ribono shel Olam is the sole Master of the entire world and all that fills it, which includes this physical world and every individual man and woman. And since the Eibishter is the essence of goodness, He certainly desires to bestow only good and kindness upon every individual, of which physical health is one of the foundations, as explained in the Rambam, Hilchos Deios, end of chapter 3 and beginning of chapter 4. Also well-known is the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse, "If you see the donkey of one who hates you crouching under its burden... you shall surely help him," which was explained in the maamar of 10 Shevat 5713.

When one feels (not just knows) all of the above, the soul is naturally permeated with an inner tranquility that brings with it an immediate improvement in health and a speedy recovery. May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success in bringing good news regarding all of the above, and may it be His will that this happens as soon as possible.

Awaiting good news.

## 2513

For although the value of davening in the nusach of the AriZal and our Rebbe (the Alter Rebbe) is great, "Hashem loves the gates of Zion," and as our Sages have said, there must also be a place for Torah...

With blessings for a complete and speedy recovery and with thanks in advance for the aforementioned.

## 2515

B”H, 11 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and diligent in communal affairs,
Rabbi Betzalel, may he be a shaliach,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 3rd, 7th, and 12th of Adar II, along with the enclosures, and the check for 750... has also been received.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the purchase of the building for the Yeshiva: I was pleased that you have set your sights high (*geשטעלט ברייט*), and consequently, you must continue in this with a similar breadth of vision. This makes a positive impression on the *baalei batim*, and they too will see that, as our Sages of blessed memory stated, gold was created only for the sake of the Beis HaMikdash. The magnitude of the spiritual advantage—namely, the development of the Yeshiva—is understood simply.

You must strengthen the hands of all those involved in this with enthusiasm, so that it should not be in the manner mentioned in *Likutei Torah*, *Vayikra*, at the beginning, regarding *is'arusa d'le'eila* (an arousal from Above) and "a man who sows first," etc. Rather, it should come into actual, tangible reality, and the Yeshiva should develop with outstanding success, increasing in quantity, and in the course of time, in quality as well.

Surely you have heard the story of what the students of the Maggid used to say about our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe—*a Litvak vil iberzaylen* (a Litvak wants to recount it). But in any event, after that, there should be no room for doubt or hesitation...

As for the upcoming days of Purim, may it be the will of Hashem that there be joy *ad d'lo yada* (until one does not know), which comes about through *l'vusumei b'yaina* (becoming intoxicated with wine), for this is the teaching of Chassidus, and may this be drawn down throughout the entire year.

With blessings.

Regarding your inquiry concerning what is written in the *Kol Bo* (end of section 122), here is the text (with additional explanation in brackets): To know the calculation of a person’s [years] in his soul (by way of a riddle and *gematria*, without revealing it explicitly), take... for every remainder of thirds (after you discard the thirds), count [for each of them] 70...

From the fifths (the explanation is as above), add [instead of each one] 21... from the sevenths, add [instead of each one] 15, and from the entire total, subtract [all the] 105s (this is the correct reading, not "take"), and the remainder is the calculated number.

Riddles such as these were common in the Middle Ages, and even now among *yeshiva bochurim*. It is also worth noting the statement of our Sages in *Megillah* (23a): "Three, five, seven—against whom...?"

B"H, 11 Adar II, 5714

Furthermore, just as the giving of tzedakah is a segulah for this very thing, the recitation of Tehillim is also effective. ## 2517

B"H, 11 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters from the 26th of Adar Rishon and the 6th of Adar Sheni: Thank you for informing me of the improvement in your health. Surely you are also taking care of your physical health in a material sense, as is explained in many places in Chassidus, that one must "surely leave it with him" (*az der guf zol zein a gezunter* — so that the body should be healthy); consequently, it will be easier to influence him so that he does not cause distractions, and on the contrary, he will assist in the *avodas haborei*, especially as the Baal Shem Tov desired — that it be with *simcha*.

... It is understood that I am in great pain over the magnitude of the *he'elem* and *hester* (concealment). For when we see even with physical eyes that the external *he'elem* and *hester* are steadily diminishing — and on the contrary, this is an opportune time to expand their borders with students from various circles, including those from the "true *chutzah*" (outside) among them, initially increasing the quantity of students, and in time they will surely grow in quality as well — yet the internal *he'elem* and *hester* are growing and increasing, concerning matters that even the *nefesh habahamit* understands to be trivialities.

As I have already written many times, there is enough work for everyone, and enough true honor — and even imagined honor — for everyone. Despite all this, everyone pulls to their own side, and decisions and rationalizations change and flip from one extreme to the other very frequently.

This is similar to what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, said in one of his *sichos*: "Soon a time will come when one will grab his head [in regret], realizing that a short time before, there was a *geshmake avodah* (delightful work) available, and one did not utilize the opportunity." Although the explicit context was regarding the *Geulah Shleimah*, when people will regret not having utilized the opportunity of the time of *galus*, this applies — *b'ze'er anpin* (in miniature) — to everyone during the time of *galus*. Since many matters are being revealed by removing the *he'elem* and *hester* from them, this entire matter and the aforementioned grievances are relevant to this detail.

... Regarding the teachers — one should explain to them that they are working in the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h nebag"m zya*. Consequently, even if we assume they are correct in their grievances against this person or that person, that is no reason for them to punish **themselves** by diminishing their own merit and success, even in their personal affairs, through their reduced participation in the aforementioned institutions. You will surely find the appropriate words for this.

It is self-understood that I do not mean to say that *zai darfen oisgerissen veren* (they should be uprooted), *chas v'shalom*. On the contrary, we have seen recently the magnitude of the influence through the awakening of mercy of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, which he grants to those who participate in his affairs — not only in spirituality but also in materiality, materiality in the literal sense, as is evident to the senses.

My intention in the above is that you explain to them that their entire approach is not true; they view the matter as if it belongs to this person or that person, and therefore they must wage war with them. And if so, what do they have to do with this matter? They should look for a better place. This is not true at all.

The reality is that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, placed them on the "beautiful portion," both regarding material matters and spiritual matters, and he says to them, "Choose in this," as it is written, "And you shall choose life." Further elaboration on this is superfluous.

... May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success in bringing good news regarding all of the above. Surely you will create *an shturem* (a stir) with this, but with *hisyashvus* (settledness) in the *keilim* (vessels) — meaning that it should also be settled in the vessel of the recipient and the influenced, for then it will be a lasting thing.

With blessings for a *Purim sameach* to you and to your entire family, may they live, in true health,

**M. Schneerson**

## 2518

B"H, 12 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and scion of a noble lineage, the descendant of holy ancestors, our friend Rabbi Avraham, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of the 23rd of Adar, in which you write regarding the visit to the summer camp of the esteemed Chossid, a man of many accomplishments and great energy who achieves great things, etc., Rabbi Shimon Yaakobovitch, may he live. You mention that he delivered a lecture in his shul and beis medrash, and that the listeners were well satisfied. Consequently, it is to be hoped that these words will enter their hearts, and thereby the promise of the verse will also be fulfilled: "The matter is very close to you, in your mouth and in your heart, to do it" (Devarim 30:14). May Hashem grant each and every one of us the merit to fulfill our mission in this world, for every Jewish person is, as it were, a shaliach of the "Man above upon the throne," as explained in Likutei Torah (by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Shulchan Aruch and Tanya) at the beginning of Parshas Vayikra.

It is understood that in fulfilling this mission, there are various obstacles and hindrances arising from the nature of the world and the personal portion of each individual. However, there is the advice offered by our Sages regarding this: "Joy breaks through barriers"—the joy of a mitzvah, both in the performance of actual mitzvos and in the general instruction that is a "great principle of the Torah": "In all your ways, know Him" (Mishlei 3:6). Even so, the words of the Rambam at the end of Hilchos Lulav regarding joy apply. These days are especially conducive to this—the days of Adar, when we increase in joy, and especially in a leap year, when we are stringent (as per the ruling of the Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim 688:7) to increase in joy in both Adar Rishon and Adar Sheni.

With respect and with wishes for a joyous Purim.

#### ***2518***

**Rabbi Avraham:** Abuchatzeira, Yavne.

## 2,519

B"H, 12 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks the date of writing—in which you write once again regarding the rationale for leaving here: It is surprising, considering that you see the success of the Ribono shel Olam in your avodah in your current location, and you also see that there is no one else to do what you are doing. Since all of this is a tangible indication that you have found the purpose of your shlichus in this world during these months, why must you seek advice and ways to abandon your shlichus and travel to other places?

This is especially true based on what is explained in the sicha of 19 Kislev 5664 regarding the confusion of avodah when one thinks about a different task while in the midst of one's current work. It was also explained at the farbrengen here regarding the precise phrasing of "foreign thoughts" (*machshavos zaros*): it does not necessarily mean idle thoughts, and certainly not forbidden thoughts; rather, since the thought is "foreign" to this particular place, it confuses the entire avodah. This is especially so since every Jew is called a "holy nation," and it is known how much thought affects holy matters (*kodshim*).

Consequently, you should perform your avodah in your current location with great joy that you have merited to be a channel through which there is drawn down and added to the matters of "a mitzvah is a candle and Torah is light," and the "light" of Torah—which is the Torah of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs. In the course of time, it is not impossible that you may also be able to travel to a better place, but not in the current situation, where several large and important matters are still in the stage of development. Further elaboration on this is superfluous.

I await good news regarding this, and in general regarding what is happening with anash and their affairs,

**M. Schneerson**

2,519

In the sicha: Toras Shalom, p. 39.

## 2520

B.H., 12 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Jewish women and daughters, and to the Nashi U’Bnos Chabad in particular, may Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

In the coming days that connect Purim with Pesach, every Jewish woman and daughter should reflect upon the significant role that the Jewish woman played in these Yomim Tovim, and what we must learn from them.

The Yom Tov of Purim, as well as the Yom Tov of Pesach, obligate the Jewish woman to observe the special mitzvos associated with these Yomim Tovim (such as Megillah, Haggadah, etc.), because the Jewish woman had a special merit and share in the miracles that occurred "in those days, at this time."

The Megillah (Megillas Esther) tells us clearly how Esther helped bring about the great miracle for Klal Yisrael, and the fast before Purim and the Megillah itself are named after her.

Regarding the great merits of the Jewish women in connection with Pesach, *zeman cheiruseinu*, the Midrash speaks at length. In those difficult times of the Galus Mitzrayim, it was the Jewish women who maintained the courage and bitachon of the men and raised generations of loyal Jews, who merited to receive the Torah at Mount Sinai and the eternal inheritance, our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days.

The manner in which the Jewish women and daughters contributed to the great miracles of these mentioned Yomim Tovim was not the same:

In the case of Pesach, the influence and impact of the women was directed primarily toward the home—*kol kevudah bas melech penimah*—through tzniyus and family life.

In the case of Purim, it was required that the Jewish woman, according to the demands and precise instructions of the gedolei haTorah v’hayirah, utilize her position and influence to the fullest extent entirely for the benefit of her people, and she did so with actual mesiras nefesh, risking her life for the sake of the survival of our people.

These two Yomim Tovim—Purim and Pesach—are eternal witnesses that the Jewish woman, whether at home or outside when circumstances demand it, is devoted heart and soul to Torah and mitzvos, taharas hamishpachah, and the kosher chinuch of the children—the very foundations of the survival and Geulah of our people.

Jewish women and daughters! Follow the example of the nashim tzidkaniyos of all generations, for upon you and in your hands lies, to a great extent, the fate of our people.

And when one truly commits to fulfilling these Divine obligations, the Ribono shel Olam helps, just as He helped Esther, and all difficulties vanish, and He sends His Divine blessings in *bnei, chayei, u’mezonei revichei*, and in all good, both physical and spiritual.

With blessings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 2521

B"H, 12 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter of the 9th of Adar Sheni. I was pleased with the first half of your letter, in which I see that you have correctly grasped the content of my letter to the N'shei Chabad in... and, most importantly, that you have translated this into *maaseh b'poel*—conducting yourself as a Jewish daughter in general, and a Chassidic woman in particular, should conduct herself. Hashem will surely fulfill His promise that this will add blessing and success in all that you require.

In connection with this, I am particularly surprised by the second half of your letter, in which you write that you are overthinking your current condition, now that you are in a delicate state, etc.

In general, every one of our generation who has merited to be saved by Hashem—and especially those who have witnessed actual miracles, where Hashem led them out of the previous country, guided them through various lands and borders, and ultimately brought them safely to a peaceful country—has the best proof that Hashem wishes to protect them. When they simply create the appropriate *keilim*, Hashem will surely provide them with what they need, especially healthy children, which is one of the first and primary *mitzvos* of the holy Torah, and the greatest happiness that Jews can wish for themselves.

I hope that when you receive this letter, you will stop overthinking the aforementioned matter entirely and will be secure in your *emunah* in Hashem, who is the sole Master of the entire world and everything within it. He, blessed be He, will grant you an easy pregnancy, and at the proper time, you will have a *veled chai v'kayama* (a healthy, living child), and together with your husband, *sh'yichyeh*, you will raise the child to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to *maasim tovim*.

It would be appropriate to have all the *mezuzos* in your home checked to ensure they are all *kosher*, and that you give a cent or two to *tzedakah* every Monday and Thursday morning from the money you receive for expenses. Your husband, *sh'yichyeh*, should do the same. The amount is not important; the main thing is that it be done with consistency. It goes without saying that this should be done *bli neder*.

I reiterate the aforementioned point: one must be strong in the decision to lead a Jewish, Chassidic home, and be strong in *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach that He will grant healthy, living children and everything one needs, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

P.S.
Enclosed is a copy of a *michtav klali* of mine, which you will surely make known among your friends.

## 2523

B"H, 13 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your personal matter, it seems I have already written to you previously citing the Sages' teaching: "Descend a step and take a wife," and apparently these words have not yet "reached" you—in the sense of the interpretation in Likutei Torah at the beginning of Parshas Shemini, where "reached" means "touched" (engaged). In a humorous vein, one could say that since the Sages said that "their pairing is as difficult as the splitting of the Yam Suf," the sea was split specifically through the jumping of a Jewish man into the sea without excessive calculations, knowing only that this was the will of Hashem, and the stretching out of the staff by Moshe Rabbeinu.

As you requested, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the aforementioned matter. However, it is also known from the Sages that in order to open an entrance as wide as the entrance to the Ulam, one must at least make an opening the size of a needle's eye.

With blessings for a Purim that is joyous "until one does not know," and specifically with wine—which in our Torah, which is our life, refers to the hidden part of Torah, as is also hinted at in the Sages' teaching, "When wine enters, the secret emerges," which is explained in the Zohar and in the teachings of Chassidus in many places.

With blessings that you bring good news regarding all of the above as soon as possible.

## 2524

B"H, 13 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, the G-d-fearing, esteemed, and distinguished, engaged in communal needs,
R' Yaakov Eliezer, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Regarding your question as to whether to include a minor in a minyan: this is a matter that is highly surprising among anash. Since you and the other anash, may they live, are in a country where the customs of our Nasi, our holy Rebbes, and their Chassidim must also be publicized, it is naturally necessary to be more precise in this matter. Therefore, in my opinion, the aforementioned should not be done. Surely, if you make the effort, in most cases you will find a minyan of those thirteen years of age and older.

I have received the news that a building has been purchased for the yeshivah in the city center. Surely you are also making efforts regarding the practical aspect—that is, to be able to move the yeshivah there as soon as possible—and everyone is exerting themselves in this as much as they are able... And may Hashem guide you on the path that is good before Him, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With blessings for success in all the above and for a happy Purim.

***

**2524**

**R' Yaakov Eliezer:** Herzog, Melbourne.

**That a building has been purchased for the yeshivah:** See also above, Letter 2110, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 2525

B"H, 13 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 28th of Adar I: Regarding *machshavos zaros* (alien thoughts), one must increase the recitation of the letters of Torah and the letters of *tefillah*. Furthermore, one should have engraved in the mind of his memory certain chapters of *Tanya* and certain chapters of *Mishnayos*, which provide protection even at times when one is not reviewing them, and even when they are only in one’s thoughts—as is understood from *Likutei Torah*, at the end of *Parshas Kedoshim*. Consequently, it is appropriate that you also learn by heart the aforementioned *maamar*, "Ve'hadarta Pnei Zaken."

Since these thoughts frequently cause distraction specifically during *tefillah* and during learning, it is good that during *tefillah* and learning, the *Siddur* or the *sefer* you are studying should be open before you at the place where you are holding. When you feel your thoughts wandering, you should immediately gaze into the *Siddur* or the *sefer*, for the written letters "hold one in" (*alten ayn*).

Regarding your upcoming birthday, which you mention in your letter: May it be the will of Hashem that you have a successful year. Since you still have several weeks for preparation, you will surely endeavor during this time to increase your diligence and perseverance (*hasmadah*), and your *mesiras nefesh* (dedication), and may the Almighty grant you success.

With blessings.

## 2526

B"H, 13 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Yosef, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

From time to time, I receive news regarding your communal involvement, and in particular regarding your good deeds in assisting our Yeshiva, Tomchei Temimim in Lod. Surely, like everything that is alive and holy, this assistance will continue to grow and increase, especially since the hour demands it. For if in all places and at all times the education of the youth was a vital issue, how much more so is this true in our generation—an orphaned generation—and in the land that all the nations of the world agree to call the Holy Land. Fortunate is the portion of anyone who can take part in this work.

It was pleasant for me to learn that your health has improved and that you have already returned to your work. Surely this will also be the case regarding the health of the soul. For a Jewish person—who for generations has been a standard-bearer for the concept of unity in the world: one G-d, one Torah, and one nation—the idea of unity permeates the very existence of every individual among them, and first and foremost, that the body and soul must be a unified entity. There is nothing that can stand before the will, especially since whoever comes to purify himself is assisted from Above.

With a blessing for success in your work, that you may fulfill your part in raising a youth devoted to everything that has been holy to the people of Israel since they stood at Mount Sinai, and may this be with proper health.

## 2,527

B"H, 16 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write about the necessity of a commentary on the holy Tanya: It is already a well-known saying of our Nasi that in the study of Tanya—which is called the Written Torah of the teachings of Chassidus—the greatest of the great cannot fathom its depths, yet even the simplest of the simple can understand it to some extent. Consequently, it is understood that everyone must study it without waiting for a commentary to be printed, etc. This is especially true in our days, now that several Chassidic texts have already been printed in which the concepts presented in Tanya are explained in brief.

The main point is that just as in the study of Chumash, and even Gemara, the initial study is done simply, and from year to year one adds understanding and depth, so too is the path of study in all parts of our holy Torah. This naturally applies as well to the study of the inner dimension of Torah in the Tanya, Torah Or, Likutei Torah, etc. One should not pay attention to the incitement of the Yetzer that the study is difficult, etc. You have surely seen the Kuntres Limud HaChassidus, from which the above is also understood.

As you requested, a copy of the holy Tanya is being sent to you in a separate package. You will surely share the merit of it with your friends as well, since it is not possible to send one to each individual separately.

With blessings for Torah study with fear of Heaven.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 2,528

2,528

B"H, 16 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you write about your nervousness: it would be worthwhile for you to study a few chapters in *Shaar HaBitachon* of *Chovos HaLevavos*, and to search in *D'ch* for the places where the concept of *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Section 25 (140b) is explained. For if one truly believed that "this was from Hashem," etc., it would be understood that there is no reason to be nervous. The paths for drawing down the blessings of the *Ribono shel Olam* for everything one needs are well-known; they are paved roads upon which everyone can ascend and walk securely, and consequently, there is no reason to be agitated or nervous, as is understood.

With blessings for success in all the above, for you and for your wife, the *Rabbanit* (may she live and be well).

P.S.

Following up on what your wife (may she live and be well) wrote to me previously, that she does not like matters that are left unfinished: it is surprising that it has not yet been finished—meaning, that I have received no response to what I wrote to her twice regarding the necessity for her to work within her environment to increase not just Judaism in general, but *Chassidus* as well. As is known, the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (of blessed memory, whose merit will protect us), that although the work of baking bread is essential for the survival of the human race, nevertheless, one who has the ability—and has been taught—to be a diamond cutter should not busy himself with a task that so many others can perform.

It is also understood that I do not mean that they must write to me specifically about what is being done in this regard; rather, the main thing is the actual work that should be done in practice. And since the *Ribono shel Olam* does not deal unjustly with His creatures, surely the strength and the possibilities have been given to her to act in this matter, and I will await good news.

With blessings.

## 2,529

B"H, 16 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long silence, I was pleased to receive your letter, although I am not pleased with its content, as I see that you are preoccupied with the health of your children, and you conclude your letter with the question of what you can do, other than weep and lament.

Firstly, one must stop weeping and the like, in accordance with the frequent demand of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of the *gedolei Yisrael* of previous generations, that one must *avodu es Hashem b'simcha* (serve Hashem with joy). It is explained in the *Zohar HaKadosh* that when one is in a state of joy and is strong in *bitachon*, this itself is a *segulah* that one is granted from Above more and more matters to be happy and satisfied with, both regarding oneself and regarding the entire family.

Especially in your case, since the children have merited to study in an institution for which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *masar nefesh*, this in itself is a certainty that for the children, this is the path to be healthy and happy, both *b'gashmius* and *b'ruchnius*. One should not pressure the husband, *shichyeh*, so much that you must move immediately. In time, this too will come, and one must wait for the *sha'ah tovah u'mutzlachas*.

Regarding your question of what you can do: as mentioned above, bring joy into the home and continue your work of spreading *Yiddishkeit* among your friends. This will hasten and increase the *bracha v'hatzlacha* in your personal matters as well.

Enclosed is a copy of a *michtav klali* in connection with the days of Purim, and surely you will utilize it in your aforementioned work.

With a wish for much *nachas* from your children—*Yiddishe, Chassidishe nachas*—and to receive this in good health and joy.

## 2,530

2,530

B"H, 17 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings! I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 11 Adar I, in which you write regarding your friend...

You should certainly also provide his mother’s name, as explained in the Zohar Hakadosh and hinted at in the Shas, that in matters of health—both physical and spiritual—one must mention the mother’s name (see Zohar Vol. I, 84a; Shabbos 66b; Panim Yafos, end of Parshas Beha'aloscha; Divrei Torah, Mahadura Tinyana, sec. 6). And according to our Sages, of blessed memory, who stated that the Torah granted the physician permission to heal and one should not rely on miracles, you should have sought the opinion of a specialist physician and followed his instructions.

It is understood that he should have his Tefillin checked, as well as the Mezuzos in the room where he sleeps, and he should endeavor to divert his mind from thoughts about himself and to cheer him up in an appropriate manner.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant him the merit to bring good tidings regarding the above, and also that they fulfill the demand of our holy Torah—which is emphasized most strongly by our Rebbe, the Baal Shem Tov, of blessed memory, and for all of Klal Yisrael—that the avodah of the Ribono shel Olam must be specifically with simcha, as it is written, "Serve Hashem with simcha." This is also a halachic ruling for practical application in the Rambam, at the end of Hilchos Lulav. And since it is ruled in Hilchos De'os, as well as in the Tur and Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, sec. 231, that a great principle in a person's life is the avodah of the Ribono shel Olam in "all your ways," it is understood that the aforementioned ruling to serve Hashem with simcha applies to this as well.

With blessings for Torah study with yiras shamayim, and awaiting good tidings.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 2531

B"H, 17 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Adar II, in which you write that... and request that I pray for you and your wife, may they live, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good, for living and enduring children.

As you requested, when I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you for the aforementioned.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the well-known teaching of our Sages that the attribute of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is "measure for measure," and that nothing in the world is in vain. Since, through Divine Providence, your position is a public one connected to a certain measure of influence in your city, you must utilize it with all your ability and strength to bring the hearts of the sons and daughters of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven, who sometimes, due to various reasons, forget that they are children of G-d. Your efforts to return the lost and to bring closer those who are distant and cast away—which, when done with sincerity and the appropriate energy, is surely guaranteed success—will, measure for measure, provide a strong hope that the Almighty will grant you, the essence of goodness, *nachas* from your children, and that you will raise them to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds.

It is also a well-known instruction of our holy Torah that for every matter, there must also be a foothold in the ways of nature. Therefore, you should consult a specialist in this field and ask for his professional opinion as to what you should do within the ways of nature regarding the aforementioned.

It is appropriate to have the *mezuzos* in your home checked, as well as your *tefillin*, to ensure they are *kosher*. Furthermore, on Mondays and Thursdays of each week, in the morning, you should give a few coins to *tzedakah* that is connected to education based on Torah and *mitzvos*. Your wife, may she live, should do the same before lighting the candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 2733

B”H, 18 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Moreinu HaRav Yisrael Moshe, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 3rd of Adar Sheni—which, for some reason, the response to has been delayed until now—especially since at the conclusion of your letter you also hinted at the content of the response, which is:

The custom of the Rebbe’s house is well known, that we do not write approbations for seforim and booklets, and it is known from our Sages, of blessed memory, “Do not change the custom of your ancestors.” Regarding the matter at hand, the sefer you are transcribing—although you did not mention its name or the name of its author in your letter, it is apparent from the proof sheets you enclosed that it is the commentary on the Torah by the author of the sefer *Chorev*—these seforim are well known and famous in the circles to which you are apparently directing your transcription.

May Hashem merit each and every one of us to fulfill our portion and role in clarifying and refining the darkness of the world, and illuminating it with the candle of the mitzvah, the Torah of light, and the light within the Torah—which is *pnimiyus haTorah*.

I hope it is unnecessary to remind you of the absolute necessity in our times to establish *shiurim* in the study of *pnimiyus haTorah* as well, and this necessity applies even to those G-d-fearing individuals from circles that in previous generations did not engage in this. As the well-known parable goes, when the darkness intensifies, it is necessary to increase both the quantity of the light and its quality.

## 2536

B"H, 18 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you write concerning the various difficulties that have arisen in your business: according to the instruction of our master, the Baal Shem Tov, every detail—and every detail of a detail—regarding a Yid is by *Hashgacha Pratis*. Since Hashem has granted you the merit and success that, alongside the aforementioned difficulties, the new building for the *yeshiva* has been found—which holds great promise to become a center of *yiras shamayim* for the entire city and perhaps even the entire state—you should perceive a connection between these two matters. You should accept this as a directive from Heaven that you should throw yourself into this, both with money and, primarily, with your own physical efforts, to see to the arrangement of the *yeshiva* building and subsequently to involve yourself with the *yeshiva* to the maximum extent. This will repair the *tzinoros* (channels) of your private business and expand them, so that they, too, will be met with extraordinary success.

It is not my way to indicate specific figures, especially when I am not on-site. However, the statement of our Sages is well known: "Whoever adds, they add to him." Consequently, the more you add—both with your money and with your own personal labor in doing this yourself, as well as by involving others—Hashem will certainly add to your success in the matters you require.

You surely had a joyous Purim, and I hope that you will also be able to report good, gladdening tidings regarding all that has been mentioned above...

## 2737

B"H, 19 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, a man of pure thought, etc., our teacher Rabbi Avraham Yehuda, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...I was pleased to learn a few days ago... that the matter of your new residence is being arranged. May it be the will of Hashem that "a change of place brings a change of fortune" for good and for blessing in all matters, in accordance with the phrasing of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (as it seems was also the case with the Nasi’im before him), both materially and spiritually.

It has been explained several times during farbrengens that the belief in one Hashem is a logical necessity. It leads to the acceptance of one Torah specifically, and a necessary result of this is that there must be "one nation on earth"—meaning unity in all matters—for only then is the belief in the unity of Hashem complete. It is remarkable that precisely in recent times, even in the sciences, this idea is gaining strength, taking giant strides toward unifying all the various phenomena in the physical nature as much as possible, both in the formulation of laws and, primarily, in finding one general force of which all other forces—and consequently all phenomena—are branches and parts.

It goes without saying that I am not writing this for the sake of pilpul, but rather for the aforementioned point: that you should soon share good news in both material and spiritual matters—namely, an improvement in your health and that you are finding spiritual satisfaction...

I have seen the various reprints that were here in the hands of Rabbi Telushkin and Mr. Rivkin. Certainly, you do not need my approval for this, but as is the way of all Bnei Yisrael, not to let a matter pass without commenting on it—and specifically not in a way of providing assistance, as our Sages said (Bava Metzia 84a), "Do I not know that I speak well?"—I will draw a general principle from the parable of our Sages (Sotah 40a): the merchant who sells haberdashery always has customers, because he deals in items of absolute necessity for the widest circles, unlike one who sells precious stones and pearls.

I look forward to hearing good news, and send my regards to your entire family, may they live.

P.S.
Many thanks, especially for the stories you transcribed in your letter. Surely, continue to write these excellent things, whose "garments are precious."

As you requested, the aforementioned reprints have been sent in a separate package addressed to you.

## 2538

B"H, 19 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak - Lubavitch
in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live,

Shalom and Bracha!

...They see tangibly, and even with physical eyes, success that is above the natural order regarding the affairs of the Reshet. This is true both in the attitude of the various individuals and institutions that were initially opposed, as well as in the resources they received, which they had not anticipated beforehand... And now, according to sound reason—even human reason, and even natural reason—this should have awakened in each and every member of the administration an addition of strength in their avodah, to strengthen and develop the Reshet, and to increase it in both quantity and quality...

I have come in this letter with a heartfelt and soulful appeal: it is now in their hands to sanctify the name of Lubavitch, and consequently, the name of our holy Nasi, and consequently, the great name of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He—by acquiring many of the sons and daughters of Israel, the "little ones of your people"—as the Midrash Esther Rabbah phrases it regarding the nullification of Haman’s decree—to bring them close to our Father in Heaven. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "Whoever teaches his fellow’s son Torah, it is as if he gave birth to him," etc., etc.

For the aforementioned, there is no need at all for matters of mesiras nefesh, bitul b'metzius, or even bitul hayesh. It is enough that each one dedicates themselves to their work in their own professional capacity... This is connected not only to their spiritual well-being and that of their families—may they live—but also to material matters, even those matters that the nefesh habehamis is drawn toward, such as honor, etc. And if there is no other way, our Sages of blessed memory have said that if one loses a coin and a poor person finds it, it is considered tzedakah. So, let it be that the nefesh habehamis of one becomes jealous of the nefesh habehamis of another—as long as they perform the actions necessary for the expansion of the Reshet in their entirety.

It is already known how the Mitteler Rebbe answered one of his Chassidim: According to the instruction of the Mitteler Rebbe, all those who returned from Lubavitch were commanded to repeat Chassidus in the places they passed through on their way back from Lubavitch—to disseminate the teachings of Chassidus. One of the distinguished individuals complained to him that he felt an increase in his own sense of self and yeshus because he saw that he was successful in repeating the Chassidus, etc., etc. The Mitteler Rebbe answered him: "You may become an onion—as long as you repeat Chassidus."

I hope that these lines of mine will suffice, even though they are few in quantity, and perhaps also in quality—in light of the matter that is entrusted to their hands and for which they have been given all the strength...

Awaiting good tidings soon.

## 2539

B"H, 20 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and scholarly R. Yitzchak, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and scholarly R. Shlomo Zalman Hecht, may he live, who is involved in communal needs. He also wrote to me that your son, Yosef, may he live, will turn three years old around Pesach, and you are asking when to perform the *upsherinish*.

While according to the letter of the law it may be done even during *Chol HaMoed* Pesach, nevertheless, taking into account the *minhagim* of Yisrael—and especially in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established—that the *upsherinish* is held on *Lag B’Omer*, it is my opinion that you should also do it on that day, *Lag B’Omer*, with all the *minhagim* associated with it, in accordance with the attached excerpt of an instruction from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

May Hashem grant you and your wife, may she live, the merit and success to raise him for Torah, for the *chuppah*, and for good deeds, in good health and with ample livelihood, in truth and with true joy.

With blessings for success in the above.

## 2541

B"H, 21 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, engaged in communal needs, R' Shlomo, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from Rosh Chodesh Adar and the 7th of Adar II, along with their enclosures. I also received the package of seforim you sent on the 15th of Shevat. Many thanks for what has been sent, and a request for the future.

I have already written to the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, R' B.A.G., may he live, that it is surprising how much you skimp on writing... However, we do not cry over the past. I am writing to urge you that regarding the matters currently necessary here—including those from the past—you should surely fulfill this at the next opportunity, without relying on someone else’s writing, or even on a verbal report. This is especially true regarding the visit of Mr. Cole, may he live, and subsequently of Rabbi Gold, may he live. It is certainly necessary to know the details of this here as well, since from time to time we are in contact with the various offices in the United States that are relevant to these matters.

Many thanks for the good news that all the members of your household, may they live, are in good health. May you continue to bring good tidings.

As in every year, I will urge you now as well: since many of the students—both boys and girls—are traveling to their homes for the days of Pesach, it is necessary to provide them with spiritual provisions for their journey. This applies both to them personally—so that they do not remain idle—and, most importantly, to make them channels through which to disseminate the ideas of Yiddishkeit in general, and the ideas, guidance, and concepts of Chassidus in particular, in the places they will be visiting. Beyond the necessity of this for the sake of the many, this is also a channel and a method to instill in the students themselves a desire to know these matters with greater depth. As is explained in many places in Chassidus, in order to influence another, one must understand the subject with deeper comprehension.

I am certain that the days of Purim were utilized in the appropriate manner; please inform me regarding this.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and regards to all those participating in this,

**M. Schneerson**

## 2542

B"H, 21 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...We spoke at the Purim farbrengen this year about the fact that when one does not fully utilize the strengths that Hashem has granted a person, as well as the strengths inherited from one’s ancestors, then all the ancestors come with a complaint that their strengths are being nullified and not used for their intended purpose. This is in addition to the main point: that one is failing to fulfill the Divine intent, for the possibilities and strengths were certainly given with the expectation that they be utilized in all their manifestations, rather than remaining in a state of "sleep." ## 2,543

B"H, 21 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a long interval, I was pleased to receive your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Shushan Purim, in which you write regarding your state of health, which was not as it should be and has now improved, and you also write regarding the shiurim that you have. It is surprising that you do not also mention the recitation of Tehillim after Shacharis (which is a takanah of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of our generation—a takanah for every soul), nor that you participate in the distribution of Shas, which, according to what is stated in several Likutei Diburim published by Machne Israel, is an ancient custom that our Nasi, the Nasi of Chabad, upheld and publicized as well. My hope is that this is merely an omission in writing, but that in practice you do have the aforementioned shiurim.

Furthermore, it is my hope that what is implied in your letter upon a superficial reading—that because your health was not as it should be, there was a weakening in your shiurim—is not the case. On the contrary, if one feels unwell, etc., our Sages have ruled that one should then engage in Torah with added intensity. This is understood based on the maamar that although Torah is called food and nourishment, it also brings healing to the world. For a Jewish person, where physicality and spirituality go hand in hand, when there is a weakness in the physical, it is certainly an indication regarding the spiritual as well, and one must engage in spiritual medicine—namely, an increase in the study of Torah. By doing so, one fulfills the command, "You shall be wholehearted with Hashem your G-d," both physically and spiritually, as explained in Likutei Torah on this verse (Nitzavim 45c).

It is unnecessary to point out that surely your eye is also good toward others, to arouse them and draw them as well to the Torah of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs. May Hashem grant you success in all of the above.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 2544

B"H, 21 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you during the time of Purim through your husband, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, involved in communal needs, R' [Name]—may he live and be well. May Hashem help that you should always be able to report good news regarding you both, both in material and in spiritual matters.

And certainly—as I have already told your husband, the esteemed Chossid—you are looking into how to influence your surroundings as well, to bring into them the warmth and vitality of Torah and mitzvos in general, and of the conduct of Chassidus in particular. This accelerates and increases all the blessings that Hashem gives from His full and expansive hand in all that one needs, both materially and spiritually.

Just as in material livelihood one does not sit at home waiting for someone to come and knock on the door to provide a living, so too regarding the aforementioned spiritual livelihood: one should not wait until the person who needs it comes to demand that they be made warmer and more vital in Yiddishkeit and in Torah and mitzvos. Rather, one must go out and seek them. And when one desires this in truth, one succeeds both in finding them and in the influence itself, which adds more desire to continue doing so in the future with success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.
