## 2546

B"H, 23 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Moreinu Harav Yoetz Dovid, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from some time ago, along with the resolutions of the Kinus of 8 Shevat 5714. Surely, by this time, you are already able to report on how these resolutions are being brought into action, for "it is not the study that is the essential thing, but the deed," and the deed is the test of how the study was conducted and the like, as explained in the interpretation of the saying, "There is no wise man like one with experience."

I was pleased by what you wrote in your letter regarding the establishment of the various shiurim in your camp, but what surprises me most—and this is also a continuation of the above—is that you do not mention anything about a shiur for learning the necessary halachos, most of which are found in Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim. Since there is a great need to know them, it is imperative to learn, first and foremost, at least a **summary** of them, such as the *Derech HaChaim* by the Gaon of Lissa, which is printed in the Siddurim, and one should also make use of the *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch* (skipping certain simanim whose laws are not as necessary) and the like. If only those who are students, and those whom Hashem has granted the portion of being "dwellers of the tent," would learn these laws of *brachos hanehenin*, interruptions during *davening*, etc., etc., the lack of which, to our great distress, is significant and alarming. May Hashem grant that through you, this study will be established in your camp as well, and with great expansion—and how good it would be if it were mandatory for all participants in the shiurim—and the same applies regarding women and the laws of *taharas hamishpachah* and the like.

Although you do not mention in your letter that you have a shiur in the study of Chassidus, I am certain that this is merely an omission in writing, and not that it is lacking, Heaven forbid, in practice. May Hashem grant you success in bringing good tidings regarding all of the above.

With blessings for success.

P.S.
Enclosed is a copy of my general letter to the women and daughters of Yisrael, which I am sure you will publicize in an appropriate manner.

## 2,547

B"H, 23 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 3 Adar II, in which you write that you are deeply worried about your wife and children—may they live—as well as about your livelihood, and consequently, you have no peace of mind to study the Torah of Hashem.

It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding the channels and vessels for receiving the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam in all these matters, which are Torah and mitzvos. It is already a well-known saying of our Alter Rebbe, the author of the Tanya (who decides the hidden aspects of Torah) and the author of the Shulchan Aruch (who decides the revealed aspects of Torah), who replied to someone who complained about a similar matter: "You are worrying about what you need, but not about what is needed of you." This is brought down in a letter from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which is printed in Kuntres 57. It is explained there as well that when one exerts effort in those matters that are the purpose of man’s creation on earth—as our Sages of blessed memory say at the end of Kiddushin, "I was created only to serve my Maker"—then the Ribono shel Olam fulfills those matters that the person needs.

Surely you are aware of the three daily shiurim for every soul, established by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: 1) Reciting the daily portion of Tehillim—as divided by the days of the month—each day after Shacharis; 2) Studying the Chumash parsha with Rashi’s commentary (on Sunday, from the beginning of the sedra until the second aliyah; on Monday, from the second aliyah until the third, etc.); 3) Studying the daily shiur of Tanya, as the Tanya is divided for the days of the year.

Surely, at the next opportunity, you will inform me regarding all of the above. As you requested, I will mention everyone at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, for whatever they need in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings that you should have good news regarding all the above, and for a kosher and happy Pesach.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## B'Takamach

B'Takamach

B"H, 24 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter—though it lacked a date—in which you share the good news regarding your son, may he live and be well. Certainly, when one witnesses miracles from Hashem Yisbarach, it should inspire the entire family to strengthen themselves further in matters of Torah and mitzvos. This strengthening accelerates the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in the other matters you mention in your letter as well.

Regarding what you write about modern [trends], you must explain to all your children that the Holy One, Blessed be He, is the same as He was hundreds of years ago, and likewise, the Torah is the same as it has always been. Hashem Yisbarach leads the world just as He did in the past, and therefore, one must hold fast to the path that the Torah has indicated. This is the only way for Jews to receive the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach in all that they require.

When your children conduct themselves in this manner, you will surely be able to share good news regarding all the matters you write about in your letter.

With wishes for a kosher and happy Pesach.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 2549

B"H, 24 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following your long silence regarding your involvement in Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, I was pleased to receive your letter of the 18th of Adar II, and I am certain that you will continue to write regarding this in the future.

Although, officially, joint letters should be arranged, for several reasons it is appropriate that, in addition to official correspondence, the personal opinion of the members of the administration also be received unofficially.

It is understood that this does not constitute a departure from refined speech, as this pertains to actual *avodah*. As is explained in several books—and regarding our Sages of blessed memory—concerning the concept of "clean language" where the Torah circumvents eight letters to avoid an impure term, this applies only when narrating a story, but not in matters of *piskei dinim* (halachic rulings), as seen in this week’s *parsha* and the previous one.

May your participation in the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, hasten and increase the blessings of Hashem for you and your household, may they live, in general, and specifically regarding *nachas* in a Chassidic spirit from your sons and daughters.

I await good news and conclude with a blessing for a kosher and happy Pesach.

P.S.
My letter to the administration of the Reshet has surely been received by now.

## 2550

B"H, 24 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...First and foremost, you should, in consultation with the appropriate elders of Anash, convey my bewilderment to the esteemed Chossid, our teacher Rabbi [Name]... regarding the fact that, apparently, he has still not abandoned his path of serving Hashem specifically through *marah shechorah* (melancholy).

How this path is refuted requires no explanation, even for a *olam-she* (simple person), since the verse states, "Serve Hashem with joy." This is especially true for those who belong to the community of Chassidim, as is explained in the command of the Baal Shem Tov regarding the service of Hashem with joy. In particular, for those who have seen the wonders of the Ribono shel Olam tangibly and literally—that He brought them out of their country previously, etc., etc.—this is like the well-known saying of the Rebbe Rashab, of blessed memory: "A Litvak does not believe until he counts it over. But to count it over and still not believe—that is a truly terrible *helem v'hester* (concealment)."

May the Ribono shel Olam grant the aforementioned success in serving Hashem specifically through joy, which will, in turn, enable him to share joyful tidings...

I await good news, and I sign with a blessing for success in your holy work and for a kosher and joyous Pesach.

## 2551

By the Grace of Hashem
25 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 24 Adar II. I must begin my letter by stating that I was extremely disappointed by this letter, in addition to the disappointment regarding the matter in general.

It is surely unnecessary to repeat that it is a *davar hapashut*—a simple fact—and it has been discussed many times at *farbrengens*, that the Ribono shel Olam did not create anything in vain. Consequently, everyone must utilize their *kishronos* (talents) in the direction of the *maamar* of the Gemara in *Kiddushin*: "I was not created but to serve my Creator."

Seeing in you the talent to influence your environment and also to lead your peers, I was certain that you would utilize this in accordance with the aforementioned *maamar* of our Sages, so that they, too, would become closer to "serving their Creator."

Therefore, when a report emerged that you had given advice and led them in the opposite direction—and according to your writing, it appears that this was indeed the case—it made a difficult impression on me, as stated above.

Nevertheless, taking into account that "there is no righteous man on earth who does good and does not sin," I assumed that upon recognizing that this was a failure—and as you yourself write in your letter—you would accept the consequences. When one wishes to free oneself from an inappropriate act or a failure, it is not done by trying to forget about it and doing nothing further. Rather, if a *mesubav* (a consequence or punishment) follows, you should have enough strength to acknowledge that "since I am at fault, I deserve this punishment."

Even if you think that the punishment is not commensurate with the failure, you should at least take into account that, as an interested party, you cannot judge objectively, and you will likely want to minimize the fault.

Secondly, even if, after consideration, the punishment is indeed too severe: the older a person is who caused the failure—and especially when it concerns a group, and this individual was a leader who gave advice—one must demand more of **oneself** and not want to be treated leniently in relation to one's peers. As I see from your letter, you view the punishment as an act where your honor and your very *metzius* (existence) have been touched, and therefore you want to retaliate by leaving the *yeshiva*.

And thirdly—which is a source of great wonder and disappointment to me—I was certain that you, and the *bnei yeshiva* in general, view the *yeshiva* as one should view and look upon a *yeshiva*. It is not a place where one comes to learn like a guest, and when one finishes learning for a certain time, one says goodbye to the "landlord" and leaves. Rather, one should understand well that a *yeshiva* is built not only by *roshei yeshivos* and *mashpi'im*, but by the *bochurim* and *talmidim*. Consequently, they should look upon it as a spiritual edifice to which **everyone** must contribute their share. It should not be treated as a matter of "how could it be otherwise," where in one's free time one has nothing to do with the *yeshiva*. On the contrary, one must act with *mesiras nefesh* and dedication, just as a person acts in their own affairs and builds their own structure.

It goes without saying that having such an attitude, it would not occur to anyone to play a trick on the *yeshiva* (!) or the *hanhalah* (administration) of the *yeshiva* (!) by leaving the *yeshiva*!

There is a well-known parable for this: when a person tangles their left foot with their right, they do not take a whip to punish the right foot; rather, they seek ways to ensure it does not happen again.

I am writing all this to you, naturally, not to lecture you, but to express my disappointment and my hope that the *kochos* (energies) that have been invested in you, and the *kishronos* that the Ribono shel Olam has gifted you, will not allow the *yetzer hara* to strengthen itself over you and overwhelm you to the point that you leave the *yeshiva* where you can learn Torah with *yiras shamayim*, *Toras HaNigleh*, and *Toras HaChassidus*. May the Ribono shel Olam help you to be a *mofes*—a model—for your other peers.

With blessings for pure *yiras shamayim*.

## 2552

B"H, 25th of Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Shemini: Regarding what you wrote about your memory, it is not advisable to force the issue—that is, to place a burden upon your memory. On the contrary, you should ease the pressure. Furthermore, study in a place where your heart desires, for then the power of *taanug* assists the power of memory, and consequently, it will eventually return to its strength. This is especially true since, in your case, it is surely also a matter related to your nerves.

It is unnecessary to remind you of what is explained in many places regarding the absolute necessity of guarding one’s physical health, and consequently, to follow the doctor’s instructions...

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

P.S.
I would be interested to know how you utilized the days of Purim that have passed.

## 2553

B"H, 25 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Moreinu HaRav Nathan Menachem, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 12 Adar II, as well as the postcard enclosed with it.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning the halachic discussion on the law of *taanis bechorim* on Erev Pesach: Without entering into the substance of the matter, a *Haggadah* that is printed for the masses, especially in the United States, is viewed by *anash* as a *psak din* and a final conclusion that should not be questioned. And it is well known that, ultimately, the essential thing is the practical action. Therefore, I have focused on this matter specifically, because in my opinion, it is a distortion that requires correction.

Regarding what you noted concerning the report about the *tzaddik* of Zidichov, *zt"l*, regarding what is transmitted in his name about a different *girsa* in *Maseches Sofrim*, etc.: This report has already been nullified from the outset in the book *Divrei Torah*, *Mahadura* 5, letter 15, by the *tzaddik*, etc., author of the *She'eilos U'Teshuvos Minchas Elazar* of Munkacs, and he reinforced his words in *Nimukei Orach Chaim*, *siman* 470. And since he was in close proximity to the subject of the report and also stood in a close family relationship with him, this adds weight to his nullification of it.

Regarding what you note in your letter about the *divrei Torah* in *Yalkut Nassan* and *Lekach Tov* in your book: In general, in these days, any matter that leads to *yiras shamayim* and to the strengthening and beautification of *mitzvos*—may the strength of those who occupy themselves with this be bolstered, for *Chavakuk* came and established them upon one principle: that is the matter of *emunah*.

With a blessing for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 2554

B"H, 25 Adar II, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter requesting a blessing for your mother, she should live and be well: When I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, at a time of favor, I will mention her for what she needs. You should write to her that she must strengthen her trust in Hashem, who performs wonders and is the essence of goodness and kindness, that He will bless her with what she and her family—may they live—need. She has no reason to worry at all. However, she should have the mezuzos in their home checked, as well as the tefillin that are worn, and any that need replacing should be replaced with kosher ones.

It is known from our Sages that a son brings merit to his father (and mother as well). Consequently, you, too, must increase your strength in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, with dedication, self-giving, and the nullification of personal desires. For the study of Torah, which is our life—and especially the study of Torah in purity—draws down blessing and success in everything a person and their family needs. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for success in Torah study with fear of Heaven.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita.

## 2558

B"H, 1 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your question about not finding satisfaction and not seeing room for great achievements for yourself in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) now or in the future, and consequently, the question has been raised again about moving from there.

In my opinion, on the contrary—from how I see the situation in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) regarding the avodah of Chabad, and also after speaking with Mr. Shazar (may he live) here—there is actually room for the greatest development. Just as it is always the case that from the disputes of Midian and Moav, Bnei Yisrael must utilize this to strengthen their standing and situation, the same applies in a spiritual sense within Bnei Yisrael themselves. This is provided that they remain on guard to utilize every such opportunity in ways of pleasantness and ways of peace.

It is understood that the above concerns the field of education, public communal work, and so on. As I have seen since the passing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (of blessed memory), involvement in this is linked to an increase in blessing and success in what is needed for those involved—both for themselves and their households, both materially and spiritually.

All of the above would hold true even if the prospects for settling abroad were extremely bright, and it goes without saying at this time and in the near future, when, on the contrary, the prospects for this according to the ways of nature are steadily declining.

With blessings for success in your holy work, with proper health, peace of mind, and livelihood for you and all your household (may they live), and to celebrate the Festival of Matzos with kashrus and true joy. I await good tidings.

## 2560

B”H, 1 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 19 Adar II and the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed with it.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the successor to the late Rabbi Merari, *a”h*, which has been entrusted to so-and-so, son of so-and-so: I wish to clarify the intent here. It does not mean that the responsibility has been removed from Agudas Chabad. Rather, since every matter requires someone to attend to it specifically, it was entrusted to that individual. However, it is understood that you must remain on guard, and everything must be done in a manner that ensures the matter is brought to a successful conclusion. It is unnecessary to emphasize (*baavaren*) that my intention is not, *chas v’shalom*, to diminish the standing of the person you selected for this task, but only to increase the responsibility of all involved, for "in the multitude of counselors there is safety." This also applies to all future matters: when a task or issue is entrusted to an individual or a group to execute, the intention is certainly as stated above—that they are merely the ones to carry it out, and this in no way diminishes the responsibility that rests upon Agudas Chabad.

Regarding what you wrote about... and beginning with a proposal to remove so-and-so from his position: you do not state the reason for this. Why suddenly remove a man from a position he has held for so many years? If the person has begun to slacken or fail in his duties, you must endeavor to ensure he fulfills his role properly and warn him about this twofold and threefold, but not begin by removing him from the position entirely...

Regarding your statement that there are apparently other tasks for Agudas Chabad besides those I pointed out in my previous letter: it is self-evident that I did not need to list in my letter matters such as knowing the status of Chabad synagogues in the Holy Land, or Chabad rabbis and *shochtim*, etc. I only wrote in my letter regarding those points where there was doubt.

Since I have arrived at the point regarding synagogues, it would be worthwhile to know the current situation—that is, where there are Chabad synagogues, as well as Chabad rabbis and *shochtim*—in order to ensure that their numbers are not reduced, and on the contrary, that they increase. Likewise, in new settlements where there are activists from *anash* and Chabad, you should endeavor through them to find means of livelihood for *anash* or the descendants of *anash*, especially in positions that grant their holders influence in spiritual matters.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and awaiting good tidings.

P.S.
Please publicize my proposal to study during the upcoming days of Pesach the *maamarim* for Pesach from the year 5704, which are now printed and were also published some time ago in a separate *kuntres*—*Kuntres* 91.

## 2561

B"H, 1 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...And moving from one topic to a related one: Since there are those who complain that they do not look after their health, claiming that it interferes with their *avodah* in the *yeshiva*, it is already well-known that no such arguments are valid against the *Shulchan Aruch*, nor are they valid against the *psak din* of the Baal Shem Tov, the Maggid, the Alter Rebbe, and the *Nesi'im* who followed them. All of them were extremely particular about maintaining one’s health, as is brought in brief regarding the magnitude of this matter in the *maamar* of 10 Shevat, 5713. And since this is the demand of our *Nasi*, surely it will not cause any harm to the *mitzvah* in general, and specifically regarding the *yeshiva*. On the contrary, one *mitzvah* leads to another, and through this, one will also increase the benefit to the *yeshiva*. Further elaboration is unnecessary.

With blessings for proper health for you and your entire household, *shichyu*, and for a *kosher* and happy *Pesach*. — Awaiting good news regarding the above.

## 2562

B"H, 1 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who engages in communal needs,
Rabbi Shlomo Chaim, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 24th of Adar Sheni, as well as the one preceding it. I was pleased to read what you wrote regarding the Yud Shevat farbrengen, and that, as is apparent from your letter, bochurim from other yeshivos also participated. It is understood by anyone who contemplates the activities of the Baal HaHilula throughout his lifetime in this world, how great was his yearning to disseminate the wellsprings outward, and subsequently, to bring those who are outside, inside.

Now is a uniquely opportune time for this (and in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily), for several reasons. One of the primary reasons is that, as was explained in one of the farbrengens here, we see tangibly how all the rivers (the various approaches of the students of the students of the Baal Shem Tov and the Maggid) flow into the sea (the general sea of knowledge, to **know** Hashem specifically, which is impossible without the study of Chassidus Chabad).

Regarding what you ask about specific students whose presence in the yeshiva might positively influence other students, while on the other hand, if they were to leave the yeshiva, there is a significant concern for their own standing and situation:

Although it is difficult to enter into details, as the situation changes depending on the nature of each individual, his family situation, etc., there is one general principle in questions such as these: the damage to the many overrides the benefit of the individual. This is especially true in an educational institution, and an education whose primary point is yiras shamayim, where the parents and the bochurim who come entrust their fate to the yeshiva administration—particularly regarding yiras shamayim, which increases the responsibility many times over.

Specifically regarding [the student you mentioned]... it would be worthwhile to try to influence him by appealing to his sense of pride. As is known from the Chassidic story about one of the great Chassidim of our Alter Rebbe, of whom it was said that it was difficult for him to commit any sin due to his sense of pride—saying to himself, "Shall I, one of the great Chassidim of such a great Rebbe, be enticed by the incitement of the yetzer hara, through which I am liable to lose my standing among the Jewish people, and especially among the community of Chassidim?"

Regarding what I wrote in my letter to the students concerning maintaining their health, it would be worthwhile for you to speak about this at one of the farbrengens, as it seems there are several students who are still being stringent with a stringency that leads to laxity. You should explain to them that this, too, is a tactic of the yetzer hara—to quiet their demands for yiras shamayim through physical self-affliction, while at the same time "fattening" the yetzer hara itself by failing to accept spiritual self-affliction, namely, self-restraint in speech, in sight, and dedication and commitment to study, etc., etc.

## 2563

B"H, 2 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, R' Ephraim Eliezer HaKohen, may he live:

Shalom u’vracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the eve of 26 Adar II. I was especially pleased to receive your postcard from the eve of Shabbos, Parshas HaChodesh—the festival of redemption, miracles, and joy (see Rashi, Taanis 29a, end).

As we approach the upcoming Chag HaMatzos, I wish to extend my blessings to you and your family, may they live, that you may celebrate it with kashrus and joy. In accordance with what is explained in many places—that the Yomim Tovim influence the days that follow them until the next festival, as is also explained in Likutei Torah by the Alter Rebbe, Parshas Bracha 94b—may this influence extend throughout your home and your surroundings throughout the entire year.

In that same source (in the aforementioned Likutei Torah), the discussion concerns the level of bitul that exists in all the festivals, which consequently only needs to be drawn down until the next festival. This is not the case, however, regarding the matters unique to each specific festival, which are drawn down for the entire year. This is especially true regarding Chag HaPesach, as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the sicha of Chag HaPesach 5703: "The illumination of all the festivals shines throughout the day, but the illumination of Chag HaPesach is drawn down constantly."

With esteem and with blessings for the Chag.

## 2764

B”H, 2 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 22nd of Adar Sheni, in which you ask for details and specifics regarding your conduct:

In matters such as these, one should consult with the elders of Anash in your location, and they will instruct you, as it is impossible to enter into details, especially since circumstances change. I will, however, touch upon a few points:

1) Regarding your question of whether to devote yourself entirely to the work of *taamulah* (outreach) and not think about yourself at all: It is surprising even to consider such a premise, for conduct along a single line belongs to *Olam HaTohu*. You must have a set schedule for studying *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*, so that ultimately you will also be a *lamdan*. This is relevant both to the work of *taamulah* and to the essence of a person as a *chossid*. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

2) Likewise, regarding your question of whether one should take health into account: As mentioned above, it is surprising that such questions are asked, as these matters are well-known in every place. See also the *maamar* of 10 Shevat 5713, which explains that having a healthy and whole body is one of the ways of Hashem.

3) Regarding your question of whether one must fulfill every resolution even if it is contrary to logic, or whether one should take into account the people, the place, and the time: This question, too, belongs to *Olam HaTohu*. In *Olam HaTikkun*, one must take into account the place, the time, and one’s health; one simply must not be immersed in them, but rather use them for the service of Hashem. True, in order to be able to do this, the foundation and beginning of *avodah* must be through *kabbalas ol*, and the ultimate goal of *avodah* is service that transcends *taam v’daas* (logic and intellect)—but this does not mean *avodah* that is always contrary to logic. It is surprising that even regarding such simple matters, you were unable to consult with the Anash in your location...

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and for organized *avodah* as required by our holy Torah and as explained by our holy Nasi.

## 2,567

## 2,568

## 2559

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the day of the Hilula, 2 Nissan. It is puzzling that during all the times of the farbrengens, you either arrive at the very end or do not come at all. It seems that you were not present at the farbrengen of 2 Nissan either.

If this is because you use the days of the farbrengens to conduct a farbrengen in your own surroundings, it is possible that this is worthwhile. However, generally speaking, there is enough time to be present at a farbrengen where one is in the position of a recipient, and afterwards to conduct a farbrengen where one is the mashpia. As is explained in many places in Chassidus, it is the role of every individual to be both a mashpia and a recipient. Since Hashem demands this, it is certainly within the power of everyone, and it is therefore understood that until one conducts himself in this manner, it is impossible for him to fulfill his role completely, as our Sages said—at the end of Kiddushin—to serve my Creator in a manner that aligns with the will of Hashem.

It is understood that, as I have told you many times, my intention is not to offer rebuke, but rather to speak regarding practical action, at the very least for the future.

You should view the event where the meeting regarding your raise and contract was postponed as a hint—and perhaps even more than a hint—that you are being granted additional time to increase your activities of the aforementioned type, so that in the Heavenly Beis Din they will rule in your favor regarding the raise and contract as is fitting, which will naturally lead to this being realized below as well. Further elaboration on this is superfluous, and in general, this is a matter of "Polish letters" [i.e., unnecessary words].

You mention in your letter that you lecture several times a week to young men and women, as well as to elderly people, but you do not write anything about the content of your lectures. Surely you emphasize matters of practical action and the point of yiras shamayim. May Hashem grant you success and may you have good tidings regarding all of the above.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 2575

B"H, 3 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, illustrious, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs and is a man of action,
Rabbi Yehuda Zev Halevi, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

...I was pleased to hear that your studies during the winter term were successful, and you add that this was the case both in learning and in yiras shamayim. Certainly, your intention regarding yiras shamayim is specifically as it relates to actual practice in daily life. For when there is a tangible hold in actual deed, the matter becomes more deeply rooted and established in a person’s soul. This is especially so when it is possible to turn these good practices into a habit for the students, at which point it becomes a second nature for them, and they continue to act this way even when the consciousness of yiras shamayim is hidden from them. After all, the deed is the essential thing...

Approaching the upcoming Chag HaMatzos, I hereby wish you and your family, may they live, that you celebrate it with kashrus and joy. Based on what is explained in many places—that the Yomim Tovim influence the days that follow them until the next festival, as is also explained in Likutei Torah by our Rebbe HaZaken in Parshas Bracha, 98b—may this influence be drawn down into your home and your surroundings throughout the days of the year as well.

Now, there (in the aforementioned Likutei Torah), the discussion concerns the level of bitul present in all the festivals, and consequently, it is only necessary to draw it down until the next festival. This is not the case, however, regarding the matters unique to each specific festival, which are drawn down for the entire year. This is especially true regarding Chag HaPesach, as per the adage of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in a sicha from Chag HaPesach 5703: "The illumination of all the festivals shines every day, and the illumination of Chag HaPesach is drawn down constantly."

One may explain, briefly at least, that in general, Shavuos is the matter of Torah, the time of the giving of our Torah; Sukkos is, in general, the matter of mitzvos, and their totality is the mitzvah of tzedakah, which encompasses (see Tanya, Chapter 5), as it is written: "I have placed My words in your mouth, and in the shadow of My hand I have covered you"; and Pesach, the time of our freedom, is the matter of emunah, in the language of the Zohar, "the food of faith." Now, there are matters of Torah and mitzvos that are dependent on time and place, whereas emunah is a constant mitzvah and the foundation of all Torah and mitzvos, and this is well understood.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Chag Pesach.

## 2571

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your telegram of 3 Nissan (it is puzzling that you send telegrams for all matters rather than a letter, which would allow for more detail; furthermore, the Torah is protective of the assets of Yisrael, and even if one is personally exempt, one is not permitted to [waste], as our Sages have said (Bava Kamma 91b), and this applies to financial loss which falls under the category of *bal tashchis*), in which you write regarding the reasoning for scheduling the wedding on Thursday, the eve of Friday, Lag B'Omer.

In general, it is better if possible for the wedding to take place on Isru Chag of Shavuos or in the days following, until the middle of the month of Sivan. If, for some reason, you specifically desire Lag B'Omer, then due to the differences of opinion regarding this, as explained in the *Acharonim*, it should be held on Friday, but not on the night preceding Friday.

Regarding what you write about the name of the bride, that she does not have a name in *Lashon HaKodesh* and is called Alga, and you ask whether to add a name to her: In general, it is explained in many places that the letters of a name are the conduit of life that connects the *neshamah* to the body. It is stated in the writings of the *Arizal* and generally among the Kabbalists that the name given by the parents is the one that Hashem calls the *neshamah* by in the Upper World (see *Shaar HaGilgulim*, Introduction 23; *Ohr HaChaim* on Devarim 29:17; *Chefetz Hashem*, *Berachos* 13, and elsewhere). Consequently, one should not change or add a name without a significant reason. Since the name Elka or Elkeh and the like, as mentioned above, are brought in books of women’s names, it should not be changed.

I am certain that you are increasing your efforts in your work in the field of kosher education; please inform me regarding this, as well as regarding your fixed *shiurim* in *Toras HaNigleh* and *Toras HaChassidus*.

Awaiting good news, and with blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 2512

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks the date of writing—containing the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein (which, G-d willing, I will read at an opportune time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory), in which you write that several doctors have suggested you have some of your teeth extracted, and as of now, you have not reached a decision to do so.

Now, although it is stated in *Pesachim* 113a, "Do not uproot a tooth," it is already well-known that the nature of things has changed regarding the medical treatments mentioned in the *Gemara*. Regarding what you heard in this matter in the name of the Tzemach Tzedek, and similarly, I have heard a report told about the *tzaddik* R' Hillel of Paritch, that he would not have teeth extracted—however, we have only what we have seen in the Rebbe’s household, where they followed the instructions of doctors in such matters, especially in your case, where the doctor states that the health of the entire body is affected and dependent upon this.

In these days, as we begin the matter of *matzah*, the "food of healing," which is why one must be careful not to eat *matzah* for thirty days before *Pesach*, may a complete healing be drawn down for you through the aforementioned, and likewise for your wife, may she live...

With blessings for a kosher and joyous *Pesach* holiday.

## 2573

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Michael, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 27 Adar Sheni, together with the enclosure, and I have also received your previous letter of 27 Adar Rishon and its enclosure.

I will begin with the *inyana d'yoma* (the topic of the day). Since many of the students are traveling to their homes for the days of Pesach, it is necessary to provide them with spiritual provisions for their journey—both for their own sake, *men zol nit arumgein leidig* (so they should not go around idle), and primarily to make them conduits to disseminate, in the places they visit, the ideas of Yiddishkeit in general, and the ideas of Chassidus, its guidance, and its concepts in particular. Beyond the necessity of this for the sake of the many, this is also a conduit and a method to instill within the students themselves a desire to know the aforementioned matters with greater depth, as is explained in many places in *Chassidus*—that in order to influence another, one must understand the matter with deeper comprehension. I have also written regarding this matter to the esteemed R' S.

Regarding the supplement...

Concerning what you wrote in the sheet attached to your letter, explaining the concept of the "loves" mentioned in *Tanya*—this matter is indeed highly complex.

As for your opening question—whether there are many loves in the human heart—it is not clear what is "bothering" you, for it is tangibly evident that they exist, even though they all share a common denominator: they are all a movement of love and closeness.

Likewise, your question—that the *nefesh* is comprised of ten [faculties], and if the source of the *midos* is *Chabad*, then *Chabad* are not included in the *nefesh*—is not difficult. Aside from the fact that since *Chabad* themselves are included in the *nefesh*, their derivatives are also included in the *nefesh*, it is understood that they are a distinct matter, even if the derivative is included in its source, as is explained in many places regarding the fundamental differences between *mochin* and *midos*. This is in addition to the main point: within the *nefesh* itself, every faculty stands on its own, and there they are ten faculties.

In general, regarding the levels and categories of love, you should look into the letter of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, printed at the end of *Kuntres HaAvodah* (published by Kehot, Brooklyn), in the places marked in my notes to *Kuntres Etz Chaim*, Chapter 2. By studying them, your doubts—most of them, at least—will be resolved. Likewise, see the *Biur Tanya* which appears to be by R' S. Gronem, of blessed memory, which was published in copy form by the esteemed R' A. some years ago.

Regarding love that comes through the arousal of mercy, see *Likutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim*, the *maamar* beginning "Mah Yafu," and at length in the book *Boneh Yerushalayim*, section 108.

It goes without saying that regarding the corrections in the *Tanya* (Brooklyn edition), there is room to *pilpel* (debate), raise questions, etc.

Regarding your comment there on the note to page 55a, line [regarding] the intent, which you felt required further study: what is added by the word "etc." (*ko'*)? You wish to interpret it as excluding a love that remains hidden in the heart, which does not elevate at all.

However, according to this interpretation, the "etc." does not fit with what was written previously, which discusses *dibur* (speech) that elevates, and not [cases] that do not elevate.

What appears to me is that with the word "etc.," [the author] hints at and adds the intent and the ascent to the world of *Atzilus* (53a).

With this, it is simply resolved: 1) How this ascent was omitted entirely. 2) Why the matter is hinted at with the word "etc." and not stated explicitly. And from the aforementioned, it is understood, for "we have no business with hidden things, etc."—as mentioned there, 53a.

With blessings for a kosher and happy *Chag HaMatzos*, and awaiting your response regarding the above, as well as regarding my previous letter which I am certain has already been received.

## 2544

B"H, 4 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you write, that you have long had the thought of leaving the yeshiva, and although you like it, it is connected for you with difficult battles, etc.—this is no wonder at all. As it is written in Koheles 9:14, "A small city"—the Gemara in Nedarim explains that this refers to the body—"and few men in it, and a great king came against it"—which is interpreted as the "old and foolish king," the Yetzer Hara—"and he waged bloody wars against the city."

If you study the Kuntres Eitz Chaim by the Rebbe (Rashab) n'e, and the third supplement printed at the end—specifically on page 87—you will see to what extent the Yetzer Hara opposes studying in a yeshiva where Chassidus is taught.

However, since the principle is *l'fum gamla shichna*—meaning that everyone is given an avodah according to **their** own strengths—if you will only utilize those strengths, which is relevant to your entire avodah, then it will be as the end of the verse (in Koheles) says: "And there was found in it a poor, wise man"—which, according to the Gemara, is the Yetzer Tov—"and he saved the city by his wisdom."

May Hashem help you so that this thought does not cause harm, neither to you nor to your friends. Nevertheless, a *tikkun teshuvah* is required for this (and also for the incident, even if it was exaggerated, as you write—you are, after all, the older one among them). I would like to suggest, both regarding yourself and regarding your friends, that the *tikkun teshuvah* for all of the above should be: to fast half-days of the Taanis Behab that occur after Pesach, and to redeem the other half of the day with tzedakah. 

Secondly, the time you are free from English studies should be utilized—if possible, all of you together—to study the first eleven chapters of Sefer Derech Chaim by the Mitteler Rebbe. Study them several times until you know their content by heart. Also, if possible, study Maseches Taanis together as a group. This will also resolve the question of what to do with the free time that remains from not studying secular subjects.

May Hashem grant you and your friends a kosher Pesach and the eating of matzah, which is the concept of *bitul*—the opposite of the *yeshus* (selfhood) present in *lechem chametz*—and may this effect an internal change for the entire year.

With blessings for all of the above.

See also above, letter 2551.

## 2505

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 2577

B"H, 5 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Enclosed is a check from one of the funds of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, a man of integrity, G-d-fearing, and turning away from evil. Consequently, this will fulfill the ruling of our Sages (Bava Basra 15b) that "he who takes a *prutah* from Iyov is blessed."

## 2578

2578

By the Grace of Hashem, 6 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It is surprising that for a very long time I have not received any news from you, even though I do receive regards through others and your relatives.

I am writing now regarding the current season, the days of the festival of Pesach that are approaching. Their essence lies in the eating of matzah on the first night, and one of their foundations is the concept of "you shall tell your son." As understood from the text of the Haggadah and from the halachic ruling for practical application, the Torah speaks even to the wise son and the grown son. From the different responses provided in the aforementioned text, which are based on the variations in the verses, it is understood and simple that the response must be tailored to the essence of the son.

Since Hashem has blessed you with an only son whose heart is sensitive to matters of ahavas Yisrael—even to the point of acting without calculation, and not necessarily through avodah based on intellectual reasoning—as he has demonstrated in practice through his participation in the defense and rescue of Jews and those coming to Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established speedily by Moshiach Tzidkeinu), this certainly comes from the parents to the children and from the vitality of Chassidim who are children of Chassidim. This is complete proof that with assistance and an appropriate approach, he could have been an oved Hashem, utilizing all his aforementioned strengths not only in the realm of ahavas Yisrael, but also in the realms of ahavas HaTorah and ahavas Hashem, which, according to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, are one.

If, for whatever reason, he is not inclined toward the world of commerce, you must strive with all your might and strength to prepare a path for him to find his livelihood in another field—whether in clerical work, agriculture, or in a factory or farm, etc.—provided that he finds himself in an environment where he will not be forced to constantly face trials regarding every matter of Torah (which is light) and the candle of a mitzvah. After all, "great is the bond of friends," etc.

Since you have been in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) for many years, it is most surprising that you have not invested the necessary energy in searching for such an opportunity, so that after he works in it, he himself would later be able to introduce his son into it. At the beginning of one’s entry into a field, everyone needs help from a relative or friend, and all the more so does a son need it from his parents. In this way, your son would naturally succeed in both material and spiritual matters, which is also the success of the parents.

It is understood that in all of the above, I do not intend to offer rebuke, and I also remember the principle that "one does not cry over the past." However, my intention is regarding the present and the near future, that at the very least, from now on, you should focus your attention on your aforementioned son specifically and constantly. We are promised by the words of our Sages, "If you have labored and found, believe it."

It is surely unnecessary to add that the conduct of an only son also influences the conduct of an only daughter, and when you secure the first, it is also a good beginning—and perhaps more than a beginning—to secure the second matter as well.

It is known that the concept of the festival of Pesach is the matter of the trust of the Children of Israel in the Ribono shel Olam, as it is written: "I remember for you the kindness of your youth, your following Me in the wilderness," etc. Just as in those days, so too in this time, when the Jewish people showed their trust to the greatest degree, they saw with their own physical eyes the manna and the well of Miriam, and "your garment did not wear out upon you." Every year at this time, these matters are awakened, and the strength of the attribute of bitachon draws down general and personal salvation in all that is needed, both materially and spiritually. According to what is explained in Likutei Torah by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in Parshas Beracha (93b), this is drawn down into one’s home and environment throughout the days of the year.

Now, there (in the aforementioned Likutei Torah), the discussion concerns the level of bitul that exists on all the festivals, and consequently, one only needs to draw it down until the next festival. This is not the case with matters unique to each specific festival, which are drawn down for the entire year. This is especially true regarding the festival of Pesach, as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in a sicha on the festival of Pesach 5703: "The illumination of all the festivals shines every day, and the illumination of the festival of Pesach is drawn down constantly."

One can explain these things briefly: In general, Shavuos is the matter of Torah, the time of the giving of our Torah. Sukkos is, in general, the matter of mitzvos, and its totality is the mitzvah of tzedakah, which are "garments" (see Tanya, Chapter 5), as it is written: "I have placed My words in your mouth, and with the shadow of My hand I have covered you." Pesach, the time of our freedom, is the matter of emunah, and as the Zohar states, "Matzah is the food of faith." Now, matters of Torah and mitzvos are dependent on time and place.

This is not the case with emunah, which is a constant mitzvah and the foundation of all Torah and mitzvos. And the rest is understood.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 2579

B"H, 6 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, Moreinu HaRav Chaim Yehuda, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Nissan, in which you write about your involvement in the field of kosher education, pure and holy, and that in addition to your work as a teacher at the Eitz Chaim Talmud Torah, you have also prepared supplementary booklets for the study of Sefer Vayikra, based on the experiences you have had in your holy work. May Hashem grant you the merit and success to bring the hearts of the children of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven, in the spirit of the Israel of old—the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos, founded upon the love of Hashem and the fear of Hashem. Great is this merit to draw down the blessings of Hashem for you and your household, may they live, with all that they require.

The days preceding the Festival of Matzos, and the days of the Festival of Matzos itself, are auspicious for the aforementioned. Its beginning is with the matter of "And you shall tell your son"—all four sons regarding whom the Torah speaks—who are ultimately gathered into the Seder, which begins with "This is the bread of affliction" and concludes with "Next year in Jerusalem" (a complete *yirah*, as explained in many places), may it be rebuilt speedily in our days through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, in the true and complete Redemption.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 2580

B.H., 6 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter—which was undated—in which you write that you are nervous again. It surprises me greatly that after the many times we have had the opportunity to speak about this, and after you have seen even with your physical eyes that Hashem Yisbarach leads and guides you, in the end, toward the good, you do not possess sufficient strength in your emunah and bitachon. You are nervous again, overthinking, and forgetting that Hashem Yisbarach is the Baal HaBayis of the entire world, acting as if it depends on someone else.

Especially during these days between Purim and Pesach, which are days of miracles *bayamim haheim* and likewise *bazman hazeh*, the wonder is even greater that you are overthinking.

May Hashem Yisbarach help you and your husband, the Rav, that from today onward you should both be strong in emunah and bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach, who is the King of kings of kings, that He is the essence of good and will lead your lives so that it will be in a way that is good, both visibly and revealed. And as Rabbeinu HaZaken writes in Tanya, when one believes in this truly, even that which is "hidden good" becomes "visible and revealed good."

And in these days of preparation for Pesach, which are the concept of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*—and as Chassidus explains, to go out from all limitations—may this hasten all that has been mentioned above.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 2583

B"H, 8 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Regarding the fasts on Thursdays: I have already written to you at length that this is not the path we heard from our holy Nasi. Furthermore, regarding the reciting of Tehillim every night—aside from the fact that according to our custom, one does not recite Tehillim before midnight—even after midnight, while it may be a matter to stay awake and go to sleep later on occasion, making it a fixed routine interferes with one's health. Consequently, it hinders the avodah of Hashem as one would wish, as well as the study of Toras HaChassidus.

Therefore, you should establish a routine, after a calm deliberation with the esteemed Chossid, Rabbi N. Nemannov (may he live and be well), both regarding your shiurim in the study of Toras HaNigleh and Chassidus, but without any fasts or staying up at night. May Hashem lead you on the good path in this as well.

I ask for your forgiveness...

## 2580

B”H, 13 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Regarding what you wrote about your son’s haircut, whose birthday falls on the seventh day of Pesach: although according to what is written in the *Acharonim*, one can find grounds for leniency to perform a haircut during the days of Sefirah, and certainly during Chol Hamoed (see *Shaarei Teshuvah*, Siman 531), nevertheless, since I have not seen this practiced—and especially given the well-known custom of Israel to perform the haircut on Lag B’Omer—in my opinion, you should do this on that day, and if possible, in Meron. May he and his wife live to raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds.

Regarding what you wrote about communal activism... I agree with what you write, that it is painful to see the lack of proper activity in general. The pain is even greater when one evaluates this lack in light of the immense possibilities that have appeared recently, where one sees that even a small action yields extraordinary success, yet due to trivial matters, the opportunity is not utilized. I do not wish to elaborate at all on the opposite of the reward associated with this, nor on the concept that the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself—*tzavta* (connection) and bonding. When from Above they "pour down" [the influence], and below they do not take what is given to them—even when it is being "fed" to them—without any rational cause, all those reasons and justifications you write in your letter should not have been written to me, but rather to yourself, and subsequently to your colleagues... As is well known, the Mishnah rules: "Know what is above you"—meaning that the matter depends on you and within you, in all matters above, and certainly in all matters below. Elaborating on this is superfluous.

In these auspicious days, the days of the month of Nissan, the month of redemption from the *mitzrayim* (limitations) and boundaries, may it be the will of Hashem that each person... also goes out to freedom from their *mitzrayim* and boundaries—at the very least from those whose root is on the side of *le'umat zeh* (the opposing side), so that eventually they will also emerge from the *mitzrayim* and boundaries of *kedushah*.

As you requested, I will mention your daughter and your wife, *tichyena*, when I am at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, zya".*

May the Almighty fulfill your wife’s pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child, in its time and season, properly and with ease.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach holiday.

## 2587

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the 27th of Adar Sheni, I was startled by your question regarding the public shiur you are conducting in Ein Kerem, near Jerusalem—may it be rebuilt and established speedily. You ask whether you should continue, given that although the attendees are very satisfied, the matter takes up nearly half a day, twice a week. My astonishment is this: After it has been explained in many places in the words of our Sages, and especially in the teachings of Chassidus, and primarily in the saying of the Baal Shem Tov that a soul descends to this world for seventy or eighty years just to do a favor for one fellow Jew, once, in material or spiritual terms—you are still in doubt as to whether it is worth the effort of half a day, twice a week, to merit bringing several Jews—dozens of Jews—closer to Torah, mitzvos, and yiras shamayim? You should certainly continue this in the future as well; on the contrary, as our Sages have ruled, we increase in matters of holiness.

Surely, in your shiurim, you emphasize the halachos and matters that pertain to daily life, for the deed is the essential thing. However, for the deed to be as it should, it must be preceded by study. There should be a special emphasis on yiras shamayim and ahavas Yisrael, as explained in the teachings of Chassidus, which are brought into practice through its guidance and conduct. You will surely strive in the aforementioned as is proper, and the merit of your involvement in this is great, to draw down proper health for yourself, for your wife, and for all your household, may they live.

As you requested, I will mention all those you wrote about when I am at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 2588

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished, R' Avraham, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 26 Adar II, and I hasten to reply, for I was alarmed to read therein that people are saying in my name that I rule—as a practical halachic matter—that if a prayer lacks a specific, particular kavanah, it is a nullified prayer, and furthermore, that they add that this applies to Birchas Hamazon as well! In general, I am astonished: what business is it of others to issue rulings in my name, when they could simply ask me directly regarding the practical application? It is already a known ruling of our Sages (Bava Basra 130b) that one may not derive a halachic ruling until one is told that it is for practical application.

It is true that I said to certain individuals regarding the "greatness of the kavanah of prayer," even among many who are not Chassidim, as is explained in the Chiddushei HaGriz on the Rambam, Hilchos Tefillah, where he interprets the words of the Rambam to mean that a lack of kavanah—standing before Hashem—is as if one skipped those words. However, aside from the fact that I doubt whether the Griz himself ruled this as a practical matter—for his aforementioned book is a commentary and not a collection of halachic rulings—since this law is not brought in the Shulchan Aruch or the Acharonim, nor in the Shulchan Aruch of our Rebbe HaZaken, it is certainly not to be practiced as a ruling. One should also note the Tanya, beginning of Chapter 38.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the text of the blessing of Shehecheyanu brought in the Kehot-published Haggadah, to say "lazman" (for the time), this is the instruction of our Nasi, and I believe its source is from our Rebbe HaZaken, author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

## 2590

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the 27th of Adar II. You write that although you received my response instructing you to remain in the yeshivah, you nevertheless left, even though you were among the outstanding *avreichim*. You now realize that your departure was due to a *ruach shtus*.

You also write that you are going without a beard and with short *pe'os*, and you are requesting advice and a blessing.

Based on the above, it is difficult to understand what your request is, since you acted entirely on your own initiative. It is well known that regarding such matters, our Sages have ruled: "If one says, 'I have not labored and yet I have found,' do not believe him." The matter is in your own hands; if you truly desire what you write—to be a Chabad Chossid—there is nothing that can stand before the will. The path to this is the study of Torah with *mesiras nefesh*, without excessive calculations, and seeking *tachlis* at every step—specifically a *tachlis* that even the *yetzer hara* would agree to—along with the performance of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*. First and foremost, you must fulfill what is written at the very beginning of the *Tur* and *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim*: not to be embarrassed by those who mock, as this provides the possibility for the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos*. It is already known that first and foremost, there must be the matter of *kabbalas ol* and *mesiras nefesh* in potential (see *Tanya*, end of Chapter 25, and Chapter 41, citing the *Zohar*, *Parshas Behar*). You are already assured by the aforementioned statement of our Sages that if you have only labored, then you will find.

I was pleased to hear that you are studying Chassidus a few times a week. Surely you are striving to translate this into action in the thought, speech, and deed of your daily life. May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant you success.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## B'591

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, who occupies himself with communal needs, a man of noble character, a scion of noble ancestors, etc., R' Sh.Z. Shlita,

Shalom u'Bracha!

Approaching the festival of Matzos that is upon us and upon all of Israel for good, I hereby wish to extend my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday.

Regarding the theme of the day:

One of the lessons of *Zeman Cheiruseinu* (the time of our freedom) is that the Jewish people began their existence as a nation under entirely unsuitable conditions. They required faith of the highest degree, and within a short time, they saw tangibly that the hope by which they lived through their faith was realized. Great is this faith, which we celebrate on the festival of Matzos; it moved an entire nation—elders, women, and children alike—to the point of leaving a country that was the provider of grain for the entire world, a country with industry and a highly developed order of life according to the standards of that era, and to go out, in the words of the verse, into the "great and terrible wilderness, with its fiery serpents and scorpions."

And in the words of our prophet: "I remember for you the kindness of your youth, your following Me in the wilderness, in a land not sown."

And in every generation and every day, a person is obligated to see himself as if he is going out of Mitzrayim. Through his strong faith in "I am Hashem your G-d, who brought you out of the land of Mitzrayim," he goes out to freedom from all the *meitzarim* (limitations) from within and from without.

As is our custom to send *Matzah Shmurah* to friends and relatives, I am enclosing with this letter three *Matzos Shmuros*.

Since, as a resident of Eretz Yisrael, the obligation of the second day of Yom Tov of the Diaspora does not apply to him,

And in the language of the Zohar: "Food of healing, food of faith."

With respect and holiday blessings.

## 2592

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished, G-d-fearing, man of character, who understands the nature of goodness, etc.,
Mr. Yisroel, may he live, known as Dr. Efrat,

Peace and blessing!

It was a pleasure to make your acquaintance on the occasion of the Purim farbrengen. As is the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: when two Jews meet, there should—and will—emerge a benefit for a third party as well, in addition to the benefit for the two of them.

I was told that you lecture in the fields of literature and philosophy, specifically on the system of the Rashbag in *Mekor Chaim*. Surely you are aware that there are several points in common between the teachings of Chassidus Chabad and the system of the Rashbag, and there is no doubt that anyone with a proper understanding of Chassidus Chabad will be better able to grasp the depth of the Rashbag’s intent in *Mekor Chaim*. Needless to say, one should not conclude from the above that this diminishes the originality of Chassidus in general, and Chassidus Chabad in particular, for there are many points in common throughout all parts of our holy Torah. And although several attempts have been made to interpret the Rashbag’s system as an "international" philosophy that is not specifically bound to the Torah of Yisrael, this is not the case; his system is not only founded upon the Torah of Yisrael and the ancient Kabbalah, but these are the very elements that constitute an integral part of his system.

As we approach the festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday, and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and from spiritual worries—from everything that hinders the avodah of Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

In his days and in our days, may the hoped-for promise be fulfilled: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders," with the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and holiday blessings.

## 2593

13 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs, Rabbi Yaakov Yosef, Shochet u’Bodek,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the day of the Hillula, 2 Nissan. Regarding your daughter... I have heard that in London itself, or in Gateshead, there is a school for girls that is G-d-fearing as it should be. You can certainly verify this on the spot, and if that is the case, it is worthwhile for her to enroll there. Surely, over time, in addition to the knowledge and development she will gain, she will also be able to influence her surroundings there.

Regarding your material livelihood, surely the Ribono shel Olam will help. Generally speaking, our Sages have said that one should not be affected by temporary straits and pressures. This is all the more so for those of our country from before, who witnessed open miracles and also saw that money is a lie and material possessions are vanity, etc.—that one should not be affected by this at all. Even though it is understood that such straits and pressures cause confusion and interfere with many matters, and primarily with the avodah of the Ribono shel Olam, one must pray specifically for this. For when "from the straits I called out to G-d," then "He answered me with the expanse of G-d." First, an expanse in spirituality, where the confusing material straits are diminished, and subsequently, an expanse is created in material matters as well. The days of Pesach are auspicious for this, as it is called the Festival of the Exodus from Mitzrayim—an exodus from the Mitzrayim and boundaries of the *sitra achra*, and even from the Mitzrayim and boundaries of *kedushah*, as is explained in Chassidus in many places.

Regarding what you wrote about your involvement in the field of kosher education—"that one walks around all day and comes home with almost nothing"—it is astonishing to what extent the sayings of our Nasi are known, and even those who contemplate them ultimately think, "This refers to someone else, not to me." Surely you know the saying of the Baal Shem Tov, cited many times, that a neshamah descends below into a body for seventy or eighty years, all for the sake of doing one favor for a Jew, one time, in spiritual or material matters. And if the *Shechinah* brings down a "part of G-d from above" literally, to "suffer"—as the saying of the Rashbatz goes—in a sack of flesh and bones for seventy or eighty years for the sake of one action or one favor, then all the more so should each of us be happy with our lot when the Ribono shel Olam grants us the merit and success to perform such actions many, many times a day and in a single week. This is also explained in my General Letter for 19 Kislev of this year.

Since others among Anash are also doubtful regarding the above, it would be good to publicize the content of these lines, and it will serve as a response to them as well.

As per your request, when I am at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention all those you wrote about regarding what each of them needs, and may the Ribono shel Olam grant you the merit to share good news regarding all of the above.

With the blessing of a kosher and happy Pesach,

**M. Schneerson**

## 2594

B"H, 13 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 3 Nissan, in which I see that you are being subjected to false and lying accusations. It is already known that the verdict in the Heavenly Court is that in every matter of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected and follow in the footsteps of our Rebbe HaZaken and the Nesi'im who followed him is on top.

This is as brought in the name of the Mitteler Rebbe, printed in the book *Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya*, end of page 122.

We have merited in this generation of ours, the generation of *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, that even though "impudence will increase"—and primarily, impudence without a crown, as brought in the discourses of the book *Shaarei Orah* at the end—nevertheless, on the other hand, we see the conduct of the Ribono shel Olam in a manner that is above nature, that all those who attempt to rise up against our holy Nasi, their end is bitter and in a state of *galus* and *rachmanus*.

If only they would perform a complete and true teshuvah very soon, for then there is nothing that can stand before teshuvah, even to the point of transforming [their status] from absolute judgment to kindness and mercy.

Regarding your comment that when an individual is at *Shema Koleinu* and the chazzan is saying *Kedushah*, one should recite a text of supplication within which he also integrates the *Kedushah*, based on the principle that a person may ask for his needs during *Shomei'a Tefillah*—based on this, there would be room to interrupt during *Shomei'a Tefillah* for all matters, as every matter could be integrated and phrased in a text of supplication so that the matter is included within it. Yet, no *posek* has ever been cited as bringing such a thing, such a great innovation. Therefore, the aforementioned instruction does not seem correct to me, and one might suggest the reason for its rejection: one should not be clever with a matter that is not a necessity...

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

...And there is no "after the fact," etc., since it is in a kesubah and not in a get. And in all the examples that you brought (and even regarding those there is a dispute), they also mention the manner by which he is actually called, and they write "that he is called," etc.

And there is no need to elaborate further.

## 2597

B"H, 18 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 5 Nissan with the good news that everything went through peacefully. I must reiterate what I wrote in my previous letter: when one sees how Hashem directs everything, one must strengthen one’s bitachon and emunah. In truth, this is not just a matter of emunah alone; even one’s intellect shows that everything will be good. May Hashem grant everyone success in creating great vessels to receive the good that Hashem wishes to bestow, both in ruchniyus and in gashmiyus.

This is especially true during these days of Pesach, which are days of emunah and bitachon, just as it was for the Yidden in those days—to go with their wives and children into a land of "serpents, scorpions, and drought," relying solely on the word of Hashem that they should go there. At that time, they saw that when it was needed, there was manna to eat, good water from the well of Miriam, and success in that "your garment did not wear out upon you," and so on. Likewise, in every generation and every day, a person is obligated to see himself as if he personally went out of Mitzrayim. When one proceeds with that emunah and bitachon—at least a portion of that same emunah and bitachon—one is certain that Hashem provides a person with what he needs, both in gashmiyus and in ruchniyus. May Hashem help you to see this, and to see it soon.

With the blessing of a kosher and joyous holiday.

Due to the sanctity of the festival, the Rebbe shlita has not signed, and I am signing on his behalf,

The Secretary:

## 2,598

B"H, 18 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Regarding what you write concerning melancholy and sadness: It is unnecessary to elaborate on a matter whose ruling has already been established by our holy Nesi’im, and as is explained in Tanya and elsewhere, that one must distance oneself entirely from sadness and melancholy. The way to achieve this is through *hesech hada’as* (diverting one’s mind). If that is not possible in any other way, then one must divert one’s mind from the sadness itself and think about Hashem—how He is the essence of good, and so on. When one truly desires this and makes an effort, one succeeds, in accordance with the ruling of our Sages: "You have labored and found."

With blessings for *mazal tov* and a kosher and joyous holiday.

Due to the sanctity of the festival, the Rebbe shlita has not signed personally, and I am signing on his behalf.

## 2,400

It is therefore understood that just as you strive to increase your material livelihood, you must all the more so strive to increase your spiritual livelihood—both because the spiritual is greater and more exalted than the material, and furthermore, because the increase in the material depends, first and foremost, on the increase in the spiritual. May Hashem grant you success.

## 2472

All of the above serve as vessels and channels to draw down what is needed for a person and their household, both materially and spiritually.

Great is the merit of this in fulfilling the desires of your heart and the heart of your wife, *shichyu*, that you may have the ability to support [these institutions] not only in the sense of "your children" — these students — but literally, as the Sages of blessed memory ruled: "A verse does not depart from its literal meaning."
