## 2707

B"H, 24 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about the incident where you changed certain matters in the yeshiva without consulting the *menahel po'el* as required... I am transcribing here a story I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukl"h, nbg"m, zy"a*, which is as follows:

It is known that in the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in general, and in the conduct of the *talmidim* in particular, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, was the *menahel po'el*. Once, it happened that one of the *talmidim* was given a severe penalty. Since it touched him deeply, this *talmid* made an extraordinary effort to meet my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), *n"e*, and wept before him with bitter tears. My father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), *n"e*, told the administration to cancel the penalty or, at the very least, to lighten it. When my father-in-law, the Rebbe, arrived and learned of this, he went to his father, the Rebbe, and told him that it is self-understood that he is not, *chas v'shalom*, questioning the substance of the matter. However, since he had been appointed *menahel po'el*, and consequently bears a certain measure of responsibility for the institution—and discipline is its essence and foundation—he could not bear responsibility for a leadership style where the decision of the *menahel po'el* is overturned, etc., and therefore he was resigning from his position. The end result was that his father, the Rebbe, changed the entire matter. I do not know the details of how, but the matter was conducted solely through the *menahel po'el* and the administration.

It is self-understood that I am not comparing the *menahel po'el* in the yeshiva of... to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, but it is also understood that I am not comparing your honor to the Rebbe (Rashab), *n"e*.

The moral of the above story, which my father-in-law, the Rebbe, publicized—and his intention in doing so was surely to teach us how to conduct ourselves in matters such as these—is that not only must we conduct ourselves from here on in accordance with the conclusion of the Rebbe (Rashab), *n"e*, mentioned above, but as much as possible, one must also rectify the past in this regard. There is no element here, *chas v'shalom*, of diminishing one's stature, and it is obvious that this is not a ruling regarding the substance of the matter itself, as in the story above. However, one of the foundations of accepting the fulfillment of Torah in general, and the possibility of the existence of Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva and its mission in particular, is the matter of discipline—both of the *talmidim* and of the administration, the *ramim* and the *roshei yeshiva*, *shichyu*.

My hope is strong that you will not take offense at this remark of mine and will fulfill it... And may Hashem merit each and every one of us to have the mind rule over the heart, which adds health in the physical sense and health in the spiritual sense.

With blessings, awaiting good news.

## 2008

B"H, 24 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding the work of the Reshet, I have already written about this many times. Nevertheless, due to the importance of the matter, I am repeating it once again: I am deeply astonished by the attitude of several teachers toward their work in the Reshet—and this includes a portion of the teachers from Anash, and he [the recipient] is included in this—who view it as a job where they are working for others. Consequently, they come to them with complaints, and if they feel these complaints are not being addressed fully, their immediate conclusion is that they must look for another job, for what difference does it make to them how they earn their livelihood and the livelihood of their families?

This entire approach is fundamentally flawed. The proprietor of the Reshet is the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, in whose name the institutions are named. It is understood that all those whom Hashem has enabled and granted the privilege to participate in this institution—this is the gate and the channel through which their sustenance, and that of their families, is drawn, both in spirituality and in physicality.

However, as with everything in the world, there is a division of roles. Those who have been privileged with the greater portion have as their primary task the actual education, whereas others are merely administrators, supporters of Torah, and so on.

It is understood that after this premise, it is truly astonishing that a person of intellect who has been privileged and succeeded in the aforementioned portion would come to an administrator and say: "Listen, I am doing you a favor by participating here, and therefore, if you fulfill all my demands, good; if not, I will leave the institution!" To elaborate further on this is unnecessary.

If this premise were held by the teachers from Anash, then even through natural means—and additionally through effort—it would permeate those teachers who, for the time being, are not from Anash. Consequently, their work would be in the manner explained in the *Hemshech* of 5666 regarding the work of a "faithful servant," where even when one works only with simple *kabbalas ol*, one is still meticulous not only in fulfilling the work but also in doing so with *hiddur*.

It is obvious that someone who possesses a great treasure would not go to others and say, "If you fulfill my wishes, I will use the treasure, and if not, I will cast the treasure aside and wander the markets and streets for a penny." As mentioned above, a word to the wise is sufficient.

You will surely explain this entire matter not only to yourself but also to the teachers you know or can come to know. May these few lines—few in quantity—be effective in their quality.

It goes without saying that I do not mean to say that all their complaints are unjustified, or that all members of the administration are one hundred percent correct in all their conduct. My intention is only that the "beautiful portion" in the Reshet is the portion of the teachers, and they receive much more in spirituality than the members of the administration. Since for a Jewish person the physical is governed by the spiritual—as it is written, "If you walk in My statutes... I will provide your rains in their time"—they also receive more in physicality than the members of the administration, whether immediately and openly, or over time and in a way that the recipient of the miracle does not even recognize the miracle. It is already known what is explained in the *maamarim* of the Rebbe Maharash, that in our generations, the matter of livelihood is miraculous and in the manner of the *man* in the desert. Therefore, Heaven forbid that they should sabotage themselves by leaving the institution of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory.

...Regarding the manner of educating the students of the Reshet concerning conduct according to *Shulchan Aruch* and conduct of *yiras shamayim*, here too it is impossible to set rigid rules, for the situation certainly differs from the students of one school to the students of another, depending on the environment in which they were raised and educated. However, in general, in a matter that does not involve *chillul Hashem*, it is understood that one should attempt the approach of "little by little I will drive them out." It is also understood that in this, it is worthwhile for the teachers to consult with one another, for "in the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

You will surely involve yourself in the Reshet with the appropriate energy, and Hashem will increase their borders with good students, who will be a source of pride for the entire Reshet, and the teachers will be able to say with justice: "See the seedlings we have grown."

With blessings for success.

## 2,512

B"H, 25 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your questions:

a) Regarding what is written in the Kuntres of 18 Elul 5703, page 76, that the Rambam explains the distinction between a *min*, an *epikores*, and a *kofer*—where this is explained in the Rambam:

It is surprising that you did not see the note at the bottom of that page, which refers to Rambam, Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 3; see the commentaries there. See also the Rambam’s Commentary on the Mishnah, Sanhedrin, Chapter 10, Mishnah 1; Chullin, Chapter 1, section 2; and Moreh Nevuchim, Part 3, Chapter 17.

b) Regarding what is written in the Sicha of Pesach 5703, end of section 38, that Ben Zoma was in solitude—the source for this:

See Chagigah 15a and Bereishis Rabbah, Chapter 2:4.

c) Regarding what is written in the Likkutei Dibburim there, section 52, that according to Kabbalah one should sleep between Mincha and Kabbalas Shabbos:

See the discussion of this in the sefer Toras Shalom, page 17, and the notes there. It is also well-known what is cited from the Maggid of Mezeritch, who would sleep on Erev Shabbos before Kabbalas Shabbos.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

P.S.
It is surprising that you do not mention anything regarding establishing regular study sessions in both the revealed Torah and the inner dimension of Torah—that is, the teachings of Chassidus.

## 2611

B"H, 25 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter some time ago, and due to the press of many matters, I did not reply until now. This is especially because my hope is strong that once my letter to your sister and her husband, *sheyichyu*, was received, things were settled, or at the very least, improved in a significant way. I look forward to hearing good news from you that this is indeed the case.

In our current time—following the period of destruction, *rachmana litzlan* and *lo aleinu*, and in this generation of *ikvesa d'Meshicha*—as per the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nivga"m, zya"e*: "He"—Melech HaMoshiach—"is standing behind our wall," waiting only for the completion of the *avodah* incumbent upon our generation. This *avodah* is, relatively speaking, easier than the *avodah* of the generations that preceded us. Therefore, it is incumbent upon every man and woman to fulfill what is stated in the verse: "Let the weak say, 'I am a hero.'"

With a firm resolution, one brings even their hidden strengths into revelation; consequently, one can accomplish many times more than if this were in a regular time and under regular conditions.

This is especially true when the subject is a *Tamim* and from the lineage of *anash*, and when his spouse—his *ezer*—is also the daughter of a *Chassid* and has received a *Chassidishe* education. In such a case, it is clear that the matter depends only upon their decision with the appropriate strength. And this is not merely a decision made in a moment of *hisorerus* or during a *farbrengen*, but a decision intended to be brought—and which they do bring—into actual practice in their daily lives. Then, it is not beyond reach that there be fulfilled in each of us a semblance of the saying of the Baal Shem Tov, who said that every Jew can cross the sea on a handkerchief if only they believe with simple faith. Further elaboration is unnecessary.

It is understood that you have permission to show this letter of mine to your husband, *sheyichyu*, and also to share it with others, for many of *anash*—both men and women—need to be reminded of all the above, even though it is a simple matter.

Surely the haircut of your son... *sheyichyu* was at its proper time. May Hashem grant you the merit to derive much *Chassidishe nachas* from him and from all your children, *sheyichyu*, with a sense of spiritual satisfaction that you are fulfilling your role in the *shlichus* of the *Ribono shel Olam* and the *shlichus* of our holy *Nesi'im* in your immediate and also distant surroundings.

With blessings, and awaiting good news.

## 2,712

2,712

B”H, 25 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It has been quite some time since I have heard from you, and I hope that you are continuing your work regarding the study of Chassidus in the schools, and, needless to say, that you are also studying Torah Nigleh and Toras HaChassidus yourself, with yiras shamayim.

I would be pleased to hear good news in this regard, and also that you are influencing your friends in this direction. May Hashem grant you success so that you may accomplish this in a manner that is above nature.

With blessings for success in the study of Torah Nigleh and Toras HaChassidus, and in the performance of mitzvos with hiddur.

#### ***2,712***

**The Torah should teach:** See also above, letter 2,257.

## 2,513

B.H., 25 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the first day of Chol Hamoed Pesach, containing a *pidyon nefesh* regarding the state of your health: as you requested, I will mention you at the *eis ratzon* at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for a complete and speedy recovery.

It is surely unnecessary to awaken you to the necessity of strengthening your *middah* of *emunah* and *bitachon* at all times, and especially during these days, as we have just emerged from the days of the festival of Matzos—*michla d'meheimenusa* (the food of faith) and *michla d'asvusa* (the food of healing)—and are moving toward the festival of the giving of our Torah, regarding which Chavakuk established them upon one principle: namely, *emunah*.

It is already a well-known foundation, publicized by the Baal Shem Tov, that every matter and event in the world occurs through *hashgacha pratis*. This is especially true regarding a Jewish person, and even more so for one who holds a position that provides influence over a specific circle, for *kal v'chomer* he is appointed from the "head of the spring" of Heaven. And since He, may He be blessed, is the essence of good, and it is the nature of the good to do good, there is no room at all for undesirable thoughts, etc.

It is understood that I do not come here to offer rebuke, *chas v'shalom*; I am merely studying a *sugya* in the foundations of *emunah*, for even in the study of the simple matters of Torah, it is also a matter of *talmud Torah*. I hope to hear good news from you soon, and that you are adding strength in *Torah* and *avodah*, especially in your particular field—namely, exerting influence in the spirit of *Yisrael Sava* upon your immediate surroundings and those further away as well. May Hashem grant you success.

Awaiting good news.

## 2,314

B”H, 25 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, R’ Mordechai Hakohen, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha,

Your letter was received, and you have surely received my letter with holiday greetings. Recently, a letter was also received from the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, R’ Yisroel Naeh, along with his article.

Now, by way of introduction: I am not entering into the content of the article—it is surely appropriate for the situation in your location, and especially since, as you write, it is making a good impression. I assume this means it has also achieved practical results, at least in terms of drawing the readers closer to matters of Yiddishkeit. However, I must say that this was not my intent. As I wrote explicitly, my intention is that they should publish in the Italian language matters of Chassidus and the atmosphere of Chassidus.

I have emphasized several times in my letters that my intention is for translations from the sichos, letters of the Rebbeim, etc. Surely there are those who know the Italian language who will engage—and are already engaged—in spreading the spirit of Yiddishkeit in general. One must not forget the warning of the verse, "My own vineyard I have not kept" (Shir Hashirim 1:6). Even within the realm of holiness, there is "my own vineyard"—that is, the unique mission that no one else will handle—and there are shared vineyards that others will also handle.

The same applies in our case: everything that leads to the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos is most necessary, and it is obvious that Anash and the Temimim must engage in this with mesiras nefesh. However, it is essential that they also engage in the dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus. Regarding this, I have written several times to the avreich, R’ Y., may he live.

It is understood that I do not intend to offer mussar, but rather, regarding practical action for the future: one must provide the aforementioned individual with excerpts from the sichos or from the letters of our Nesi’im, as well as simple maamarim suitable for the nature of the Bnei Yisrael currently in Italy, and endeavor to have them translated and published, etc.

Surely you will not be offended by this letter, for it is the demand of the hour. I did not write the above to the avreich, R’ Y., may he live, because for several reasons I want the initiative to come from you, without him knowing that this was not my original intent, so that it does not, chas v’shalom, cause him any discouragement.

With blessings, and awaiting good news.

## 2515

B"H, 26 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, the G-d-fearing, esteemed, and distinguished, engaged in the needs of the community, R' Yisrael, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter... and thank you for the article you enclosed that was printed in Italian regarding the festival of Pesach. Certainly, from here on, you should endeavor to print, frequently and regularly, excerpts from the sichos of our Nesi'im and their holy letters, or even accessible maamarim of Chassidus, as the needs of the hour demand. Fortunate is the one who merits to take part in disseminating the revealed and inner dimensions of Torah to the masses, in the most diverse circles.

It is surprising that you do not mention in your letter your influence upon your peers at the university, among whom there are surely Jews as well. Furthermore, you do not write about your regular shiurim in the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus. Surely this is merely an omission in your writing, and not, G-d forbid, in your actual practice.

May Hashem grant you success in arranging a suitable shidduch for you soon, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

Awaiting good news.

## 2,516

B"H, 26 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Since we are currently between Pesach and Shavuos, when every day has its mitzvah of counting Sefirah—which, according to the explanation of our Sages of blessed memory, originated from the fact that the Jews counted the days with longing, [counting] how many had passed since they left Mitzrayim, knowing that upon reaching the fiftieth day they would receive the Torah, and they could hardly wait—

And this [longing] also provided them with **all** their material needs—food, drink, and clothing—as it is told in the Torah that they had the Manna, the Well of Miriam, "your clothing did not wear out upon you," etc.,

So too, in every place and at every time, through longing for Torah and doing everything as the Torah dictates, Hashem is certain to fulfill His promise, "I will provide your rains in their time," etc., provided that a Jew, for his part, fulfills "and you shall keep My commandments." May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings.

## 2,517

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your reply, and especially your emphasis that you do not wish to say that things are not good, Heaven forbid. It is well known what our Sages said: if one thinks good, it will be good—which is also a promise. May Hashem help that this should be in a way that is visibly and revealedly good, and very soon.

I was also pleased to learn that you participated in the farbrengen of Acharon Shel Pesach, the Seudas Moshiach. It is a well-known ruling of our Sages that joy breaks through barriers, especially joy that is called by the name of Moshiach, for regarding Moshiach it is said, "The breaker is come up before them" (Agadas Bereishis, end of Chapter 63; see also Bereishis Rabbah, end of Chapter 85; Ohr HaTorah by the Tzemach Tzedek, Shemos, end of page 51).

On this occasion, I would like to ask you to convey my regards to your brother, may he live and be well, and I conclude my letter with my blessing to you and all yours for a healthy and happy summer.

With blessings.

## 2,818

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your letter, along with the *pidyon nefesh* for your son, may he live. I trust that by the time you receive this letter, his health has already improved, and I would appreciate it if you would inform me of this.

May the *Ribono shel Olam* grant him the merit to spread the light of Torah and the "light within the Torah" in his surroundings. The attribute of the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* is *midah k’neged midah*—to add light in a manifest way—

—as is known, that all influences from above are called by the name "light," as is explained in many places in *Chassidus*, and the foundation of this is in the *maamar* of our *Alter Rebbe* explaining the teaching of our Sages regarding *Ohr Ein Sof*—higher and higher without end, and lower and lower without limit—which is recited on the last day of *Pesach* at the *Seudas Moshiach*—

—in whatever he requires, for himself and for his entire household, may they live, both in material and in spiritual matters.

With blessings,

P.S.
Your letter has just been received. Thank you for the good news regarding the improvement in your son’s health, may he live.

## 2,619

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and scholarly R' Yisrael, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your regards through the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and scholarly individual, who is involved in communal needs with energy and good character, R' Nissan, may he live, known as Dr. Mendel. As he requested, I mentioned him at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for long days and good years. The explanation of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding this—"good years," with all its interpretations—is already well-known.

And surely he will bring good news that these days and years are indeed good for him, both materially and spiritually.

Regarding what you raised concerning the mitzvah of tzitzis—whether one fulfills the mitzvah every moment that one is wearing the tzitzis, or only at the initial moment, similar to the taking of the lulav:

This is understood from what is written, "And you shall see it and remember." Just as the remembrance is a mitzvah at all times, so too is the cause of it, which is the act of seeing. This is explicitly stated by the early authorities in *Sefer HaYirah* by Rabbeinu Yonah, near the beginning, where he writes: "The essence of the mitzvah of tzitzis is to wear them constantly" (this is the reading of the Gra in his commentary to *Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim*, beginning of section 24, and this is also the opinion of the Gra; see there).

In *Piskei Dinim* by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Orach Chayim*, section 2, subsection 7, it is implied that his opinion is that every moment is a mitzvah *d'oraisa* (and not merely a *hiddur* of the Sages). See also the commentary of the Ibn Ezra on *Bamidbar* 15:39, where it is also proven to be so.

With blessings for long days and good years.

## 2620

2620

B”H, 27 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

To the avreich, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R’ Chaim, may he live:

Shalom u’vracha!

In response to your letter informing me about the Boy Scout meetings taking place within the walls of the yeshiva, and that consequently the yeshiva teachers can exert a significant influence upon them, daven with them, etc., and you ask my opinion on whether to continue this.

In general, this is a correct approach, provided—and this is certain—that nothing inappropriate takes place during their meetings within the yeshiva walls, and it goes without saying that nothing contrary to the Shulchan Aruch occurs.

You do not write in your letter whether there is an issue of boys and girls mixing. Surely, it is easy to separate them from the outset for the time they are within the yeshiva walls, and afterwards, this will certainly continue as a matter of course when they are outside. It is self-understood that in an appropriate manner, you should teach them the concepts of practical mitzvos and instill the idea into the Jewish children that it is impossible otherwise. May Hashem grant you success in all the above.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and that this may bring added blessing and success in your personal matters as well.

#### ***2620***

**R’ Chaim, may he live:** Ziment. Additional letters to him—above 2260, and in the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 2121

B"H, 27 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Binyamin, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter—which lacks a date—I was pleased to read that you are meeting with the esteemed and distinguished R' Shneur Zalman Hecht, may he live, and that you also have shiurim in which you study Sifrei Chassidus. I hope that you also participate in the Chassidishe farbrengens that take place from time to time in Chicago.

Regarding what you write about a daily schedule, it is difficult to set one from afar. However, as an addition to the three daily shiurim—the *shiurim shavim l'chol nefesh* instituted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, about which you have surely heard from R' Hecht, you should also have fixed shiurim in the study of the Hilchos Shechita, and study them through each year. It is also a proper thing to be one of the participants in the *chalukas haShas* and to study through the masechta over the course of the year.

As for how to divide your day, that depends on the free time you have on your work days and on the days when you are free from work...

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 2722

B.H., 29 Nissan, 5714
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 23rd of Nissan, along with the enclosure. When I visit the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you and all your family regarding what each of you requires.

It is correct, as you write at the end of your letter, that "my help comes from Hashem." As the Midrash states, Yaakov Avinu recited the psalm "Shir LaMa'alos" when he went to Charan and posed the question to himself: "From where will my help come?"—and he answered himself that "my help comes from Hashem." It was because of this that it was later fulfilled in him that "the man increased exceedingly."

May Hashem grant you success so that you will soon be able to report good news, that you see Hashgacha Pratis in your success in material matters, as well as success in spiritual matters—and, as I told you when you were here, success in communal work as well.

Awaiting good news.
